1001 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jefferson


No. 1-89-0308


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


227 Ill. App. 3d 491; 592 N.E.2d 134; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 373; 169 Ill. Dec. 647



March 18, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JAMES J. HEYDA, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. Defendant appealed his conviction, alleging that the trial judge gave improper instructions on accomplice liability, that the prosecutor made inappropriate remarks during his closing argument, and that the trial judge improperly questioned defendant and impermissibly commented on the evidence. The court determined that in weighing the probative force of the evidence relating to defendant's intent against the probative force of the accountability instruction, the error in the jury instruction was harmless. The court also held that the judge was not in error in his interrogation of the witness because the judge's question had already been covered by defense counsel and it appeared that the judge was attempting to clarify the material issue of defendant's intent. The court concluded that even if the prosecutor's remarks constituted error, it did not require reversal because it did not involve a material factor in defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

 

1002 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Haven


Nos. 1-90-0459, 1-90-0460, 1-90-0461, 1-90-0462, 1-90-0463, 1-90-0464


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


247 Ill. App. 3d 1040; 618 N.E.2d 260; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 350; 187 Ill. Dec. 669



March 13, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 24, 1992. Released for Publication September 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Sam L. Amiranti, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were arrested after delivering nude performances at an adult bookstore. Defendants were charged with obscenity, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20(a)(2) (1989), and public indecency, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-9(a)(1), 11-9(a)(2) (1989). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the public indecency charges, and the state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state argued on appeal that the trial court erred in determining that the application of the public indecency statute to defendants' conduct was unconstitutional because there had been no evidence, proof, or agreement concerning the nature or content of the conduct performed in the nude, or that defendants' conduct was "nude dancing" implicating first amendment rights of expression. The court affirmed the trial court's decision to dismiss the indecency charges on the basis that the facts, as agreed to by the parties, provided the trial court with sufficient information to conclude that the public indecency statute was inapplicable. The performance was the kind of performance that the legislature excluded from the coverage of the public indecency statute. The facts before the court plainly alleged a "commercial erotic display," and the public indecency statute was applicable to only those exposures which were shocking and disturbing to the immediate audience, and not those commercial erotic displays which were designed to sexually arouse or gratify the audience. The public indecency statute was simply inapplicable to defendants' conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the public indecency counts.

 

1003 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Banks


No. 1-88-0628


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


227 Ill. App. 3d 462; 592 N.E.2d 107; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 364; 169 Ill. Dec. 620



March 13, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE MATTHEW J. MORAN JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of one count of first degree murder and two counts of attempted murder. Defendant appealed the first degree murder conviction on the ground that the Illinois murder statute was unconstitutional, and that the first degree murder conviction should be reduced to second degree murder because she acted under a sudden and intense passion resulting from serious provocation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant instigated a large street fight that involved approximately 25 persons. After she was shot and hit during the fight, she shot and killed the person she began arguing with, and wounded two other persons. She contended that her injuries were sustained in "mutual combat" and were provocation serious enough to reduce an alleged act of first degree murder to one of second degree murder. In affirming the conviction, the court held that (1) the murder statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 et seq. was constitutional, and (2) defendant failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that the killing occurred under a sudden and intense passion that resulted from serious provocation by the victim. The court found that defendant did not undergo a sudden and intense passion that resulted from the victim's provocation. The victim did not provoke defendant because defendant testified that she was not angry with the victim, and that she did not even see the victim when she fired the gun. The court rejected the mutual combat argument by stating that defendant could not characterize the fight as "mutual combat" because she instigated it.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for first degree murder and two counts of attempted murder was affirmed.

 

1004 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mitchell


No. 2-90-0281


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


225 Ill. App. 3d 708; 588 N.E.2d 1247; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 334; 168 Ill. Dec. 3



March 11, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 6, 1992. Released for Publication April 6, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County. No. 89-CF-30A. Honorable Alan W. Cargerman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13(a)(3), and aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(b)(1). The trial judge granted defendant's motion for a new trial as to the criminal sexual assault but denied the motion as to the aggravated criminal sexual assault conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was denied a fair trial when the trial court improperly admitted into evidence a video-taped statement made by the complainant prior to trial. At trial, the prosecution had played for the jury a videotape of an interview wherein the child victim of the sexual assault detailed the facts surrounding the alleged sexual assault. On appeal, the court held that the use of videotaped statements as a corroborative complaint was not contemplated by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10. The court held that a plain reading of § 115-10 revealed that the statute did not expressly or affirmatively provide for the introduction of prior videotaped statements of a complainant. On the other hand, the court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10.1 specifically provided that certain videotaped statements could be admissible as prior inconsistent statements. The court held that the use of the child victim's videotaped testimony at trial operated to deny defendant's right of confrontation. Accordingly, the court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions, and remanded the case for a new trial. The court held that the use of the child victim's videotaped testimony at trial operated to deny defendant's right of confrontation.

 

1005 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Schuttler v. Ruark


No. 2-91-0419


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


225 Ill. App. 3d 678; 588 N.E.2d 478; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 308; 167 Ill. Dec. 837



March 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 7, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 90-CH-600. Honorable John W. Darrah, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adopted son appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County(Illinois), which dismissed his complaint against defendants, trustees and guardian ad litem, seeking a declaration of his right to receive income as the "lawful issue" of his adoptive father under trusts created by his father's grandfather.


OVERVIEW: The adopted son had filed a similar suit claiming to be entitled to his deceased father's share of the trust income as his father's "lawful issue." This claim had been rejected at trial and on appeal. The son filed the present case asserting that a 1989 amendment to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1652 expressly provided that adopted children were to be treated the same as natural children and that this statute created substantive rights that should apply to his case from the date the statute took effect. The trial court rejected the son's claim. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court considered the effect of the amendment and found that it raised a presumption that an adopted child was to be treated as a natural child but that this presumption could be rebutted by showing a contrary intent of the testator by clear and convincing evidence. The court found that a presumption was a procedural rule that dictated the effect of the absence of evidence and shifted the burden of production. As a rule of procedure or evidence, the court held that the 1989 amendment did not create or confer any substantive rights and did not prevent the application of res judicata and collateral estoppel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court dismissing the adopted son's claim that he was the "lawful issue" of his adoptive father.

Simpson v. Illinois Health Care Servs.


No. 2-91-0657


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


225 Ill. App. 3d 685; 588 N.E.2d 471; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 299; 167 Ill. Dec. 830


January 31, 1992, Submitted  
March 3, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 90-L-0514. Honorable Roland A. Herrmann, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which dismissed the patient's medical malpractice complaint against defendants, hospitals and doctors, with prejudice for failure to file an affidavit and health professional's report as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1989).


OVERVIEW: The patient filed a medical malpractice complaint against the hospitals and doctors. The patient alleged that the doctors failed to test adequately a breast lump to determine whether it was malignant and as a result failed to diagnose and treat the patient's breast cancer. The hospitals and doctors filed a motion to dismiss the complaint for failure to file an affidavit and health professional's report as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1989). The trial court dismissed the complaint with prejudice. The patient appealed, contending that the trial court abused its discretion in dismissing the complaint where the required physician's report was tendered only 48 days late and the record showed that diligent efforts were made to obtain the report within 90 days of filing the complaint. On appeal, the court reversed, remanded, and held that the trial court should have permitted the patient to file a doctor's report and abused its discretion in dismissing the complaint with prejudice for failure to do so in a more timely manner. The patient demonstrated good cause for her failure to file the report and affidavit within 90 days.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the patient's medical malpractice complaint against the hospital and doctors and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Collins v. Board of Trustees of Firemen's Annuity & Benefit Fund


No. 1-90-2082


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


226 Ill. App. 3d 316; 589 N.E.2d 799; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 292; 168 Ill. Dec. 399



February 28, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Appeal as a Matter of Right or Leave to Appeal Allowed June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Monica J. Reynolds, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff paramedics challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant pension fund trustee's motion to dismiss the paramedics' declaratory judgment action as to the constitutionality of § 6-210.1 of the Firemen's Pension Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 6-210.1 (1989).


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the motion to dismiss that the pension fund trustees filed in the paramedics' declaratory judgment action in which the paramedics alleged that § 6-210.1 of the Firemen's Pension Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 6-210.1 (1989), violated Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5. The court reversed that grant on appeal and remanded the case. The court concluded that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 6-201.1 (1989) was unconstitutional because it diminished the rights that vested under another pension plan by requiring the paramedics to either tender their previously unwanted contributions and up to nine years of compounded interest or lose service credits for the years in which they served as paramedics and contribute to the other pension fund.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a grant of the pension fund trustees' motion to dismiss the paramedics' declaratory judgment action, which challenged the constitutionality of a provision of the Fireman's Pension Code.

 

1008 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Quigley


NO. 4-91-0649


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


226 Ill. App. 3d 598; 589 N.E.2d 133; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 195; 168 Ill. Dec. 19



February 13, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 24, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 913433. Honorable Charles H. Frank, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence, to rescind suspension of his license, and to quash his arrest, which had led to a charge of violating Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501 (1989) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-502 (1989) for driving with a blood-alcohol level of over 0.10 and for unlawfully transporting alcohol in a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted defendant's motion to quash his arrest, which arrest had resulted in a charge of driving with a blood-alcohol level of over 0.10 and of unlawfully transporting alcohol in a motor vehicle in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501 (1989) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-502 (1989), as well as to suppress evidence and rescind the statutory summary suspension of his driver's license. The court reversed that grant on appeal and remanded the case. The court reasoned that the arresting officers' observation of defendant's confrontational and bizarre behavior as to his dispute with another motorist created a reasonable and articulable suspicion that justified an investigatory stop and that probable cause for defendant's warrantless arrest existed. The court also held that, because the stop was made pursuant to the police's caretaking or public safety function, the stop did not violate defendant's Fourth Amendment rights. The court further concluded that the stop was conducted reasonably and with a minimum of intrusion into defendant's privacy and mobility and that the grant of his motion was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a grant of defendant's motion to quash his arrest, to suppress evidence, and to rescind the statutory summary suspension of his driver's license and remanded the case.

 

1009 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Faulkner-King v. Department of Human Rights


NO. 4-91-0301


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


225 Ill. App. 3d 784; 587 N.E.2d 599; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 158; 167 Ill. Dec. 330



February 6, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 23, 1992. As Corrected March 24, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Administrative Review of Illinois Human Rights Commission. No. 1988SF0345



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee challenged the decision of respondent Illinois Human Rights Commission (Commission), which affirmed the decision of respondent Illinois Department of Human Rights (Department) that it lacked jurisdiction to hear her complaint. The employee's complaint alleged that respondent employer sexually discriminated against her in violation of Human Rights Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 1-101 et seq. (1989).


OVERVIEW: The Commission based its decision on the employee's filing of her complaint more than 180 days after the alleged civil rights violation occurred. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 7A-102(A)(1) (1989) of the Act required a complaint to be filed within 180 days after the date that a civil rights violation allegedly had been committed. The court held that: (1) the Department did not lack subject-matter jurisdiction to hear the complaint; (2) the complaint was not timely filed because the alleged civil rights violation occurred when the terminal contract was issued by the employer, and the employee filed her complaint more than 180 days after that date; (3) the 180-day filling period was jurisdictional and the failure to file within the prescribed time limit deprived the Department of jurisdiction, and to hold otherwise would create an anomaly because the charge-filing time period would be jurisdictional for some rights under the Act and not for others; and (4) the charge-filing limitations period was not unconstitutional and the Act provided the exclusive means of redress for civil rights violations. The period was reasonable, and the employee failed to provide authority for her position.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's order, which affirmed the Department's decision that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the employee's complaint of sexual discrimination against her employer.

Shaffer v. C S X Transp.


5-90-0218


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


224 Ill. App. 3d 769; 587 N.E.2d 1161; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 164; 167 Ill. Dec. 546



February 6, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 10, 1992. As Corrected March 3, 1992. Petition for leave to Appeal Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 89-L-100. Honorable Jerome Lopinot, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, railroad and driver's estate, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which denied defendants' motions to transfer venue on the grounds of forum non conveniens in plaintiff parents' lawsuit arising from the death of their daughter as a passenger in the driver's car when it was hit at a railroad crossing.


OVERVIEW: The parents filed a lawsuit in the home county of the driver's estate administrator in Illinois. The accident happened in another Illinois county in which both the parents and driver lived. The railroad was a Virginia corporation with its principal place of business in Florida. The trial court denied defendants' motions to transfer venue on grounds of forum non conveniens. Affirming, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in striking a balance of factors and did not give the administrator's residence more weight than entitled. Because the administrator lived in the forum county and the railroad did business there, the court found no reason to transfer on the ground of forum non conveniens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendants' motions to transfer venue.

Ebbing v. Prentice


NO. 3-91-0275


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


225 Ill. App. 3d 598; 587 N.E.2d 1115; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 151; 167 Ill. Dec. 500



January 31, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 11, 1992. Released for Publication March 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Knox County, Illinois. No. 90-L-45. Honorable Daniel J. Roberts, Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Knox County (Illinois), which dismissed her medical malpractice complaint against defendant doctors for failure to comply with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622. The patient's complaint against defendant hospital was previously dismissed and the hospital was not a party to the appeal.


OVERVIEW: One of the doctors filed a motion to dismiss the case for the patient's failure to allege separate causes of action, and both of the doctors filed motions to dismiss for the failure to attach a written physician's report to the complaint pursuant to § 2-622. The patient amended her pleadings to comply. The trial court, however, granted the doctors' motions and dismissed the patient's case. The patient appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court and held that the trial court abused its discretion. The court ruled the patient should have been afforded every reasonable opportunity to establish her case. The court held amendments to the pleadings were to be liberally allowed in order to comply with § 2-622. The court found the patient made a sufficient showing of good cause for her failure to file the § 2-622 documents in a timely manner. The court ruled the physician's report contained minor deficiencies, but it was sufficiently clear and detailed to meet the requirements of § 2-622, absent a showing by the doctors that they were prejudiced. The court found the patient's failure to file separate reports as to each doctor was a mere technical deficiency.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court which had dismissed the patient's medical malpractice case, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1012 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Village of Lake Bluff v. City of N. Chicago


Nos. 2-91-0293, 2-91-0319, cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


224 Ill. App. 3d 866; 586 N.E.2d 802; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 109; 166 Ill. Dec. 844


January 14, 1992, Submitted  
January 30, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 3, 1992. Petition for Appeal as a Matter of Right or Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 86-MR-92. Honorable William D. Block, Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, landowner and contract purchaser, sought review of an order entered in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which denied the landowner's motion for post-judgment relief under § 2-1401 of the Code of Civil Procedure, denied the contract purchaser's motion for declaratory judgment, and denied both petitioners leave to intervene in a quo warranto action filed by plaintiff village against defendant city.


OVERVIEW: The village and city entered into a consent decree in the village's quo warranto action against the city that incorporated an intergovernmental boundary agreement between the two municipalities pursuant to § 11-12-9 of the Municipal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-12-9 (1989). The trial court denied petitioners leave to intervene in the action. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court ruled that petitioners did not have a sufficient interest in the subject matter of the action and thus had no right to intervene under § 2-408(a) of the Code of Civil Procedure because, while property owners had a right to petition municipalities for the annexation of their land, the legislature did not give property owners the right to have that land annexed. The court further determined that petitioners were not unconstitutionally deprived of their property rights without due process because an owner of unincorporated property did not have a fundamental right to be annexed to a municipality and the city entered into a permissible bargain with the village not to annex property within the village's planning jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the landowner's motion for post-judgment relief, denied the contract purchaser's motion for declaratory judgment, and denying both petitioners leave to intervene in a quo warranto action filed by the village against the city.

People v. Carreon


No. 1-89-2390


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


225 Ill. App. 3d 133; 587 N.E.2d 532; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 95; 167 Ill. Dec. 263



January 27, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE VINCENT BENTIVENGA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which was entered on the jury's verdict in defendant's second trial that convicted him of two counts of murder and armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to natural life imprisonment for each murder, with the sentence for the armed robbery merged into the life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lost money to the victims while playing cards. Later that night, defendant shot and killed the victims while riding in a car with them. The car struck a parked vehicle, and defendant and his friend exited the car. Defendant then took money out of one victim's pockets. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of murder and armed robbery. The court held that the trial court erred in precluding questions regarding a venireperson's attitude toward defendant's U.S. Const. amend. V privilege. However, such error was harmless because the evidence of defendant's guilt was overwhelming. The friend testified that he sat in the back seat of the car with defendant as he shot the men, he saw defendant go through a victim's pockets, and defendant gave him bloody money. Another witness identified defendant in a line-up and at trial. A bullet was found at defendant's apartment that was consistent with the bullet fragments removed from the victims, and the blood stains on defendant's clothes matched one of the victims. The murders and robbery were closely related such that the property was taken from the "person" of the victim even though he was dead.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of two counts of murder and armed robbery.

 

1014 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Weber v. Crossfield Chems., Inc. (In re Collector's Application for Judgment for Taxes Paid Under Protest)


No. 3-91-0411 (Consolidated with Nos. 3-91-0412, 3-91-0413, 3-91-0414, 3-91-0415, 3-91-0416, and 3-91-0417)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


223 Ill. App. 3d 896; 585 N.E.2d 1101; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 42; 166 Ill. Dec. 79



January 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 25, 1992. Released for Publication February 25, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County. No. 89 TX 1070. Honorable William R. Penn Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which found in favor of appellee tax collector in an action by the taxpayers challenging the tax levy of certain taxing bodies under the authority of § 16 of the Local Government Debt Reform Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 17, para. 6916 (1989).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers objected to the levy by taxing districts for the payment of principal and interest on bonds issued by the districts. The taxpayers alleged that the county clerk illegally extended a tax on the bonds for a prior year under an allegedly unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority in § 16 of the Act. The taxpayers claimed that the Act improperly delegated to the county clerk legislative discretion in determining whether or not to accept the filing of the levy ordinance. The trial court found that the decision was an exercise of ministerial or administrative discretion and found that the Act was constitutional. The appellate court affirmed, holding that § 16 of the Act was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative discretion to the county clerk. The court concluded that the practical construction of § 16 was that anything filed before the completion of the prior year's tax books was included in that tax year. Because the tax books had not been completed when the bond resolutions and ordinances were presented for filing, the levies were filed on the prior tax year. The process did not involve any exercise of discretion by the county clerk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment in favor of the tax collector.

 

1015 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Felder


1-89-3502


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


224 Ill. App. 3d 744; 586 N.E.2d 729; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 23; 166 Ill. Dec. 771



January 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 28, 1992. As Corrected October 19, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable James J. Heyda, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, after a jury trial, entered convictions for murder, attempted murder, and home invasion under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 9-1(a)(1), 8-4(a), and 12-11(a)(2) and sentenced him to 80 years' imprisonment for murder, 30 years for attempted murder to run consecutively with the murder sentence, and 30 years for home invasion to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: After a party, defendant beat and threatened to kill a woman who he believed stole money and shot another woman to death. Defendant was convicted of murder, attempted murder, and home invasion under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 9-1(a)(1), 8-4(a), and 12-11(a)(2) and received consecutive sentences for the murder and attempted murder convictions. The court affirmed the convictions and the sentences. Because the evidence that defendant intended to kill the woman was overwhelming, any error in the court's instructions on murder was harmless. The trial court did not err in allowing testimony from the state's witnesses that they were reluctant to cooperate with the police out of fear for their safety because the testimony did not give rise to the inference that defendant in any manner threatened them but explained why those witnesses did not initially provide information to the police. The trial court did not err in finding that defendant failed to establish a prima facie case of discrimination during the selection of the jury. Consecutive sentences for the murder and attempted murder were mandated by the factors in mitigation and aggravation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for murder, attempted murder, and home invasion.

 

1016 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Chavin v. General Employment Enterprises, Inc.


Nos. 1-90-3430, 1-90-3483, and 1-90-3694 (Consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


222 Ill. App. 3d 398; 584 N.E.2d 147; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 16; 164 Ill. Dec. 935



January 13, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE ROBERT L. SKLODOWSKI, JUDGE PRESIDING.

Original Opinion of September 16, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1587.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a corporation and its directors, challenged orders from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted a preliminary injunction to plaintiff shareholders and permanently enjoined the corporation from implementing a share purchase rights plan.


OVERVIEW: Shareholders purchased approximately five percent of the corporation's common shares. The corporation and its directors received a statement informing them that the shareholders had acquired the shares and intended to increase their investment. The shareholders were also considering whether to seek control of the corporation. Thereafter, the directors unanimously adopted a "poison pill" plan, designated the share purchase rights plan. The shareholders filed a complaint against the corporation and its directors, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial court granted a preliminary injunction and later permanently enjoined the implementation of the plan, concluding that it was void, invalid, and unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that the trial court had jurisdiction to issue the preliminary injunction. However, the court also found that the plan did not conflict with the right to cumulative voting guaranteed by the state constitution. Therefore, the court held that the trial court abused its discretion when it issued the permanent injunction. The judgment was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order, which granted a preliminary and a permanent injunction to the shareholders, was reversed and remanded.

People v. C.S.


No. 2-89-0644


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


222 Ill. App. 3d 348; 583 N.E.2d 726; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2201; 164 Ill. Dec. 810



December 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 31, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 88-CM-1712. Honorable Richard W. Vidal, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which ordered defendant to undergo a blood test for human immunodeficiency virus (HIV), and ordered the disclosure of positive test results, after defendant plead guilty to the unauthorized possession of a hypodermic needle or syringe.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to the unauthorized possession of a hypodermic needle or syringe. Thereafter, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(h) (1989), the trial court ordered defendant to submit to HIV testing. Defendant's test results were positive and the state moved for disclosure of the results. The trial court ordered the test results disclosed to all attorneys in the criminal division, two persons in the county jail, and to the police supervisor. Defendant appealed and argued that para. 1005-5-3(h) was unconstitutional and that the disclosure order was an abuse of the trial court's discretion. The court held that the test mandate of para. 1005-5-3(h) was constitutional and was limited to persons convicted of criminality connected with high-risk behavior for the transmission of a deadly disease. The court vacated that portion of the trial court's order that directed disclosure of the test results to the attorneys as there was no justification for the disclosure. The court affirmed that part of the order requiring disclosure of the test results to county jail personnel and the police supervisor, as it was reasonable that such disclosure was in the public interest.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the portion of the trial court order that ordered disclosure of defendant's HIV-positive status to the state's attorney personnel, after defendant plead guilty to the unauthorized possession of a hypodermic needle or syringe. The court then affirmed the order as modified.

Rognant v. Palacios


1-90-3376


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Willard J. Lassers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff's personal injury action against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was employed by the city transit authority. Plaintiff was injured while riding a public city bus driven by defendant. Plaintiff filed an action against defendant two years later. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the one year statute of limitations in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 341 (1985) was not being retroactively applied to bar plaintiff's complaint and plaintiff's due process rights were not violated. The court found that the one-year statute of limitations in § 341applied whenever a city transit authority employee such as defendant was made a party to an action because the city transit authority employee could bring a subsequent contribution or indemnification action against the city transit authority. The court found that defendant did not waive the defense of the statute of limitations for failing to articulate it in his answer because defendant could obtain permission to file an amended answer asserting that defense prior to the final judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court which granted defendant's motion for summary judgment.

People v. Kluxdal


1-89-0421


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


225 Ill. App. 3d 217; 586 N.E.2d 701; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2248; 166 Ill. Dec. 743



December 31, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Janice Bierman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of murder, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a) (1985). The circuit court sentenced defendant to natural life in the custody of the Illinois Department of Corrections. Defendant sought review of his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder for shooting and killing his wife and his mother-in-law. Defendant presented an insanity defense at trial. The circuit court found defendant guilty as charged. Defendant appealed, raising numerous grounds of error. The court reversed defendant's conviction, holding that the circuit court erred by requiring defendant to prove insanity by clear and convincing evidence because the insanity statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 6-2(e) (1985), provided for a preponderance of the evidence standard. The court also held (1) the circuit court's determination of defendant's sanity was not improbable or contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence, (2) the circuit court did not improperly restrict defendant's cross-examination of the state's expert witness, (3) the state presented sufficient evidence to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant intended to kill his mother-in-law, (4) the circuit court's finding of guilty, rather than guilty but mentally ill, was not contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence, and (5) defendant's sentence was mandated by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1985), and was thus not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's murder convictions and remanded the matter for a new trial.

People v. Haynes


NO. 5-90-0083


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


223 Ill. App. 3d 126; 584 N.E.2d 1040; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2227; 165 Ill. Dec. 606



December 30, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. No. 89-CF-152. Honorable Thomas Sutton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of attempt of a criminal trespass to a residence pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8-4, 19-4 (1989).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of attempt of a criminal trespass to a residence in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8-4, 19-4 (1989). Defendant appealed his conviction and his sentence. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court concluded that defense counsel's failure to request a jury instruction on the defense of necessity did not deny defendant effective assistance of counsel. There was insufficient evidence at trial to entitle defendant to have the jury instructed on the necessity defense. The court found that the sentencing scheme that allowed attempt misdemeanors to be punished as severely as the offenses attempted while attempt felonies were not punished as severely as the offenses attempted was not unconstitutional. The court determined that the sentencing scheme was constitutional because there was a rational basis for the differing classifications established by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant.

 

1021 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bole


No. 2-89-1218


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


223 Ill. App. 3d 247; 585 N.E.2d 135; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2196; 165 Ill. Dec. 739



December 30, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 89-CF-221. Honorable Henry L. Cowlin, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to three counts of criminal sexual assault in violation of § 12-13 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13 (1989). The Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) entered a judgment of conviction and sentenced him to consecutive terms of imprisonment for each count pursuant to § 5-8-4(a) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(a) (1989). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was sentenced, he filed a motion to withdraw his guilty pleas, arguing that the trial court and his attorney failed to advise him that under § 5-8-4(a) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(a) (1989), that if prison terms were imposed, they were mandatorily consecutive. The motion was denied. On appeal, defendant argued that § 5-8-4(a) was unconstitutional, his guilty plea was unknowingly and involuntarily made, he received ineffective assistance of counsel, the offenses were not committed in a single course of conduct, and the sentences were excessive. The court affirmed the convictions, but vacated the sentences. Section 5-8-4(a) provided an exception to the general ban against consecutive sentencing for, inter alia, violations of § 12-13 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13 (1989), but only where they were committed as a single course of conduct. Defendant's separate offenses against the same victim at distinct points of time separated by several days did not constitute a single course of conduct. The court remanded for resentencing. All other grounds of appeal no longer needed to be addressed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of three counts of criminal sexual assault, vacated the sentences for consecutive jail terms, and remanded for resentencing.

People v. Smallwood


Nos. 1-89-2235, 1-89-2432 (Consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


224 Ill. App. 3d 393; 586 N.E.2d 636; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2210; 166 Ill. Dec. 678



December 30, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 28, 1992. As Corrected November 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE THEMIS KARNEZIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, defendants challenged their conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for first degree murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 and sentence of 35 years.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendants' conviction, finding that there was no obligation on the trial court to believe defendants' alibi testimony over positive identification of the accused. The court found that comments made by the prosecutor during closing argument were not grounds for reversal because the comments were directly related to witness testimony, and not related to a witness refusing to testify. Defendants were not deprived of the right to have the jury evaluate the identification evidence, finding that defendants were positively identified in open court. The court ruled that one defendant was not unfairly prejudiced by the rebuttal testimony by two witnesses, finding that the rebuttal testimony was proper when it reflected adversely upon the credibility of that testimony. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 9-1 and 9-2 did not violate due process by requiring defendant to prove a mitigating factor to reduce a first degree murder charge to second degree murder. One defendant was properly sentenced because the court found that the trial court had properly considered his voluntary manslaughter conviction as a juvenile.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' conviction for first degree murder and 35 year sentence.

People v. Smalley


No. 1-89-0950


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


249 Ill. App. 3d 964; 621 N.E.2d 7; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2150; 190 Ill. Dec. 138



December 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOHN N. HOURIHANE, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; vacated in part; remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for first degree murder and armed violence from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first degree murder and armed violence, and was sentenced to concurrent prison terms of 24 years for first degree murder, and 10 years for armed violence. On review, the court held that the Illinois murder statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 et seq. (1987), was constitutional. As to defendant's argument that he should have been found guilty of second degree murder, the court concluded that a rational trier of fact could find that defendant failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that a reasonable person would have reacted with intense passion and attack the victim with a knife, stabbing her four times, after arguing over the proceeds of a lottery prize and an insurance refund. The court, however, found that defendant's convictions for armed violence and murder were predicated on a single physical act, and vacated the armed violence conviction. Finally, the trial court did not err in failing to appoint new counsel after defendant alleged ineffective assistance of counsel. Even assuming that his counsel made an error in trial strategy, defendant failed to show that the outcome of the trial would have been different.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder, but vacated the conviction for armed violence. The court remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing on the murder conviction alone.

People v. Driskel


No. 1-88-2817


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


224 Ill. App. 3d 304; 586 N.E.2d 580; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2209; 166 Ill. Dec. 622



December 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph J. Urso, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgments of conviction on the jury's guilty verdicts for four counts of murder, attempted murder, aggravated battery, armed robbery, and residential burglary. Defendant was sentenced to natural life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, attempted murder, aggravated battery, armed robbery, and residential burglary, and sentenced to natural life imprisonment. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the compulsion defense did not apply to felony murder charges because: (1) the case was not one where defendant was compelled to commit the armed robbery and had nothing to do with the murders; (2) the legislature specifically excluded offenses punishable with death from the compulsion defense; and (3) defendant could have received the death penalty. The court ruled that 50 graphic photographs depicting the victim's injuries were properly admitted as relevant to whether one or two persons participated in the crimes because the pictures depicted the amount of force used. The court determined that once the death penalty was not imposed, the trial judge was mandated by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(c) to impose natural life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, attempted murder, aggravated battery, armed robbery, and residential burglary, and his sentence of natural life imprisonment.

Gordon v. Boden

People v. Laws


1-90-2677


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


224 Ill. App. 3d 167; 586 N.E.2d 453; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2135; 166 Ill. Dec. 495



December 24, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 23, 1992. Released for Publication February 28, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard E. Neville, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed conspiracy indictments for pimping, pandering, soliciting for a prostitute, and keeping a place of prostitution against defendants. The state appealed the dismissal.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court dismissed the conspiracy indictments against defendants on the ground that they were barred by Wharton's Rule, which provided that an agreement by two persons to commit a particular crime could not be prosecuted as a conspiracy when the crime was of such a nature as to necessarily require the participation of two persons for its commission. The court reversed and remanded with directions to reinstate the indictments. The rule had current vitality only as a judicial presumption, to be applied in the absence of legislative intent to the contrary. The conspiracy statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-2, specifically provided for enhanced sentencing for the conspiracy charges of pimping, soliciting, pandering, and keeping a place of prostitution, and the comments to the statute clearly stated that Wharton's Rule had been annulled. The rule was also inapplicable based upon the third-party exception because the conspiracies alleged against defendants involved a greater number of persons than was required for commission of the substantive offenses.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of indictments against defendants for pimping, pandering, soliciting for a prostitute, and keeping a place of prostitution was reversed and remanded with directions to reinstate the indictments.

People v. Morrison


No. 3-90-0635


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


223 Ill. App. 3d 176; 584 N.E.2d 509; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2156; 165 Ill. Dec. 330



December 24, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 90 CF 1668. Honorable Edward F. Masters, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of child abduction.


OVERVIEW: The father contended that the child abduction statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(3) (1989), violated the Due Process and Equal Protection clauses. The court reversed the circuit court's judgment, finding that the statute was constitutional, but that it was unconstitutionally applied to the father. The court determined that the state's failure to grant the same measure of recognition of legal parentage at birth to an unwed father as that accorded an unwed mother was based merely upon the biological reality that motherhood was obviously more apparent and more easily established. The court noted that once an unwed father complied with the statutory procedure of legally establishing his biological relationship with the child, he could not be convicted under the statute. The court concluded that the application of the statute would have deprived the father of equal protection of the law because the father was not a neglectful father who had abandoned his child. The court explained that prior to the child's removal by his mother from the shared residence, the father had resided with the child from his birth and provided financial and emotional support.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court. The court found that the statute was constitutional, but concluded that it was unconstitutionally applied to the father.

Dickerson v. Industrial Comm'n


NO. 5-90-0810WC


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT, INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION DIVISION


224 Ill. App. 3d 838; 587 N.E.2d 1045; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2114; 167 Ill. Dec. 430



December 20, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Alexander County. No. 90-MR-2; Hon. Stephen L. Spomer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Alexander County (Illinois), which affirmed the denial of his occupational disease claim by the Industrial Commission (commission). The commission denied the employee's claim that he had contracted silicosis as a result of his employment with respondent employer on the ground that it was time-barred under the Occupational Diseases Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the employer between 1959 and 1971. In May 1983, he filed an occupational disease claim, which alleged that he had contracted silicosis as a result of that employment. An arbitrator found in favor of the employee. The commission reversed that decision on the ground that the employee's claim was time-barred. The trial court affirmed the commission's decision. The employee appealed from the trial court's judgment, which was affirmed. Section 1(f) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 172.36(f) (1989), provided that a claim had to be brought within three years of the last exposure to silica dust. Section 6(c) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 172.41(c) (1983), stated that a claim was barred unless it was brought within three years of the date of the disablement. The court stated that the purpose of those two provisions was to protect employers against claims that were too old to be adequately investigated and defended. Therefore, para. 172.36(f) acted as a statute of repose and disablement within the applicable time frame was a condition precedent to recovery. The court held that para. 172.36(f) was not subject to the discovery rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which sustained the commission's decision to deny the employee's occupational disease claim.

Shutes v. Fowler


NO. 4-91-0383


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


223 Ill. App. 3d 342; 584 N.E.2d 920; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2093; 165 Ill. Dec. 486



December 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Vermilion County No. 91MR4. Honorable Thomas J. Fahey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant construction company sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which ordered the company to comply with appellee injured party's request for discovery under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 224, 134 Ill. 2d R. 224, even though the injured party had not initiated any lawsuit.


OVERVIEW: The construction company filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that Rule 224 did not confer jurisdiction on the circuit court because there was no case or controversy. The court found that Rule 224 was clear and unambiguous. The court found that a petition under Rule 224 became a justiciable matter when it had been determined that, under the court's rule-making authority, a litigant was able to file for discovery to learn the identity of potential parties prior to filing the lawsuit. The court held that Rule 224 was constitutional and the construction company as required to comply with the discovery order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that Rule 224 was constitutional and conferred subject matter jurisdiction on the circuit court. The construction company was required to comply with the discovery request.

People v. McCreadie


NO. 4-91-0155


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


223 Ill. App. 3d 316; 584 N.E.2d 839; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2068; 165 Ill. Dec. 405

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 90CF227. Honorable Rodney A. Scott, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of first degree murder pursuant to § 9-1(a)(1) of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1) (1989) and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 1005-8-1(a)(1) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to the murder. On appeal, defendant claimed that the natural-life sentencing statute was unconstitutionally vague and violated the eighth amendment prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The trial court properly found defendant eligible for the natural-life sentence because the murder was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Webb v. Lane


No. 5-90-0609


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


222 Ill. App. 3d 322; 583 N.E.2d 677; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2063; 164 Ill. Dec. 761



December 13, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County. No. 90-MR-52. Honorable Jerry D. Flynn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois), which dismissed his complaint against appellee prison officials, alleging a violation of the inmate's civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The inmate argued that he was denied due process of law when prison officials confiscated and forfeited United States currency recovered as a result of a search of the inmate's cell.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a complaint against the prison officials based on an alleged violation of his civil rights pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The inmate argued that he was denied due process of law when the prison officials confiscated and forfeited his United States currency without a due process hearing. Plaintiff alleged that as a result of a search of his cell he had been charged in a disciplinary report with possession of money, a violation of department of correction rules, and that the had appeared before the institutional adjustment committee to respond to the charges. At the hearing, the inmate admitted to having the money and the money was confiscated and forfeited. The court affirmed the trial court's granting of the prison officials' motion to dismiss because the inmate had no protectable interest in the property seized by the prison officials and its disposal did not work a deprivation of any constitutional right. The court concluded that the regulation prohibiting the unauthorized possession of United States currency was a legitimate regulation and that, as a result, the inmate has no protected property interest in the possession of the unauthorized currency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the prison officials' motion to dismiss the inmate's complaint because the department of correction rule prohibiting possession of currency by the inmate did not violate substantive due process because there was a legitimate penological interest in promulgating such a regulation. The court found that in light of such regulation, the inmate had no property interest in possession of the currency.

 

1033 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Forest Preserve Dist. v. Estes


No. 2-91-0222


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


222 Ill. App. 3d 167; 583 N.E.2d 640; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2033; 164 Ill. Dec. 724



December 6, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 16, 1992. Released for Publication January 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 89-ED-0003. Honorable James F. Quetsch, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county forest preserve district (district) appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) granting defendant property owners' motion to dismiss its eminent domain action on the ground that the district failed to establish its authority to condemn the land; district failed to obtain the town's approval as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 961/2, para. 6309 (1989) for lands used as a linear park or trail.


OVERVIEW: A district filed an eminent domain action seeking to acquire land for use as an access trail. The property owners' filed a cross-claim alleging that the land was part of a larger tract and requested damages for the remainder of the land. The property owners later filed a denial and motion to dismiss, claiming that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 961/2, para. 6309 required the district to obtain town approval to condemn land used as a linear park or trail. The property owners were allowed to withdraw the cross-claim and to amend their motion to allege that the district was acquiring the property as a trail or linear park. The trial court then granted the motion to dismiss on the ground that the district failed to obtain town approval. The district appealed, claiming that it met its burden to establish that para. 6309 did not apply to the land because a "linear park" could only be a man-made creation and a "trail" was not an access trail. The court affirmed the trial court judgment, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the property owners to withdraw their cross-claim and the ordinary meaning of "trail" must be applied, therefore town approval was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that granted the property owners' motion to dismiss the district's eminent domain action on the grounds that the district failed to establish its authority to condemn the land because it failed to obtain the town's approval as required by statute for lands used as a linear park or trail.

Aaron v. Hendrickson


No. 5-90-0244


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


221 Ill. App. 3d 842; 582 N.E.2d 759; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2074; 164 Ill. Dec. 196



December 6, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Johnson County. No. 88-L-5; Hon. James R. Williamson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lumber company sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Johnson County (Illinois) that awarded damages to plaintiff owners in an action alleging the wrongful cutting of plaintiffs' trees. Plaintiffs challenged that part of the judgment finding that plaintiffs failed to prove ownership within an area referred to as the "overlap."


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff owners brought an action against defendant lumber company to recover damages caused by defendant's wrongful cutting of plaintiffs' trees. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiffs against defendant but found that plaintiffs had failed to prove ownership within the area identified as the overlap. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court. The court held that the Wrongful Tree Cutting Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 961/2, para. 9401 et seq. (1987) was constitutional because it did not prescribe a rule of procedure that would infringe upon the judicial power in violation of the Illinois Constitution, art. II, § 1, but rather created a cause of action for an owner of wrongfully cut trees and proposed a way to ascertain damages that a court had the option of following. After reviewing the record as a whole, the court also found no violation of defendant's due process rights. Further, the court ruled that plaintiffs failed to prove ownership of the overlap area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The state wrongful tree cutting statute was not unconstitutional because it merely created a cause of action for an owner of wrongfully cut trees and proposed a way to ascertain damages that a court had the option of following. Moreover, the evidence showed that plaintiff owners failed to prove ownership of the overlap area.

People v. Gaither


No. 5-89-0783


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


221 Ill. App. 3d 629; 582 N.E.2d 735; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2049; 164 Ill. Dec. 172



December 4, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Richland County. No. 89-CF-43; Hon. Patrick McLaughlin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Circuit Court of Richland County (Illinois) of battery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 12 -- 3(a)(1) (1989). Defendant was sentenced to serve 364 days in the county jail. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction because there was no direct evidence of injury to the victim. The court rejected defendant's argument, holding that there need not be direct evidence of injury to sustain a conviction of battery based upon bodily harm. The court said that evidence of contact between defendant and the victim, combined with the jury's common knowledge, was sufficient to establish that defendant's conduct caused bodily harm. The court also rejected defendant contention that the trial court erred in admitting evidence concerning other incidents of abuse by defendant toward the victim. The court held that the evidence was relevant to show defendant's intent and absence of an innocent frame of mind. Finally, the court rejected defendant's contention that the sentence imposed violated the constitutional assurances of proportionate penalties and due process. The court held that the statutory scheme set in place by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 75, para. 32 -- 3 (1989) was reasonably designed to remedy the increase in violent crime, especially abuse directed toward children. Thus, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for battery and his sentence of 364 days in the county jail.

People v. Coleman


No. 1-88-3514


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


222 Ill. App. 3d 614; 584 N.E.2d 330; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1989; 165 Ill. Dec. 151



November 27, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE ROBERT J. COLLINS, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in which they were convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced to 20 years in prison. Defendant one was tried by a jury and defendant two was tried simultaneously by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and appealed their convictions. Defendant one alleged that he should receive a new trial because the state forced him to be tried by a jury, and defendant two alleged that the state did not that he was accountable for defendant one's actions. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that: 1) defendant one was denied his right to waive a jury trial, requiring a reversal of his conviction and a remand for a new trial; 2) because the record showed that defendant two aided defendant one in putting the victim in to the trunk and held her while defendant one performed the act charged, the jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant two had the requisite intent to be found guilty of aggravated criminal sexual assault; 3) the trial court did not err in admitting certain evidence and testimony because such was either connected to the crime or clearly established defendant two's guilt; and 4) the trial court did not err in limiting defense counsel's cross-examination of the victim because the questions did not relate to her possible biases, interests, or motives to testify.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant two's conviction and sentence for aggravated criminal sexual assault, holding that the record supported the jury finding him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court reversed defendant one's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault and remanded the cause for a new trial, finding that he was denied his constitutional right to waive a jury trial.

People v. Hartzol


No. 1-88-0947


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


222 Ill. App. 3d 631; 584 N.E.2d 291; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2003; 165 Ill. Dec. 112



November 27, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Will Gierach, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder, armed robbery, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and home invasion. He was sentenced to a term of natural life imprisonment for murder; a consecutive, extended term of 60 years for aggravated criminal sexual assault; a concurrent term of 30 years for home invasion; and a concurrent term of 30 years for armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice broke into a family's home demanding money and drugs. During the incident, defendant sexually assaulted the mother, threw a six-month-old infant across the room into a wall, and shot and killed the father. The mother and 13-year-old son identified defendant in a photo array and a lineup. Defendant was found guilty of and sentenced for murder, armed robbery, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and home invasion. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the lineup identification and in court identification were reliable because the witnesses had a good opportunity to view defendant, their degree of attention was good, their certainty was high, and the time elapsed between the commission of the crime and the identification of defendant was only two days. The court also noted that another witness strongly corroborated the identification testimony of the mother and son. The court further held that because the evidence established that defendant was the principal in the murder, the accountability instruction for murder was properly refused. Finally, the court held that the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in its sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder, armed robbery, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and home invasion.

City of Rolling Meadows v. National Advertising Co.


No. 1-89-3080


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


228 Ill. App. 3d 737; 593 N.E.2d 551; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 2019; 170 Ill. Dec. 662



November 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE ARTHUR L. DUNNE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporations sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in favor of appellee city on its complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief to enforce a restrictive covenant that prohibited off-premise billboards in an industrial park.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporations filed a federal civil rights action against appellee city, which was resolved when appellee amended its zoning ordinance and issued permits for appellants' advertising billboards. However, when appellee learned of a restrictive covenant applicable to the property in the industrial park where appellants were located, it filed a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief to enforce the restrictive covenant and to prohibit appellants' billboards. The trial court awarded judgment to appellee, enforced the covenant, and ordered appellants to remove the billboards. On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that the federal civil rights action did not act as res judicata, under either the same evidence test or the transactional test. Appellee's action could have been sustained without reference to the zoning ordinance and, although both actions involved appellants' attempt to erect billboards in the industrial park, the actions stemmed from different conduct at different times. Appellant did not acquire a vested right in the permit. Laches did not bar enforcement of the covenant. Enforcement did not violate Ill. Const. art. VIII, § 1(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellee city enforcing a restrictive covenant which prohibited billboards by appellant corporations in an industrial park. The action was not barred by res judicata, even though appellants' prior federal civil rights action resulted in permits being issued for the billboards.

Scott v. Illinois State Police Merit Bd.

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division

November 21, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Anthony J. Scotillo, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his petition seeking review of a decision from appellee State Police Merit Board (board) ordering disciplinary suspension.


OVERVIEW: The police officer challenged a decision from the board ordering a three-day disciplinary suspension. The trial court dismissed the police officer's complaint and he sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court found that the police officer would have had no greater right to a review of his suspension if he were a county or municipal officer than were afforded him under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 307.13 (1987). The police officer was accorded the opportunity for review of his suspension as was required under constitutional principles and the public policy of Illinois. It did not appear that the suspension was either summarily imposed or arbitrarily upheld by the board without any opportunity to be heard. The court held that a meeting fell within the exception to the Open Meetings Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, para. 41 (1989) et seq.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court dismissing the police officer's petition challenging the board's decision regarding review his three day disciplinary suspension was affirmed.

People v. Hough

Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


221 Ill. App. 3d 447; 582 N.E.2d 259; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1964; 164 Ill. Dec. 51



November 20, 1991, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 89-CF-63; the Hon. William R. Todd, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction for three counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 -- 14 (1989), by the Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in precluding any evidence of prior sexual activity by the victim, who was eight years old, under the rape-shield statute and that had been denied effective assistance of counsel for failing to advance that argument in a post-trial motion. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and held that defendant had waived the rape-shield-statute argument by failing to advance it and that his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel failed because he suffered no prejudice by counsel's failure to include it. The court held that given the evidence, a rational trier of fact could easily have concluded that defendant's testimony was untruthful and that he was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt and that defendant's consecutive sentences were not excessive when compared to sentences for other similar offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for three counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault.
