Martel Enterprises v. Chicago


No. 1-89-0108


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


223 Ill. App. 3d 1028; 584 N.E.2d 157; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1924; 164 Ill. Dec. 945



November 15, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 6, 1992. Released for Publication February 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; Honorable Louis J. Giliberto, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, after a jury trial, entered a directed verdict in favor of plaintiff company and entered a judgment on the jury's verdict for plaintiff owner in an action against the city for conversion and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Police officers confiscated fireworks from the company, which were subsequently destroyed, and arrested the owner for possession of illegal fireworks. After a jury trial, the trial court entered a directed verdict against the city on the company's conversion claim, and the jury returned a verdict against the city on the owner's false imprisonment claim. The court reversed the directed verdict and remanded for a new trial, holding that the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 1-101, et seq. (1989), was applicable to the conversion claim and the city might have been immune from liability. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion by excluding evidence of the city ordinance that allowed the police to destroy seized property that was dangerous to store. The court held that the company was not required to establish that the fireworks were legal as an element of conversion. The court affirmed the verdict against the city on the false imprisonment claim, holding that the evidence did not overwhelmingly favor the city; thus, a judgment notwithstanding the verdict would not have been proper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the directed verdict against the city on the company's conversion claim and remanded for a new trial. The court affirmed the jury's verdict against the city on the owner's false imprisonment claim.

Times Mirror Cable Television, Inc. v. First Nat'l Bank


No. 4-91-0304


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


221 Ill. App. 3d 340; 582 N.E.2d 216; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1919; 164 Ill. Dec. 8



November 14, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication December 16, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 16, 1991. As Corrected January 29, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 89CH156; Hon. Richard J. Cadagin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cable provider sued defendant mobile home park owners, seeking a permanent injunction against the mobile home park owner's refusal to allow park access to the cable provider. The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) permanently enjoined the mobile home park owners from precluding the cable provider from installing cable television facilities at the park. The mobile home park owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: A cable provider notified a mobile home park's owners of its intent to install cable television facilities at the mobile home park. The mobile home park owners denied access to the park. The cable provider brought suit seeking a permanent injunction against the mobile home park's owners, alleging that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-42-11.1 (1989) precluded owners and operators of residential properties from denying access. The trial court permanently enjoined the mobile home park owners from precluding the cable provider from installing cable television facilities. On appeal, the court held that neither the United States nor Illinois Constitutions required a predeprivation hearing because the statute adequately protected the property owner's due process rights, that the statute adequately protected the owner's right to just compensation, and that the circuit court did not err in finding that the cable provider provided valid notice. The statute recognized the property owner's right to just compensation.


OUTCOME: The judgment enjoining the mobile home park owners from precluding the cable provider from installing cable television facilities was affirmed.

People v. Debusk


Nos. 1-87-3699, 1-88-0312


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1914



November 13, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; Honorable Matthew J. Moran, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; Reversed and remanded in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: First defendant and second defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of home invasion and armed robbery, and sentenced them to 25 years imprisonment and life in prison as a habitual offender, respectively.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, first defendant argued, inter alia, that he was denied a fair trial due to numerous implications of prior criminal conduct from witnesses and second defendant's pro se questioning. Second defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in not granting defense counsel's request for the appointment of another attorney to represent him due to a conflict of interest. Upon review, the court found first defendant's arguments without merit and held that in second defendant's case, the trial court's failure to appoint separate counsel or to take adequate steps to ascertain whether the risk was too remote to warrant separate counsel was reversible error.Counsel raised the issue of a potential conflict of interest at least four times several months before trial. Although the trial court superficially inquired into his reasons, no hearing was held concerning any possible conflicts. Based on objections by both defendants, the trial court found that no actual conflict existed. That superficial inquiry was not adequate to determine whether there was a possible risk of a conflict. In addition, second defendant timely requested another attorney.


OUTCOME: First defendant's convictions and sentence for armed robbery and home invasion were affirmed and second defendant's convictions and sentence for armed robbery and home invasion were reversed and remanded to the trial court.

People v. Mitchell


No. 1-88-3396


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


221 Ill. App. 3d 926; 583 N.E.2d 78; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1915; 164 Ill. Dec. 524



November 13, 1991  
November 13, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James M. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which convicted him of second degree murder pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was armed, became involved in a struggle with his girlfriend's ex-boyfriend. Defendant allegedly accidentally shot the ex-boyfriend three times during the struggle. Defendant also was shot and was treated at the hospital where he was arrested. Defendant subsequently was convicted of second degree murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2 (1987). On appeal, defendant contended that the statute violated the state and federal constitutions because it relieved the state from proving every element beyond a reasonable doubt, it violated the separation of powers, and it violated due process and equal protection. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and held that: (1) it was constitutional to require defendant to prove the mitigating factor by a preponderance of the evidence to reduce his conviction; (2) there was nothing in the statute prohibiting the state from charging defendant with second degree murder initially; (3) the evidence was sufficient to establish beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had an actual but unreasonable belief in his right to use self-defense; and (4) the trial court's rejection of the accidental shooting defense was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for second degree murder.

People v. Allen

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION

Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1. He was sentenced to a natural life in prison without parole and seven years on the arson conviction.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's murder and arson conviction.

People v. Ford


No. 4-90-0474


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


221 Ill. App. 3d 354; 581 N.E.2d 1189; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1889; 163 Ill. Dec. 766



November 7, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication December 18, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 89CF1632; Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him of intentional homicide of an unborn child. He contended that the fetal homicide statute violated the equal protection and due process clauses of the United States Constitution and that the evidence was insufficient to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of intentional homicide of an unborn child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the intentional homicide of an unborn child after he was found to have kicked the stomach of his pregnant stepdaughter, causing the death of her unborn child. The court affirmed the conviction. The fetal homicide statute did not violate the equal protection clause as it neither affected a fundamental right nor discriminated against a suspect class and the imposition of criminal penalties bore a rational relation to the protection of the potentiality of life. Further, the court rejected defendant's argument that the phrase "caused the death," absent statutory definitions of when life begins and death occurs, was constitutionally vague as the trier of fact was not required to decide whether the entity within the mother's womb was a person or human being, but only that it once had life which was snuffed out by the acts of the defendant. The court also found the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction as defendant knew his stepdaughter was pregnant, he had the requisite criminal intent to cause the death of her unborn child, and that the fetus was alive prior to his actions and thereafter expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for intentional homicide of an unborn child and the sentence imposed.

Evanston v. Paden


No. 1-90-1766


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


221 Ill. App. 3d 1003; 583 N.E.2d 47; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1864; 164 Ill. Dec. 493



November 1, 1991  
November 1, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Jerome Garoon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed three complaints against defendant property owners alleging that the properly owners' building contained exterior violations of the city's housing code and that the owners refused to grant the city the right of entry for an interior inspection. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied the city's application for an administrative inspection search warrant. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court refused to grant the city's request for an administrative inspection search warrant because the city failed to plead in its complaints that there were interior violations at the building. The trial court held that some probable cause was necessary in order to obtain such a warrant. The property owners argued that the trial court's order was not a final appealable order. The court found no reference to the procedures governing administrative inspection search warrants in the court rules or any statute. The court inferred that the legislature, by the inclusion of the express right to appeal under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 108A-10 and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604, 134 Ill. 2d R. 604, intended to exclude the right to appeal from a denial of an application for a search warrant. Therefore, the court determined that the trial court's order denying the application for a search warrant was not appealable.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the city's appeal from an order denying the city's application for a search warrant.

Rumbold v. Bureau


No. 3-90-0637


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


221 Ill. App. 3d 222; 581 N.E.2d 809; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1871; 163 Ill. Dec. 655



October 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Bureau County; the Hon. C. Howard Wampler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant farmers challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Bureau County (Illinois), which dismissed the farmers' third amended complaint against appellees, municipality and official, with prejudice in the farmers' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and intentional infliction of emotional distress action, which arose from an incident where the farmers were fined for violating a municipal weight transport ordinance that was later struck down.


OVERVIEW: The farmers were transporting grain over municipal roads, when they were stopped and fined for violation of an ordinance limiting freight weight. The ordinance was later struck down. The farmers filed an action for deprivation of their constitutional and statutory rights and for intentional infliction of emotional distress. The trial court dismissed the action with prejudice for failure to state a cause of action. The farmers appealed. The court affirmed the dismissal of the counts for unlawful arrest because the farmers were never arrested, and for intentional infliction of emotional distress because the pleadings failed to allege the elements of intentional infliction of emotional distress. The court reversed the dismissal of the farmers' civil rights claims. The municipality and the official would be liable if the farmers prevailed. Allegations that property was unlawfully seized and that the farmers were deprived of property and the free and lawful use of public highways without notice were sufficient to state a cause of action under § 1983 for violation of the farmers' rights under the Fourth and Fourteenth amendments and the due process clause of the Fourteenth amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing claims for illegal arrest and for intentional infliction of emotional distress in the farmers' complaint against the municipality and the official for alleged civil rights violations. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of claims for deprivation of property and of the free and lawful use of public highways and remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Thomas


Nos. 2-89-0711, 2-89-1016 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


220 Ill. App. 3d 110; 580 N.E.2d 1353; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1807; 163 Ill. Dec. 12



October 21, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication November 22, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; No. 88-CF-1511; Hon. Thomas E. Hogan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) convicted defendant of possession of a hypodermic needle and found him in contempt of court. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: After being convicted of unlawful possession of a hypodermic needle pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 38, par. 22-50 and contempt, defendant sought review. Defendant contended that the trial court's evidentiary rulings denied him a fair trial; that the AIDS testing statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 38, par. 1005-5-3(h), was unconstitutional; and that the trial court erred in finding defendant in contempt for failing to comply with the court's testing order. The court rejected defendant's contentions, finding that the trial court's evidentiary error in refusing to admit a report was harmless. The court also found that although extraneous or unauthorized information reaching the jury was prejudicial error, because the information of which defendant complained was no different from that provided through competent evidence admitted at trial, the court could not say that the exchange between the court and the foreperson impeached the jury's verdict. The court further found that the AIDS-testing statute was not unconstitutional because it complied with U.S. Const. amend. IV's standards for reasonableness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Consumers Ill. Water Co. v. County of Will


No. 3-90-0816


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


220 Ill. App. 3d 93; 580 N.E.2d 927; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1796; 162 Ill. Dec. 744



October 18, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication November 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; No. 90-CH-5449; Hon. William R. Penn, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor citizens group appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which denied its motion to vacate the agreed settlement order entered by the circuit court between a utility company and the county.


OVERVIEW: The utility company brought suit against the county seeking a declaratory judgment that the county's zoning ordinance as applied was unconstitutional. Prior to trial, the utility company and the county entered into an agreed settlement order which granted the utility company a special use permit for a wastewater treatment facility. The citizens group subsequently filed a petition to intervene and a motion to vacate the order. The citizens group argued that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to enter the order because it did not contain a finding of unconstitutionality. It also argued that the trial court unlawfully bypassed the legislative process by approving the order without a three-fourths vote of the county board approving the special use permit. The court held that state law did not require a three-fourths vote for a special use permit when written objections were filed. Moreover, because a majority of the board voted to grant the special use, the trial court's entering of the agreed order was not improper. All other remaining issues were rendered moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order denying the citizens group's motion to vacate.

La Salle Nat'l Bank v. Harris Trust & Sav. Bank


No. 1-89-1732


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


220 Ill. App. 3d 926; 581 N.E.2d 363; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1777; 163 Ill. Dec. 412



October 18, 1991  
October 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; Hon. Sophia H. Hall and the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a bank as trustee and an associated individual, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed its action against appellee neighboring property owners, seeking to enforce a local zoning ordinance pursuant to § 11--13--15 of the Illinois Municipal Code (Code), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11--13--15 (1985).


OVERVIEW: A bank as trustee and an associated individual (bank) filed suit against two property owners, trustees of different trusts, seeking to enforce a local zoning ordinance pursuant to § 11-13-15 of the Code. The complaint alleged violations of a special use, including unauthorized use of the property for commercial vehicles, for repair and washing of automobiles, failure to landscape a certain strip, and extension of the parking lot. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court reversed, and held that Chicago's status as a home rule unit did not deprive the bank of the statutory authority conferred by § 11-13-15 of the Code. The court also held that the bank sufficiently complied with § 11-13-15 by alleging that its property would be substantially affected by the violations, and explained that an owner need not prove any specific or unique damages in order to maintain a suit; it was the nature of the zoning violation itself that established the substantial effect sufficient for an action. Moreover, the filing of a suit by the city did not preclude suits by neighboring landowners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court dismissing an action by a bank and an individual to enforce a local zoning ordinance. The case was remanded.

Granite City Div. of Nat'l Steel Co. v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 5-90-0101


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


221 Ill. App. 3d 68; 581 N.E.2d 703; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1792; 163 Ill. Dec. 549



October 15, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for review of order of Pollution Control Board Rulemaking Order. R88-21, Dockets A and B Amendments to Title 35 Subtitle C(Toxis Control); Nos. 5-90-0101, 5-90-0431. Petition for Review of a Pollution Control Board Rulemaking Order. R88-21, Dockets A and B amendments to Title 35 Subtitle C(Toxics Control); Nos. 1-90-0580, 1-90-2143.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporations sought review of the decisions of respondent Illinois Pollution Control Board to adopt amendments to existing water quality regulations, as codified at Ill. Admin. Code tit. 35, §§ 301-309 (1985). The corporations had filed two separate petitions for review, which were consolidated for consideration.


OVERVIEW: The corporations contended that the proposed amendments that governed the derivation and application of criterion under the narrative standard were invalid as an impermissible attempted delegation of Board responsibility to the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency. Further, they argued that the new narrative standard violated due process proscriptions against vagueness and that the Board's rulemaking was invalid due to its failure to consider adequately the amended regulations' technical feasibility and economic reasonableness. The court affirmed the Board's decision and held that the Board merely granted the responsibility to derive and apply the Board's criteria to the agency according to detailed guidelines. Thus, the grant did not constitute an improper delegation of authority. Further, the corporations failed to prove that the regulations were void for vagueness merely due to a difference in expert calculations. The court deferred to the Board's expertise in technical and scientific methodology. Moreover, the Board specifically addressed the issues of technical feasibility and economic reasonableness, and those decisions were also to be accorded deference.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the opinions and orders of the Board in each of the docketed petitions.

People v. C.S.


No. 2-89-0644


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1766



October 11, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 88-CM-1712; Honorable Richard W. Vidal, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the orders of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which demanded that defendant undergo a blood test for human immunodeficiency virus (HIV) and disclose the positive test results.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to unauthorized possession of a hypodermic needle or syringe, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 22-50(1) (1989), and was sentenced. Thereafter, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(h) (1989), the lower court ordered defendant to submit to HIV testing. The test results were positive, and the state moved for disclosure of the results. The court ordered defendant to report for treatment information from public health officials. It also ordered that defendant's test results be disclosed to certain state officials. The lower court found it necessary and in the public interest that law enforcement personnel be protected against physical harm in future contacts with defendant and that both law enforcement personnel and lawyers in the state's attorney's office be informed of facts sufficient to initiate or institute proper criminal charges in future contacts with defendant. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the requirement that she be tested for HIV, and that even if she was constitutionally tested for HIV, the lower court's disclosure order was an abuse of discretion. The court affirmed the lower court's orders.


OUTCOME: The testing was justified and not unconstitutional. Regarding disclosure, even weighing defendant's privacy interests there was no reason to disturb the lower court's determination that the public officials should be informed of defendant's positive test for HIV. Those officials could protect their health by using appropriate levels of caution in any contact with defendant. The court affirmed the lower court's orders against defendant.

Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District

DISPOSITION: Order Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employer appealed an order of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which granted defendant claimants' motion to dismiss a complaint brought by the employer. The employer also appealed the denial of its petition for a preliminary injunction.

People v. McDade


No. 4-91-0111


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


219 Ill. App. 3d 317; 579 N.E.2d 1173; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1666; 162 Ill. Dec. 359



September 30, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication September 30, 1991


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended January 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; No. 90CF1395; Hon. John R. DeLaMar, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a jury verdict in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of criminal sexual assault in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 -- 13 (1989), and from his sentence of two consecutive seven-year terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted the evidence was not sufficient to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of vaginal and anal penetration by force and that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing him to two consecutive seven-year terms. The trial court stated § 5 -- 8 -- 4(a) of the Corrections Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 8 -- 4(a) (1989) required the imposition of consecutive sentences. The trial court found that, because of the particular facts and circumstances of the case, the prolonged and brutal nature of the assault, and defendant's past conviction for battery, more than a minimum sentence was necessary. The court affirmed. The jury had sufficient evidence to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt on both counts of criminal sexual assault. The victim explicitly testified she did not consent to either vaginal or anal intercourse and the jury had an opportunity to listen to extensive cross-examination of the victim as well as the other witnesses for the prosecution. The jury had the opportunity to listen to defendant's version of what happened. The trial court properly considered the circumstances of the case when imposing the sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for two counts of criminal sexual assault and the two consecutive seven-year sentences.

 

1057 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Newbern


No. 4-90-0568


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


219 Ill. App. 3d 333; 579 N.E.2d 583; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1667; 161 Ill. Dec. 912



September 30, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication October 30, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; No. 89CF391; Hon. Rodney A. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of first degree murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9 -- 1. Defendant argued that prosecutors failed to prove his use of deadly force was not justified, that the second degree murder statute was unconstitutional, that the court should reduce the offense to second degree murder, and that prosecutors engaged in improper cross-examination.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of first degree murder despite his claim of self-defense, argued that the second degree murder statute unconstitutionally required defendant to prove rather than have prosecutors disprove the existence of a mitigating factor. The court held that the new homicide statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9 -- 1, still required prosecutors to prove all the elements of first degree murder, but permissibly required defendant to prove the mitigating circumstances of second degree, either sudden passion or unreasonable belief of self-defense. The court analogized it to the affirmative defenses of civil litigation. Therefore, second degree murder was a "lesser mitigated" offense; in other words, it was first degree murder but with mitigating circumstances that warranted a lesser punishment. Consequently, the court could not reduce the first degree murder conviction to second degree absent plain error because the jury had made a finding of fact that there were no mitigating circumstances. The court held that cross-examination that elicited opinion testimony as to another witness' credibility was a de minimis error not objected to at trial and not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of first degree murder because the new homicide statute meant defendant was not entitled to second degree murder absent a showing by defendant of mitigating factors. In addition, this meant that the court was precluded from reducing the offense to second degree absent a showing that no reasonable jury could find that there were no mitigating factors.

People v. Williams


No. 1-89-0609


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of attempted murder and aggravated kidnapping, and found him eligible for an extended-term sentence for exceptionally brutal and heinous behavior. He was sentenced to consecutive terms of 60 years and 15 years, respectively, for attempted murder and aggravated kidnapping. He appealed on various grounds.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court found that defendant took the victim off the streets at gunpoint, drove her about the city, threatened her, tied her up, blindfolded her, then shot her when she attempted to flee. The gunshot severed her spinal cord and rendered her a paraplegic. The circuit court denied defendant's pretrial motion for a court-ordered psychiatric examination of the victim and refused to declare unconstitutional § 115-7.1 of the Criminal Code of 1963, codified at Ill. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court and found that § 115-7.1 did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers. The state legislature was empowered to prescribe new and to alter existing rules of evidence or to prescribe methods of proof. The court also found that § 115-7.1 neither created a suspect classification nor infringed on any fundamental right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which convicted defendant of attempted murder and aggravated kidnapping and gave him an extended-term sentence of 60 years for attempted murder and a consecutive term sentence of 15 years for aggravated kidnapping.

People v. Williams


No. 1-89-1515


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


220 Ill. App. 3d 460; 581 N.E.2d 113; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1645; 163 Ill. Dec. 162



September 27, 1991  
September 27, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; Hon. Richard E. Neville, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and Vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him, upon a jury verdict of armed violence under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A -- 2 (1987) and of attempted second degree murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8 -- 4(a), 9 -- 2 (1987).


OVERVIEW: An altercation in a car between the witness and defendant led to the shooting of a state trooper, which the witness testified was committed by defendant and which defendant claimed was committed by the witness. However, when the trooper ordered the men to cease, the witness handed the weapon to the trooper, and it was the witness who was driving when the trooper heard a driver shouting for help. On appeal of his conviction, defendant contended that his conviction for armed violence arose from the same act as the attempted second degree murder conviction and should be vacated and that the second degree murder conviction was void under Illinois law and unconstitutional. In vacating the second degree murder conviction, the court held that because it was impossible for a person to intend an unreasonable belief that he or she was entitled to use deadly force, defendant's conviction for second degree murder based, as it was on an imperfect self defense, could not stand. However, the court affirmed the armed violence conviction because the vacating of the second-degree murder conviction left only one conviction and thus, there was no incompatibility nor double conviction.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction for attempted second degree murder and affirmed his conviction for armed violence.

People v. Bulliner


No. 1-87-0366


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


220 Ill. App. 3d 438; 581 N.E.2d 86; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1641; 163 Ill. Dec. 135



September 25, 1991  
September 25, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; Hon. John Hourihane, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for attempted murder and aggravated assault and contended that he was denied a fair trial and that the circuit court improperly instructed the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for attempted murder and aggravated assault and was sentenced to six years' imprisonment. The record showed that the charges against defendant were brought because defendant beat and shot a resident of a hotel where defendant also lived. Defendant and the victim got into an argument and a fight and defendant contended that he shot at the victim in self-defense because the victim was swinging a shovel at him. The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial. The court ruled that the prosecutor's questions to defendant during cross-examination and his closing arguments violated defendant's right to remain silent as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. V. The court found that defendant's rights were violated by the prosecutor's repeated questions asking whether he had told the police that the victim had struck him and by later commenting that if defendant had been injured he would have told the police. The prosecutor improperly used defendant's silence at the time of his arrest to impeach defendant's explanation of why he shot at the victim. Also, the court held that defendant's failure to object at trial did not waive the issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment of conviction against defendant for attempted murder and aggravated assault and the court remanded the case for a new trial.

People v. Guidry


No. 1-89-2675


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


220 Ill. App. 3d 406; 581 N.E.2d 38; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1627; 163 Ill. Dec. 87



September 23, 1991  
September 23, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; Hon. Earl E. Strayhorn, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which initially convicted defendant of first-degree murder, and then vacated its finding of guilty of first-degree murder, entered a finding of guilty of second-degree murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2(a) (1987), and sentenced defendant to a term of 15 years' imprisonment in the Illinois Department of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. The trial court heard arguments on post-trial motions, vacated its finding of guilty of first-degree murder, and entered a finding of guilty and judgment of conviction for second-degree murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2(a) (1987). Commonwealth Edison Co. v. Property Tax Appeal Bd.

DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electric company appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which, on administrative review, affirmed a decision of defendant property tax appeal board (PTAB) holding that the electric company's generating machinery and equipment located in a power plant was properly assessed as real property for the 1978 tax year.

People v. Peoples


No. 1-90-0221


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


219 Ill. App. 3d 703; 579 N.E.2d 1001; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1559; 162 Ill. Dec. 187



September 10, 1991  
September 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Michael P. Toomin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of second degree murder. Defendant claimed that the State failed to afford him due process of law by requiring him to prove, in order to escape a first degree murder conviction, that he believed that the killing was justified and that this requirement denied him the equal protection of the law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried without a jury on one count of first degree murder pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1) (1961) and one count of first degree murder pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(2) (1987), for the stabbing death of a man. He was acquitted of both counts and convicted instead of second degree murder pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2(a)(2) (1987). On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that defendant was successful in proving the existence of a factor that allowed him to be convicted of second degree murder instead of first degree murder. Therefore, the court found that defendant was not prejudiced by having to shoulder the burden of proof on the issue; moreover, the court found that the issue became moot when defendant undertook such burden successfully. Accordingly, the court held that defendant had no standing to raise due process and equal protection arguments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of second degree murder.

People v. Rodriguez

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; The Honorable Thomas P. Durkin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder, residential burglary, and home invasion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, residential burglary, and home invasion. The court affirmed those convictions and held that (1) there was substantial evidence to support the verdict; (2) the testimony of two accomplices was sufficiently credible to support the convictions; (3) defendant's conviction of murder was proved beyond a reasonable doubt when viewing the evidence presented in the light most favorable to the prosecution; (4) defendant's conviction for home invasion was proper because he knew or had reason to know that the victim was present when he entered the home; (5) because defendant's name was erroneously omitted from the residential burglary count of the indictment, the defect was "formal," and therefore, amendment was permissible; (6) none of the prosecution's statements warranted reversal; and (7) there was no abuse of discretion in the sentence imposed. The court held that judgment was inadvertently entered on the charge of armed violence, which had been dismissed before trial; it therefore vacated that portion of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of murder, home invasion, and residential burglary. The court vacated the portion of the judgment that convicted defendant of armed violence.

People v. Denning


No. 1-89-3252


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


219 Ill. App. 3d 428; 579 N.E.2d 943; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1579; 162 Ill. Dec. 129



September 5, 1991  
September 5, 1991, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Patrick S. Grossi, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for criminal sexual abuse and contended that the evidence presented at trial was insufficient to sustain his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was found guilty of criminal sexual abuse of his four-year-old granddaughter, contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction and that the circuit court erred in admitting certain statements the victim made to her mother. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, held that the evidence was sufficient to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, and concluded that his constitutional rights were not violated by the admission of the evidence in question. Defendant was informed of the statements the State intended to introduce at trial and there was an adequate basis in the record upon which the circuit court could have determined that the victim's statements were reliable. The victim made repeated and consistent statements about defendant poking and rubbing her vagina and her mother's physical observations supported the finding of sexual abuse. The court held that the circuit court did not err in admitting defendant's statements to the police and that the State was not required to produce the corroborating testimony of a witness to the confession because defendant had the opportunity to cross-examine the witness at the suppression hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment of conviction against defendant for criminal sexual abuse.

People v. Allen


No. 1-89-2416


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division

August 30, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Romie Palmer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for armed violence and aggravated battery in violation of Ill. Rev. Sat. ch. 38, para. 9-1, 12-4(a), and 33A-2 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed violence and aggravated battery for the stabbing of his father. Defendant contended that he was denied a fair trial and that his sentence was unconstitutionally disproportionate to the offense charged. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the aggravated battery and ruled that the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in failing to hold a fitness hearing prior to trial. 1068 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Batavia v. Allen


No. 2-90-1103


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


218 Ill. App. 3d 545; 578 N.E.2d 597; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1492; 161 Ill. Dec. 239



August 30, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; No. 89-OV-5723; the Hon. Roger C. Eichmeier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which had entered judgment in favor of defendant tavern owner and declared a city ordinance that required the doors and windows of taverns remain closed during business hours was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city's complaint alleged that the tavern owner allowed the front door of her tavern to remain open in violation of a municipal ordinance that tavern windows and doors were to remain closed at all times. The court reversed the judgment in favor of the tavern owner and the finding that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The court agreed with the city that the door and window regulation was a valid exercise of its police power to regulate licenses, and the ordinance was a licensing restriction and not a zoning provision; it regulated establishments based on the type of business they conduct, not based on their location. The court stated that the ordinance had no effect of access to light or fresh air, additionally, the ordinance's preamble stated that it was enacted to control noise and preventing disturbing noises was a legitimate governmental purpose. The court held that the ordinance was rationally related to the goal of preventing disturbing noise. Although keeping tavern doors and windows closed might not have been the only way, or the best way, or the least intrusive way of controlling noise from such establishments, it was not an unreasonable way.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the tavern owner and the decision that the city's ordinance that required the doors and windows of taverns remain closed during business hours was unconstitutional and remanded.

Thompson v. Franciscan Sisters Health Care Corp.


No. 3-90-0880


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


218 Ill. App. 3d 406; 578 N.E.2d 289; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1467; 161 Ill. Dec. 162



August 28, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication October 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; No. 90 L 10952; the Hon. Edwin B. Grabiec, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor filed a medical malpractice action against defendants, health care corporations, physicians, and medical group. The Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) granted defendants' motions to dismiss the complaint for failure to comply with the statute of limitations for medical malpractice cases, § 13-212 of the Code of Civil Procedure, Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 110, para. 13-212 (1989).


OVERVIEW: Complication arose during the minor's birth, and defendants allegedly did not respond to those complications in a timely and proper manner. The minor alleged that due to defendants' negligence she was permanently and severely damaged. Fourteen years after her birth, the minor filed her medical malpractice lawsuit, which was later dismissed by the trial court for failure to comply with § 13- 212. Section 13-212 set forth the statute of limitation period for medical malpractice claims. On appeal, the minor argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 110, para. 13-212(b) violated her due process rights. The court held that the legislature, when faced with the need to set some reasonable time limits on medical malpractice claims, was allowed to assume that minors' parents looked after the interests of the affected minors. Therefore, the court held that it was not violation of the minor's due process rights. The court also held that the § 13-212(b) did not violate the minor's equal protection rights because a shortened statute of limitations was not unreasonable in light of what the legislature sought accomplish via § 13-212(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to dismiss the minor's medical malpractice claim.

People v. Brown


No. 1-89-1708


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


218 Ill. App. 3d 890; 578 N.E.2d 1168; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1453; 161 Ill. Dec. 522



August 28, 1991  
August 28, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified November 20, 1991. Rehearing Denied November 20, 1991. As Corrected March 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joan Corboy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of second degree murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2(1987) and sentenced him to 10 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that second degree murder statute was unconstitutional because it shifted the burden of proving an element of murder to him; that it violated due process and equal protection by deterring those convicted of second degree murder from appealing their convictions; that he acted in self-defense when he shot the victim; that he was improperly convicted of two counts of second degree murder for only one crime; and that it was an abuse of discretion to give him a 10-year sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and vacated in part. The statute did not violate due process or equal protection rights. The trial court did not err in its finding that the state negated self-defense beyond a reasonable doubt. Therefore, the second degree murder conviction was proper. However, there could only be only one murder conviction and one sentence for one count of murder, as there was only one death. Therefore, the conviction on one count of second degree murder was vacated. In light of the trial court's clear statement that it considered all relevant factors, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to 10 years' imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed conviction on one count and also vacated conviction on another count of second degree murder.

People v. James

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which denied defendant's petition to elect treatment under § 10-101 of the Illinois Alcoholism and Other Drug Dependency Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 6360-1 (1989), in lieu of incarceration, because defendant had an unresolved felony offense in an unrelated case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was due to be resentenced after his sentence of probation for burglary was revoked. Defendant was also due to be sentenced for theft, to which charge he had pled guilty. Defendant petitioned for treatment under § 10-101 of the Illinois Alcoholism and Other Drug Dependency Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 6360-1 (1989), in lieu of incarceration. The trial court denied defendant's petition because defendant had an additional unresolved felony case that was still pending. The court found that the legislature did not intend that all drug addicts were to be eligible for this alternative treatment. The court held that the legislature's exclusion for treatment of defendant's who had pending felonies was not violative of due process of equal protection because the classification of defendants who had pending charges was not a suspect classification and was reasonably designed to remedy identified threats to public health, safety, and welfare.

People v. Marcotte


No. 5-89-0462


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


217 Ill. App. 3d 797; 577 N.E.2d 799; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1415; 160 Ill. Dec. 474



August 20, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County. No. 89-CF-11; Hon. Dennis Huber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of attempting to lure a minor into a car in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10 -- 5(b)(10) (1989). In seeking review, defendant claimed that a jury instruction regarding the "lawful purpose" of defendant's actions had created a mandatory presumption, thereby shifting the burden of proof to defendant.


OVERVIEW: On two occasions, defendant allegedly attempted to lure two girls into a car with promises of free haircuts. Thereafter, defendant was charged with attempting to lure a minor into a car in violation of § 10 -- 5(b)(10). During the trial, the trial court instructed the jury that the State was required to prove an "unlawful purpose" and that the attempted luring of a child under the age of 16 into a motor vehicle without consent established an "unlawful purpose" unless rebutted or contradicted. Following a conviction, defendant sought review, claiming the instruction had created a mandatory rather than a permissive inference, thereby shifting to defendant the burden of proof and persuasion. Upon review, the court initially held that the words "other than a lawful purpose" did not constitute an element of the child abduction offense but provided an affirmative defense under § 10 -- 5(c)(4). Notwithstanding defendant's failure to present an affirmative defense, the court held the jury had been erroneously instructed because the jury had not been given a choice in applying or rejecting the presumption, thereby forcing defendant to present evidence rebutting the State's case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment convicting defendant of attempting to lure a minor into a car.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for two counts of murder, home invasion, attempted armed robbery, and armed violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of murder, home invasion, attempted armed robbery, and armed violence. Defendant appealed his convictions, alleging that the state knowingly used perjured testimony at trial. The court found that mere conflicts in the testimony of a witness with prior statements made by him did not establish that the witness had given perjured testimony. The court held that defendant failed to establish by satisfactory evidence that the testimony in question was willfully and purposely falsely given. Defendant also contended that the trial court violated his right to due process when it convicted him of multiple counts of murder, home invasion, and armed violence. The court stated that where there was only one person murdered, only one conviction was allowed. The court also held that defendant's conviction for armed violence was error because it was predicated upon the murder conviction and, as such, based upon the same act as the underlying felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on one count of murder, home invasion and attempted armed robbery. The court vacated defendant's conviction for felony murder and armed violence.

People v. Nicholson


No. 1-87-1535


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


218 Ill. App. 3d 273; 577 N.E.2d 1313; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1341; 160 Ill. Dec. 742



August 7, 1991  
August 7, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Donald E. Joyce, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, following a jury trial, convicted defendant of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and criminal trespass to vehicle.


OVERVIEW: After the state had exercised peremptory challenges to dismiss two African-American venirepersons, defendant, a black man, raised a Batson objection. Although the judge did not require the state to explain its peremptory challenges, the assistant state's attorney did offer some explanation. The trial court denied the defendant's motion. After the state had exercised its fifth peremptory challenge, defendant raised another Batson objection. Defense counsel argued that the state had exercised all five of its peremptory challenges to strike blacks from the jury. The court noted that there was no systematic exclusion because, at that point, there were two black jurors on the panel. The court denied defendant's motion for a Batson hearing. After conviction by the jury, defendant appealed. The court remanded the matter to the circuit court for a Batson hearing because it found that defendant established a prima facie case of racial discrimination in the state's use of its peremptory challenges. If the state was successful in its explanations then the conviction was to be affirmed; if not, then the conviction was to be vacated and a new trial ordered.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the circuit court for a Batson hearing. Upon remand, the state was required to come forward with neutral explanations sufficient to rebut defendant's prima facie case. If the state failed to come forward with neutral explanations, the defendant's conviction was to be vacated and defendant was to receive a new trial.

Hamilton v. Ceasar


No. 1-90-2308


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


218 Ill. App. 3d 268; 578 N.E.2d 221; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1323; 161 Ill. Dec. 94



August 6, 1991  
August 6, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Mary Heftel Hooton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that struck his jury demand in a paternity suit because he failed to pay the statutory jury fee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee mother filed a paternity action against the father. On the day of trial, the father requested a jury. The trial court struck his request because the father had failed to pay the jury fee as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, para. 27.2(14)(b) (1987). The father appealed, and the court affirmed. The father did not have a constitutionally protected right to a jury trial in a paternity action. Determination of paternity was not recognized at common law; therefore, no constitutional right to trial by jury inhered in such an action. Further, a paternity suit was a civil action and not quasi-criminal in nature. Finally, required of the fee did not violate the father's equal protection rights because a free jury trial in the context of a paternity action neither implicated a fundamental right nor involved a statutory classification based on race, alienage, or national origin.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that struck the father's request for a jury trial in a paternity action.

Bach v. County of St. Clair


No. 5-90-0485


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


217 Ill. App. 3d 291; 576 N.E.2d 1236; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1352; 160 Ill. Dec. 282

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mobile home owners appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which held defendant county had the right to enforce St. Clair Cty., Ill., Rev. Code of Ordinances ch. 42. Three separate cases were consolidated in the circuit court before the home owners filed their appeal.


OVERVIEW: Three mobile home owners possessed homes which did not comply with federal regulations, and, thus, did not comply with ch. 42 which incorporated those regulations. One home owner's structure did comply with federal regulations, but it was only 12 feet wide, and St. Clair Cty., Ill., Rev. Code of Ordinances ch. 42, § 42.131(f) required that mobile homes be 14 feet wide before they would be eligible for special use permits. The lower court held that ch. 42 was valid and constitutional, and the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court ruled that the three home owners whose structures did not comply with federal regulations did not have standing to challenge the validity or the constitutionality of ch. 42 because they all admitted that the federal standards were proper. However, the home owner whose structure did comply with federal regulations proved there was no rational basis for St. Clair Cty., Ill., Rev. Code of Ordinances ch. 42, § 42.131(f) and that § 42.131(f) violated her rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970)


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which held that the three home owners whose structures did not comply with federal regulations had no claim that the special use ordinances were improper as applied to them. However, the lower court's judgment was reversed with respect to the homeowner whose structure did comply with federal regulations, and the special use restrictions were unconstitutional as applied to her.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state department of professional regulation (department) sought interlocutory review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff dentist's motion to enjoin sanctions levied by the department and the dentist sought review of the subsequent decision of the trial court which granted judgment on the merits in favor of the department.


OVERVIEW: In the administrative proceedings, the dentist was found guilty and was sanctioned for violating the advertising provisions of the Illinois Dental Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, par. 2301 et seq. (1987 repealed) (act). The dentist sought review of the decision and the trial court granted his petition to temporarily enjoin the sanctions. DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which ordered it to issue a building permit to plaintiff property owners in a suit for a writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: Village denied property owners a building permit for construction of a single family residence on property they had recently purchased due to a certain zoning ordinance. Owners contended village official told them that the property was buildable; therefore, they instituted an action against village to compel issuance of a permit. The trial court ordered the review and approval within 30 days of owners building plans, which owners appealed prior to the status date. The evidence established that plaintiffs as innocent parties had substantial expenditures and a change in position made in good faith upon the reasonable probability of a building permit being issued. They had a vested right under the 1974 ordinance.

People ex rel. Hartigan v. E&E Hauling, Inc.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the Attorney General and the Illinois Department of Transportation, sought review from orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed plaintiffs' complaint and denied leave to file an amended complaint. Plaintiffs charged defendant contracting businesses with fraud, misrepresentation, breach of contract, and unjust enrichment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that defendants wrongfully and fraudulently attempted to avoid compliance with the minority business enterprise (MBE) provisions contained in the contracts, as well as state and federal policy requiring the use of MBEs. Defendants performed work on several state construction projects. Plaintiffs argued that the trial court erred in finding that the Attorney General lacked standing and in finding that the Consumer Fraud Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. § 1987, ch. 121 1/2, par. 261 et seq. (CFA), was inapplicable. The court held that in light of the undeniable interest of the state and its people in the proper allocation of public funds and the apparent lack of any other adequate means of redress, the Attorney General was not precluded from asserting the fraud claims. Further, the trial court erred in holding that the CFA was inapplicable absent an allegation of injury to consumers. In addition, the court held that the trial court properly dismissed counts I, II, V, VI, VII, VIII, IX, X, XI, XII, and XIII for failure to state a cause of action. However, the trial court erred in finding that counts III, IV, XIV, XV, XVI, XVII, and XVIII failed to state causes of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

 

1082 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hrobowski


No. 2-89-0299


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


216 Ill. App. 3d 711; 575 N.E.2d 1306; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1228; 159 Ill. Dec. 246



July 19, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication August 22, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 88-CF-1021; Hon. Daniel D. Doyle, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) after a jury found him guilty of first-degree murder, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 38, paras. 9 -- 1(a)(1), (a)(2) and the trial court sentenced him to a term of 50 years' imprisonment. The trial court then denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the state presented more than enough evidence to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had committed the offense with which he was charged. Thus, even if counsel had performed differently, the court was not convinced to a reasonable degree of certainty that the jury would have found otherwise. Moreover, the court believed that, on the whole, defense counsel provided zealous and effective representation. The court found that at no time had counsel conceded defendant's guilt of the crime charged, first-degree murder. Rather, throughout the entire proceeding, including closing argument, counsel vigorously tested and challenged the state's evidence. Accordingly, the court concluded that defendant was not prejudiced by trial counsel's representation, and defendant's argument that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel at trial had to fail. Regarding comments made by the state, the court found that the jury was admonished that the statements of counsel were not evidence and therefore, that the state's remarks, both individually and cumulatively, did not deny defendant a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying defendant's motion for a new trial.

Rodriguez v. Henderson


No. 1-89-1562


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


217 Ill. App. 3d 1024; 578 N.E.2d 57; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1218; 160 Ill. Dec. 878



July 17, 1991  
July 17, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; Reversed in part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, nearby manufacturers, residential owners, and residential lessees, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their amended complaint. The amended complaint alleged the invalidity of a city rezoning ordinance. Grounds for dismissal were that at least some appellants lacked standing and that some or all had failed to state a claim.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged the validity of a city rezoning ordinance on the ground that the rezoning of a parcel holding former factory buildings from a M1-2 restricted manufacturing district to a C1-2 restricted commercial district and then to a commercial-residential planned development was unlawful. The circuit court dismissed their amended complaint generally on a holding that appellants had failed to state a claim of arbitrary and capricious rezoning that would have violated their substantive due process rights under Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970). The court reversed the circuit court in this regard after taking into consideration of such factors as the existing uses and zoning of nearby properties and the extent to which the rezoning would impact the nearby properties. On balance, the court found that the rezoning did not conform to the existing uses or zoning of nearby property, and that would each suffer at least short-term losses, while the rezoned property increased in value. Further, because appellants extensively supported their allegations of special harm, they had standing to challenge the rezoning decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellants' claims that the rezoning violated the city's own rezoning criteria and that the rezoning procedure violated the city's procedural requirements. The court reversed the dismissal of appellant's claim that because of a variety of alleged injuries attributed to the rezoning, the rezoning was arbitrary and capricious in violation of appellants' substantive due process rights.

 

1084 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Pecoraro v. Kesner


No. 1-90-1597


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


217 Ill. App. 3d 1039; 578 N.E.2d 53; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1220; 160 Ill. Dec. 874



July 17, 1991  
July 17, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Marvin H. Ruttenberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lessee appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion to quash service, struck his jury demand and found in favor of plaintiff lessor in a forcible entry and detainer action.


OVERVIEW: The lessee responded to a summons he received by mail by coming before the circuit court seeking a continuance so that he could obtain a lawyer. At the next hearing the lessee appeared before the circuit court and stated that he had obtained counsel, had filed a jury demand, and while mentioning that he had not been properly served with summons, asked for a further continuance. The lessee decided to stand by his claim of special appearance even after his motion to quash service was denied and judgment was entered against him in a bench trial. The court agreed that the totality of the lessee's actions resulted in a general appearance. While appearing pro se to obtain a continuance to obtain counsel was not a general submission to the circuit court's jurisdiction, the subsequent filing of a jury demand and appearance seeking a further continuance constituted a general appearance. But, the circuit court committed reversible error when it struck the lessee's jury demand. The demand was properly and timely filed and there was no basis for striking it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court and ordered a new trial.

People v. Lendabarker


Nos. 2-90-0052, 2-90-0053 consolidated


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


215 Ill. App. 3d 540; 575 N.E.2d 568; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1181; 159 Ill. Dec. 70



July 9, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 89-CF-2388, 87-TR-130063; Honorable John J. Nelligan, Judge, Presiding.

This Opinion Substituted for Withdrawn Opinion of May 9, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 763.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) convicting him of two felony counts of driving while under influence of alcohol in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, par. 11-501(d)(3). Defendant argued that his statutory right to a speedy trial was violated because certain periods of pre-trial delay were wrongly attributed to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of two felony counts of driving while under influence of alcohol (DUI) in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, par. 11-501(d)(3). As a result of his convictions, defendant's court supervision in a prior, unrelated DUI case was revoked. On review, defendant argued that his statutory right to a speedy trial was violated because certain periods of pre-trial delay were wrongly attributed to defendant. The appeals court ruled that only one four-day period was incorrectly ascribed to defendant. The court ruled that defendant's filing of a petition under the Substance Abuse Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, par. 6322, and a motion for substitution of judges lead to a delay that was chargeable to him. The court stated it was irrelevant that the state later decided to nol-pros the charges since the mere filing of the motion and petition made it impossible to set the case for trial before resolving the motions. The court also ruled that a continuance requested by defendant to review a lately discovered videotape was chargeable to defendant, since the state was diligent in informing defendant of the videotape after its discovery.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed defendant's convictions because he was tried within 157 days of the date that he demanded a trial in this matter. The court ruled that only four days were improperly excluded from the speedy trial computations and that the other periods of delay were chargeable to defendant.

Caauwe v. Police Pension Bd.


No. 1-90-2720


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


216 Ill. App. 3d 313; 576 N.E.2d 1078; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1113; 160 Ill. Dec. 124



June 28, 1991  
June 28, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Sophia H. Hall, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff litigant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of defendant police pension board (board). The board denied the litigant's application for a policeman's disability pension under the Illinois Pension Code, Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, paras. 3 to 101 et seq. (1985). The court had previously remanded the board's decision for it to receive certifications of three doctors.


OVERVIEW: The litigant, a veteran policeman, alleged he injured his back during an altercation with a prisoner. The litigant never reported the incident. He applied for a policeman's disability pension. The board denied his request. The trial court affirmed. The court reversed and remanded for the board to receive three certificates of the litigant's disability or lack thereof. The board received one doctor's certification that the litigant was disabled. Another doctor stated he could not determine physical disability. The third doctor did not respond. The board again denied the litigant's application, stating that regardless of the certifications it would not have awarded the disability pension where the litigant failed to present sufficient credible evidence to support his application. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) where the litigant failed to allege in the original proceedings that the board violated his due process rights under the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments by not obtaining three certifications, he waived the issue on appeal; and (2) after careful review of the record, the court could not conclude the decision of the board was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to affirm the board's judgment denying the litigant's application for a policeman's disability pension.

Groenings v. St. Charles


No. 2-90-1052


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


215 Ill. App. 3d 295; 574 N.E.2d 1316; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1129; 158 Ill. Dec. 923



June 28, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 29, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; No. 89-L-746; the Hon. James F. Quetsch, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint against defendant cities for failure to state a cause of action and denied their motion to amend the complaint. The property owners had filed the action after their petition for an annexation of their property was denied.


OVERVIEW: The property owners' petition for annexation of their property from one city to the other was denied based on a boundary agreement between the cities. The property owners filed a complaint that alleged constitutional violations and tortious interference and sought to invalidate the statute authorizing the boundary agreement and the agreement itself. The cities' motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action was granted. The property owners' motion to amend their complaint was denied and they appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court and held (1) that the boundary agreement was authorized by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-12- 9 (1989) because § 11-12-9 contained clear and specific language empowering the cities to agree to restrictions on their annexation activity, (2) § 11-12-9 did not conflict with other Illinois municipal laws, (3) the property owners' due process rights were not violated because they had no legitimate claim of entitlement to an annexation, (4) the deprivation of mere hoped-for economic gain was not a deprivation in the constitutional sense, and (5) the amended complaint failed to state a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court granting the cities' motion to dismiss the property owners' complaint for failure to state a cause of action. The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying the property owners' motion to amend the complaint.
