People v. Thomas


No. 1-88-2819


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


216 Ill. App. 3d 469; 576 N.E.2d 1020; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1143; 160 Ill. Dec. 66



June 28, 1991  
June 28, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert V. Boharic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of second degree murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2(a)(1) (1987), following a bench trial. The trial judge sentenced defendant to the penitentiary for a term of four years.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant attacked the constitutionality of the second degree murder statute, found in § 9-2 of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2 (1987). Defendant first contended that the second degree murder statute violated the due process clause of the fourteenth amendment to the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. However, his argument that the statute relieved the prosecutor from proving beyond a reasonable doubt every element of first degree murder was rejected. Defendant next contended that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2 violated the equal protection clause of either the fourteenth amendment to the United States Constitution or the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. of 1970, art. I, § 2. Defendants convicted of second degree murder did not risk being put in jeopardy any more than defendants convicted of first degree murder. The court held that defendants convicted of second degree murder were not denied the equal protection of the law. Defendant's contention that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2 (1987) violated the separation of powers clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. of 1970, art. II, § 1, was rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

County of Boone v. Department of Revenue


No. 2-90-1253


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


215 Ill. App. 3d 453; 574 N.E.2d 1227; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1081; 158 Ill. Dec. 834



June 25, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 29, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County; No. 86-MR-17; the Hon. David A. Englund, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a county and a county board of review, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Boone County, (Illinois), which held that property owned by defendant Illinois State Tollway Authority was exempt from real estate taxes under the Revenue Act of 1939 (Act). Defendant Illinois Department of Revenue previously held that the property was exempt from real estate taxes.


OVERVIEW: A restaurant and a service station occupied land owned by the Authority and were required to stay open 24 hours a day and to comply with the Authority's rules pertaining to the operation of their business. The term "lease" was not mentioned in either of the agreements that each business signed with the Authority. The Department found that the agreements were licenses and were not subject to real estate taxes under the Act, the lower court affirmed the Department's decision, and the court affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 100-22 (1985) stated that Authority property was exempt from taxation unless the property was leased and that the agreements were licenses and not subject to taxation. The court ruled that because the agreements did not give the businesses control of the premises and only gave the businesses the right to use the property for a specific purpose, the agreements were licenses. Because § 100-22 was clear, the court held that later enactments by the legislature were not useful in interpreting § 100-22.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which held that land owned by the Authority was not subject to real estate property taxes.

Romero v. Selcke


No. 1-90-1097


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


216 Ill. App. 3d 138; 576 N.E.2d 276; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1078; 159 Ill. Dec. 607



June 25, 1991  
June 25, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Anthony J. Scotillo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed; Cause Remanded with Directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foreign-educated nurses sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the nurses' motion for summary judgment and granted summary judgment to appellee director of the state department of professional regulation (the director). The nurses contended that the lower court erred in finding that the director could require them to pass certain examinations prior to licensure.


OVERVIEW: A group of foreign-educated nurses ordinarily would have had to take a preliminary examination before a national examination, but that requirement was suspended by injunction during litigation attacking its validity. The state legislature then passed the Illinois Nursing Act of 1987, Ill, Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 3501 et seq. Under that act, all foreign-educated applicants for nursing licenses were required to take the preliminary examination. The foreign-educated nurses brought an action against the director of the state department of professional regulation, alleging due process violations. In the lower court, both sides moved for summary judgment. The lower court granted the motion of the director, and the nurses appealed. On appeal, the court found that the state had a legitimate interest in regulating the nursing profession. Even though the nurses had passed a higher-level examination than the one sought to be imposed on them, the court found the requirement to be a reasonable exercise of the state's power. The statute was not retroactively applied, as the nurses claimed, because the examination requirement was always in effect, only suspended during the litigation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court and remanded the cause with directions to enter an order concerning notification to all nurses affected by the judgment and setting deadlines for the nurses to take the necessary examination.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner buyer appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that the buyer was not entitled to the issuance of a tax deed. The issuance of the order for deed was contested by respondents, a partnership and its partners.


OVERVIEW: Th partnership acquired title to the property by deed and then executed a trust deed in favor of the trust company to secure an indebtedness and an assignment of rents to the bank. The property was conveyed to another trust company. The buyer filed his tax deed petition, and the sheriff served notice on the trust company, but no attempt was made to serve the partnership. The court reasoned that the partners, as beneficiaries, had a right to redeem from the tax sale by disclosing their interest of record and should have been entitled to notice of the pending expiration of the period of redemption if their names were reasonably ascertainable. In re Estate of Webster


No. 1-90-2605


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


214 Ill. App. 3d 1014; 574 N.E.2d 245; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 947; 158 Ill. Dec. 451



June 7, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Jeffrey A. Malak, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executor sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that the legacies under a will had lapsed and awarded the entire estate to appellee legatee.


OVERVIEW: The executor filed an action for probate of the will of the testator and distribution of the testator's assets. The trial court ruled that the legacy to the testator's stepdaughter, and the contingent residuary legacy to the testator's stepgrandson and lapsed pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, par. 4 -- 6(a) (1989), because their spouses were the only two witnesses to witness the testator's will. The trial court held that the testator's estate passed in its entirety to the legatee, also a step-daughter. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the statute was not an unconstitutional bill of attainder because it was a regulation and not a punishment; (2) the statute did not create an unconstitutional classification; (3) the statute did not create a suspect classification which discriminated against marital relationships ; (4) the statute did not violate due process because legatee's have no vested property rights; (5) the statute was not special legislation because it had a rational relationship to a legitimate state purpose; and (6) the executor failed to state a cause of action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the legatee in the executor's action seeking to uphold legacies contained in a will.

People v. Doyle

Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 88-CF-264; Hon. Barry E. Puklin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which certified him as an habitual child sex offender pursuant to the Habitual Child Sex Offender Registration Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 221 et seq. (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two separate incidents of aggravated criminal assault upon two different children, which occurred at two different times. The lower court certified him as an habitual child sex offender under the Act, and the court affirmed. The court held that because defendant could have been prosecuted in two different trials, he was not permitted to evade the provisions of the Act merely because both criminal charges were consolidated for administrative convenience. The court ruled that the plain meaning of the term "second conviction" under the Act was that the Act applied to those who were convicted twice of any of the enumerated offenses under the Act where the second of the two convictions stemmed from a different act or from an offense that occurred at a different time from the first offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which certified defendant as an habitual child sex offender.

People v. Timberson


No. 5-90-0482


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


213 Ill. App. 3d 1037; 573 N.E.2d 374; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 957; 157 Ill. Dec. 956



June 5, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 87-CF-528; Hon. James K. Donovan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion for a new trial when it found that it erred in denying his motion to dismiss the charge of first-degree murder as barred by principles of double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for second-degree murder. The verdict was silent on the charge of first-degree murder. The conviction was reversed and the cause was remanded for a new trial. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the charge of first-degree murder, claiming that it was barred by the double jeopardy clause and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3-4 (1989). Defendant argued that the jury's previous verdict of guilty of second-degree murder constituted an implied acquittal the first-degree murder charge. The trial court denied the motion and convicted defendant for first-degree murder. Defendant filed a post-trial motion alleging error in the denial of his motion. The trial court agreed and set the cause for a new trial. The state sought review of the order. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, holding that defendant's conviction for second-degree murder constituted an implied acquittal of first-degree murder and that second-degree murder was a lesser-included offense of first-degree murder. The court found that defendant's second trial for first-degree murder violated the double jeopardy clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting defendant a new trial for failing to grant his motion to dismiss the charge of first-degree murder on double jeopardy grounds.

 

1098 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Chicago v. Piotrowski


Nos. 1-89-3266, 1-89-3357 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


215 Ill. App. 3d 829; 576 N.E.2d 64; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 921; 159 Ill. Dec. 395



June 4, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 10, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Julia M. Nowicki, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed an ordinance enforcement action against defendant landfill for operating without a permit. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the city summary judgment and enjoined the landfill from continuing to operate without a permit. The landfill appealed.


OVERVIEW: A landfill was in operation even though it did not have a permit. The city passed an ordinance expanding sanitary landfills, and the landfill applied for a variance. The application was denied, and administrative review of the proceedings was pending. The landfill argued that it was being discriminated against. The court affirmed the trial court's order. It held that allowing the landfill to assert constitutional issues would be contrary to the doctrine of exhaustion of administrative remedies. Although the landfill contended it had been discriminated against, it had not exhausted its administrative remedies. The landfill's continued operation without a license was violative of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 17, § 6.2 (1983) and ch. 99, §§ 4 and 36.1 (1983 and 1986). Therefore, the trial court properly enjoined the landfill from operation.


OUTCOME: The decision granting summary judgment in favor of the city and enjoining the landfill from continuing to operate without a permit was affirmed.

 

1099 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Elworthy


No. 1-88-2133


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


214 Ill. App. 3d 914; 574 N.E.2d 727; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 910; 158 Ill. Dec. 614



May 31, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Shelvin Singer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded for New Trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for possession of cannabis and possession of cocaine with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court be reversed and remanded for new trial because defendant was denied the right to waive a jury trial based upon an unconstitutional statute in effect at the time. The court held that the trial court's denials of defendant's motions to quash the search warrant and suppress evidence were not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court held that the additional affidavits would not establish the untruthfulness of the affidavit presented, and the additional affidavits were not relevant to the hearing. The court held that the state was not required to disclose the informant's identity, where the court found the police officer's testimony regarding the interactions with the informant to be credible after the trial judge reviewed the informant's file. The court held that the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress was proper because the evidence would have been inevitably discovered without the coerced statements. The court also held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion when he imposed a discovery sanction and refused to admit evidence, which defendant did not disclose to the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions remanded for new trial, but upheld the trial court's evidentiary rulings in favor of the state.

Kmoch v. Klein


No. 2-90-1429


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


214 Ill. App. 3d 185; 573 N.E.2d 267; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 884; 157 Ill. Dec. 849



May 28, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; No. 90-L-513; the Hon. Terrence J. Brady, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party filed a tort action against defendant alleged tortfeasors for sexual assault. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) made two interlocutory orders denying the alleged tortfeasors' motion to quash the deposition subpoenas of two witnesses. The alleged tortfeasors sought review of the orders.


OVERVIEW: The alleged tortfeasors filed motions to quash the subpoenas pursuant to the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Confidentiality Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 801 et seq. (1989). The court determined that it did not have jurisdiction to consider the alleged tortfeasors' appeal, which was taken as a right pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 810(b) and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307. The court found there was an apparent ambiguity with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 810(b), as one provision stated such orders were to have been considered final for purposes of appeal, and the other stated that they were subject to interlocutory appeal. Nevertheless, the court found the orders denying the motion to quash were neither final for purposes for appeal nor were subject to interlocutory appeal. The court found a judgment or order was final if it terminated the litigation between the parties on the merits, which the order at issue did not. The court found that the order was interlocutory in nature, made as preliminary discovery orders in a pending suit, and were not appealable because they were reviewable on appeal from the final order.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

In re Estate of Willis


No. 1-89-2536


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


214 Ill. App. 3d 683; 574 N.E.2d 172; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 877; 158 Ill. Dec. 378



May 24, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Jeffrey A. Malak, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which amended the order of heirship in the probate proceeding of the decedent's estate to declare the widow and appellee adult daughters as the decedent's lawful heirs.


OVERVIEW: In a probate proceeding of the decedent's estate, the circuit court entered an order declaring the widow to be the sole heir. Thereafter the adult daughters filed petitions claiming that they were the acknowledged children of the decedent, and, thus, they should have been listed as heirs to his estate. Following a hearing, the circuit court amended its order of heirship to include the adult daughters as lawful heirs. The widow appealed. The court affirmed the judgment. The law did not mandate a paternity action before the circuit court could determine heirship. Under the Probate Act of 1975, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 2-2 (1989), the circuit court was permitted to determine heirship for the adult daughters through acknowledgment by the decedent during his lifetime. Moreover, the totality of the evidence submitted by the adult daughters provided clear and convincing proof that the decedent had acknowledged them as his daughters during his lifetime. Finally, one of the adult daughters presented sufficient evidence to rebut the presumption that her mother's husband was not her father because the husband had no access to the mother at the time of conception.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's amended order declaring heirship to include the adult daughters as lawful heirs of the decedent.

People v. Govin


No. 4-90-0512


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District

The court affirmed, holding, (1) the state presented substantial evidence that defendant aided and abetted an accomplice in causing cocaine to be brought into the state for the purpose of delivery in violation of § 401.1(a) of the Act, (2) the evidence was sufficient for a reasonable trier of fact to conclude that defendant was not entrapped, (3) defendant was subject to the jurisdiction of the state pursuant to § 1-5 of the Criminal Code of 1961 because he aided and abetted a transaction by which cocaine was delivered in the state, (4) § 401.1(a) of the Act was not unconstitutionally vague, (5) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's requested jury instructions because the subjects were adequately covered by other instructions, and (6) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the jury to review certain testimony.

People v. Hart


No. 1-88-1434


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


214 Ill. App. 3d 512; 573 N.E.2d 1288; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 833; 158 Ill. Dec. 103



May 17, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and sentenced him to a term of seven years' imprisonment in the Illinois Department of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse. He appealed. His arguments centered around the admission of statements made by the four-year-old victim to her mother and the investigating police officer. He contended that the trial court erred by admitting the statements under either the spontaneous declaration exception to the hearsay rule or the amended version of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10. The court affirmed. The court found that it did not believe that a child's display of excitement, or lack thereof, was controlling in the determination of whether the statement should be deemed admissible as a spontaneous declaration. Rather, the court believed that the more relevant inquiry was whether the facts of the particular case demonstrated sufficient guarantees of trustworthiness and reliability. The court held that the "totality of the circumstances" approach should be employed to determine whether the statements appeared to be the product of reflection or fabrication. The court opined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it found that the victim's statements to her mother and the officer were excited utterances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse.

People v. Lyons


No. 1-88-2791


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


213 Ill. App. 3d 617; 572 N.E.2d 1163; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 779; 157 Ill. Dec. 699

DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) after a jury convicted him of first degree murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to prison for a term of 26 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a fight with an acquaintance. During that altercation, another individual struck defendant with a stick. The following day, defendant saw the acquaintance in a car and started shooting. A passenger in the car died from a gunshot wound. At trial, defense counsel wanted an instruction on second degree murder other than Ill. Pattern Jury Instructions, Crim. No. 7.06A (2d ed. Supp. 1989). OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the sentence imposed for first degree murder.

People v. Hoke


No. 4-90-0428


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


213 Ill. App. 3d 263; 571 N.E.2d 1143; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 744; 157 Ill. Dec. 124

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ford County; Nos. 89CF97, 89TR1410; Hon. Charles H. Frank, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Ford County (Illinois), which convicted him of four counts of reckless homicide in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-3(a) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of reckless homicide after he operated a car with a blood-alcohol content of greater than 0.10, at an unreasonable speed, and disregarded a stop sign, thereby causing the death of four people. Defendant maintained that he was not acting recklessly because he was trying to help an injured friend. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction and held that the testimony of two six-year old boys in defendant's car at the time of the accident was credible, that they were qualified as witnesses, and that their testimony, together with corroborating evidence of defendant's injuries to his face, was sufficient for a reasonable trier of fact to find, beyond a reasonable doubt, that defendant was driving the car at the time of the collision. Further, the court found no conflict between Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 236, regarding the admission of writings, and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501 (1989), because § 11-501 imposed requirements for the admissibility of written blood tests unrelated to a document's admissibility under the business record exception to the hearsay rule. Further, defendant was required to bear the burden of his own prejudicial remarks made at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for reckless homicide.

Wheaton v. Sandberg


No. 2-90-0640


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


215 Ill. App. 3d 220; 574 N.E.2d 697; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 703; 158 Ill. Dec. 584



May 3, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 24, 1991. Released for Publication July 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; No. 86-ED- 57; the Hon. William E. Black, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied defendants' motion to dismiss and traverse an action by plaintiff city to condemn their property.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an action against the property owners to condemn four retail locations and other nonretail space in their building on the basis that the space was chronically vacant. The property owners filed a motion to dismiss and traverse, alleging that as a home-rule municipality, the city lacked the authority to institute an eminent domain action. The trial court denied the motion and the court reversed. The court held that the exercise of eminent domain power by the city, pursuant to an enabling ordinance found in Wheaton, Ill., City Code ch. 8, art. V, §§ 8-98 to 8-105, as a home-rule municipality to eradicate blight and promote redevelopment was a valid exercise of home-rule power. The Commercial Renewal and Redevelopment Areas Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-74.2-1 et seq. (1987) did not limit or preempt the city's power and the city was not required to abide by uniform standards. The court held that the enabling ordinance was unconstitutional because the phrase referring to vacancies was vague and overly broad. The court found that requiring the presence of only one of the factors enumerated in the ordinance to justify condemnation was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and held that an ordinance that allowed the city to exercise its eminent domain powers was unconstitutionally vague and overly broad.

 

1107 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Godwin


No. 5-89-0133


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


212 Ill. App. 3d 435; 570 N.E.2d 1276; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 719; 156 Ill. Dec. 554



May 2, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 88-CF-150. The Hon. David W. Watt, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which convicted him of felony deceptive practices, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 17 -- 1(B)(d) (1987), and imposed an extended-term sentence.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pleaded guilty to felony deceptive practices in another county, the trial court convicted him of felony deceptive practices under ch. 38, para. 17 -- 1(B)(d), and imposed an extended-term sentence. On appeal, defendant claimed that his instant sentence should be vacated because he was previously convicted of deceptive practices based on transactions occurring within the same 90-day period. The court found that the intent of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 17 -- 1(B) (1987) was to prevent a prosecutor from arbitrarily or intentionally aggregating transactions as to increase defendant's culpability and penalty. The two prosecutors neither arbitrarily divided the charges nor arbitrarily divided the chore of prosecution. Further, in the instant action, the prosecutor's delay in bring charges was due to an administrative oversight. Moreover, equal protection was not violated because any classification created by ch. 38, para. 17--1(B) was reasonably designed to promote the public interest. Thus, defendant's instant conviction was proper. Finally, defendant was eligible for an extended-term sentence by virtue of his previous felony deceptive practices conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision convicting defendant of felony deceptive practices and imposing an extended-term sentence.

People ex rel. Patrick Media Group, Inc. v. Chicago


No. 1-89-3034


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 651



April 24, 1991 


NOTICE: Released for Publication June 12, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn by Order of the Court June 24, 1991. Order Reported at 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1306.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable David J. Shields, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city alderman and an advertising competitor of appellee advertiser, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the competitor and alderman's complaint for a declaratory judgment to declare that a settlement between appellee city and the advertiser was invalid. The trial court had found that the alderman and the competitor did not have standing.


OVERVIEW: The city settled with the first advertiser. Under the agreement, the city varied its zoning ordinance, which required outdoor signs to be set back from expressways. In return, the first advertiser dismissed lawsuit against the city. The competitor and a city alderman sought a declaration that the agreement was invalid. They also sought to have an injunction issued to restrain the city from issuing permits to the first advertiser. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's dismissal of the complaint. The city alderman did not have standing by virtue of his position as alderman alone. He was only a member of the city's finance committee and city council, but he did not have authority to act on behalf of those bodies. As to the competitor, there was standing on equal protection grounds. However, the competitor could not prevail on those merits because there was no purpose to treat the competitor differently. Yet, the court found that the competitor had standing to challenge the action by appellee, the city's corporation counsel, because the competitor's interests in protecting its competitive interests were sufficiently personal and peculiar.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the complaint by the alderman, but reversed, in part, the dismissal of the competitor's complaint attacking the validity of the agreement. The court also reversed the trial court's dismissal on the issue of the competitor's standing to bring an action in quo warranto.

People v. Gore


No. 1-88-2969


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


212 Ill. App. 3d 984; 571 N.E.2d 1041; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 630; 157 Ill. Dec. 22



April 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Matthew J. Moran, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendant appealed his conviction on the ground that the second degree murder statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2 (1987), was unconstitutional because it impermissibly shifted the burden to him to prove mitigating factors so as to avoid a conviction for first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The state charged defendant with first degree murder. He claimed that he stabbed his victim in self-defense. Pursuant to para. 9-2, the state had the burden to prove beyond a reasonable doubt the elements of first degree murder. However, defendant had the burden to prove by a preponderance of the evidence one of the mitigating factors to reduce the first degree murder to second degree murder. Defendant contended that the burden shifting procedure of para. 9-2 violated the due process and equal protection guarantees of the United States Constitution and the Illinois Constitution's separation of powers mandate, Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 (1970). The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that (1) para. 9-2 did not violate the due process clause of the United States Constitution because the state was required to prove all of the elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt; (2) para. 9-2 did not violate equal protection principles because defendant was not a member of a suspect class, and the statutory scheme was rationally designed to meet a legitimate state purpose; and (3) para. 9-2 did not violate the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of first degree murder was affirmed.

Requena v. Franciscan Sisters Health Care Corp.


No. 3-89-0786


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


212 Ill. App. 3d 328; 570 N.E.2d 1214; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 634; 156 Ill. Dec. 492



April 17, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 22, 1991. As Corrected July 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County. No. 88-L-78. The Hon. Thomas Ewert, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff special administrator of an estate filed a medical negligence action against defendant physicians and hospital on behalf of the deceased. The Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) dismissed the complaint against the hospital and entered judgment upon a jury verdict in favor of the physicians. The administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court reversed and held that the trial court committed reversible error by permitting the decedent's last treating physician, who was not a defendant in the action, to testify after his ex parte communication with defense counsel. The communication jeopardized the strong policy of preserving the confidential and fiduciary relationship between a physician and patient and was improper. The court implied prejudice to the administrator from the facts and circumstances of the improper ex parte communication. The decedent's last treating physician violated his ethical and fiduciary obligation owed to the decedent. The ex parte communication between the last treating physician and defense counsel was without decedent's consent and concerned her treatment. The court prohibited the last treating physician from testifying at retrial because his testimony was tainted by the improper ex parte communication. In addition, the court held that the trial court erred by dismissing the claims against the hospital because a medical report attached to the complaint sufficiently complied with the requirements of Ill. Code Civ. P., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2 -- 622.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the administrator's complaint against the hospital and the judgment upon a jury verdict in favor of the physicians. The court remanded for a new trial with the instruction that the decedent's last treating physician was prohibited from testifying.

Fitchie v. Yurko


No. 2-90-0813


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


212 Ill. App. 3d 216; 570 N.E.2d 892; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 606; 156 Ill. Dec. 416



April 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 90-L-271. The Hon. James F. Quetsch, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lottery winner appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which held that plaintiffs, two acquaintances and a person who was present at a coffee shop, were entitled to equal shares of defendant's prize money on the legal theories of partnership and gift.


OVERVIEW: Over defendant's denials, plaintiffs testified that he had indicated to them that if they would help him scratch off the lottery tickets they would be his partners and would share in any winnings. On appeal, defendant asserted that the circuit court lacked the jurisdiction because the plaintiffs had not exhausted their administrative remedies. The court held that the purported sections of the Lottery Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 1157.3, 1163, 1169 (1989) were inapplicable and the Adopted Rules of the Illinois Lottery were at odds with defendant's position that plaintiffs had applicable administrative remedies. The court held that plaintiffs' pleading amendments had not prejudiced defendant by presenting a new theory of recovery, but had more accurately plead their original assertions. The court rejected defendant's contention that that the circuit court inconsistently awarded on the contradictory theories of both gift and partnership, and held that the circuit court found both theories as grounds for the plaintiffs' award. The court that the record evidence supported the circuit court's findings of an informal partnership, and the intention for a joint venture.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, holding that plaintiffs were entitled to equally share in defendant's prize money.

People v. Arman


No. 1-87-2705


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


215 Ill. App. 3d 687; 576 N.E.2d 11; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 592; 159 Ill. Dec. 342



April 10, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Christy S. Berkos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered a forfeiture order of certain real property and bank accounts belonging to defendant pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1655 of the Narcotics Profit Forfeiture Act (Act) after he was found guilty of narcotics racketeering.


OVERVIEW: After a jury found defendant guilty of narcotics racketeering, the prosecution filed a petition for forfeiture of certain real property and bank accounts of defendant pursuant to the Act. Following a hearing, the trial court entered a forfeiture order. Upon review of the forfeiture order, the court affirmed. The court held that the forfeiture order was properly entered against defendant where defendant was not entitled to a jury trial during the forfeiture proceeding because the proceeding was part of his sentencing rather than part of the trial. The court noted that forfeiture could only be ordered under the Act until after a conviction and that the conviction, not the forfeiture, was what determined felonious guilt. The court found the Act was not unconstitutional on the basis that it only required the prosecution to prove the forfeitability of his property by a mere preponderance of the evidence because forfeiture was simply a punishment of the crime. The court concluded evidence regarding defendant's financial activity after the dates charged in the indictment was properly admitted for the purpose of determining what property was maintained with racketeering derived funds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that entered a forfeiture order against defendant as to certain real property and bank accounts.

People v. Reyes

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which tried him as an adult and convicted him of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed a restaurant employee but was immediately apprehended by a passerby, and it was later determined that defendant had carried a gun on his person during the commission of the crime. Defendant was tried as an adult pursuant to the Juvenile Court Act of 1987 (the act), and he was convicted of armed robbery. Defendant alleged that the act was vague in regards to those charged with robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction holding that the act sufficiently apprised defendant that the carrying of the firearm during the commission of the robbery subjected him to trial as an adult. The court rejected defendant's claim that the statute was meant to only apply to those offenders who pointed a firearm during the robbery. The court also held that any error in the trial court's admission of a witness statement was harmless in light of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt. Finally, the court held that defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim was also without merit because he was not prejudiced by his counsel's failure to object to the erroneously admitted witness statement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which tried defendant as an adult and convicted him of armed robbery.

Holding Co. v. Department of Revenue


No. 1-90-0514


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


214 Ill. App. 3d 390; 574 N.E.2d 11; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 573; 158 Ill. Dec. 217



April 5, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Mary M. Conrad, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld the decision of defendant Illinois Department of Revenue (department) that assessed a tax deficiency against the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: In order to determine its taxable income in Illinois, the taxpayer, as a consolidated corporation, was required to include with its state income tax return a copy of its federal return. The department notified the taxpayer that its original state return could not be located and requested a copy of the original return with supporting documents. The taxpayer failed to provide the department with the requested documents. The department conducted an audit of the taxpayer and found a tax liability. It issued a notice of deficiency to the taxpayer. The taxpayer protested, but the department upheld the tax deficiency and the administrative law judge and trial court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The taxpayer was required to use the form prescribed for filing an original return. The taxpayer attempted to bypass the filing provisions and negate its state tax liability by the belated filing of an amended return after its loss for another year had been sustained. It knowingly tried to combine two separate tax actions in a single form. Because it did not file an original return and did not pay the taxes owed, the taxpayer could not use a loss carryback to reduce its liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the assessment of a deficiency against the taxpayer.

Cato v. Attar


No. 2-90-1058


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


210 Ill. App. 3d 996; 569 N.E.2d 1111; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 455; 155 Ill. Dec. 500



March 27, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 29, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Jack Hoogasian, Judge, presiding. No. 90-L-386



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which denied her motion for leave to amend and dismissed her complaint against defendant doctor seeking damages for medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed suit against the doctor alleging medical malpractice. The doctor filed a motion to dismiss the patient's complaint on the ground that the patient failed to attach an affidavit or written report to her complaint as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1989). The circuit court denied the patient's motion to amend and dismissed her complaint with prejudice. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the circuit court abused its discretion in not allowing the patient to amend her pleadings. The court held that there was no indication of bad faith or an intent to frustrate justice by the patient and there was no discernable prejudice to the doctor if the court would have either allowed amendment or dismissed the complaint without prejudice. The court noted that the patient presented current Illinois case law supporting the lack of compliance with § 2-622 and attempted to cure the defect in her pleadings within 10 days of becoming aware of the requirements. The court reasoned that under the circumstances, the patient should have been allowed to amend because medical malpractice cases were to be determined on the merits when at all possible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the patient's motion to amend and dismissing her complaint against the doctor seeking damages for medical malpractice. The court remanded the cause to the circuit court.

People v. Strawn


No. 4-90-0667


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


210 Ill. App. 3d 783; 569 N.E.2d 269; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 418; 155 Ill. Dec. 269



March 21, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 18, 1991. As Corrected April 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. William D. DeCardy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) convicting her of operating a vehicle with tinted front side windows in violation of § 12-503(a) of the Illinois Vehicle Code (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 12-503(a) (1989), and placing her on court supervision for six months and ordering her to pay court costs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was ticketed for driving an Illinois-registered vehicle with tinted front windows in violation of § 12-503(a). Defendant filed pre-trial motions challenging the constitutionality of the statute, which were denied by the trial court. The trial court found defendant guilty. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 12-503 did not violate defendant's right against unreasonable searches and seizures because the police had a right to stop a vehicle for safety violations. Further, the statute did not violate her constitutional right to privacy because defendant clearly violated the Code, which was the proper basis for a Terry stop. The statute also was not an impermissible burden on interstate commerce. Section § 12-503 had a legitimate purpose in protecting police officers as they approached stopped vehicles and allowed officers to easily identify and observe drivers. Additionally, any impact on interstate commerce was incidental and was not an excessive burden. The court found that the statute was neither unreasonable nor arbitrary and rejected defendant's arguments that it violated her due process rights and the equal protection clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for operation a vehicle with tinted windows in violation of the Code.

People v. McGee


No. 1-89-0905


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


211 Ill. App. 3d 641; 570 N.E.2d 578; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 398; 156 Ill. Dec. 102



March 21, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gino L. DiVito, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, and Vacated in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of possessing a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the state expressed concern as to whether trial counsel's representation of defendant was a conflict of interest because counsel had testified in a co-defendant's trial. Trial counsel was permitted to represent defendant, but a second attorney was not permitted to represent defendant. Defendant argued, inter alia, that his conviction was improper because the trial court refused to permit defendant to be represented by retained counsel of his choice. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. Defendant's constitutional right to assistance of counsel included the right to be represented by counsel of his choice. However, defendant repeatedly told the trial court that he wanted his trial counsel to represent him and never stated that he wanted the second attorney to represent him. Therefore, he was not denied his right to retained counsel of his choice. Defendant's sentence was vacated because the trial court improperly relied on evidence of a pending charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possessing a controlled substance with intent to deliver, and it vacated and remanded the sentence.

Pundy v. Department of Professional Regulation


Nos. 1-89-1702, 1-89-3296 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


211 Ill. App. 3d 475; 570 N.E.2d 458; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 375; 155 Ill. Dec. 945



March 15, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 29, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff psychiatrist appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Plaintiff, whose medical license was suspended, filed an interlocutory appeal in which he challenged § 41 of the Medical Practice Act of 1987, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, par. 4400-41 (1987), which prohibited the issuance of a stay of sanctions while judicial proceedings were pending. Plaintiff also appealed the affirmance of his license suspension.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff psychiatrist had a sexual relationship with a woman who was his patient and his employee. Defendant, the Illinois Department of Professional Regulation, found that plaintiff was guilty of unprofessional conduct likely to harm the public. Plaintiff's license was suspended for six months, followed by a two-year probationary period. The trial court refused to stay the decision pending judicial review and subsequently upheld defendant's decision. The court affirmed. Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4400-41 (1987), which prohibited a stay of defendant's decision, was not unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff and his patients. Doctors who were sanctioned presented a significant risk to the public, and the legislature could properly allocate the risk of error to the doctor as opposed to the public. The record supported the finding that plaintiff's conduct was unprofessional and likely to harm the public. Plaintiff's patient was emotionally unstable and unable to handle her work situation when she first consulted with plaintiff; plaintiff acted in his own interest, not in the interest of his patient, when he entered into a sexual relationship with her.


OUTCOME: A decision by defendant, the Illinois Department of Professional Regulation, that plaintiff psychiatrist was guilty of unprofessional conduct by virtue of his sexual relationship with a patient who was also his employee was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The statutory prohibition against a stay of sanctions while judicial proceedings were pending was constitutional as applied to plaintiff and his patients.

People v. Rainge


No. 1-87-0951


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


211 Ill. App. 3d 432; 570 N.E.2d 431; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 358; 155 Ill. Dec. 918



March 14, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 2, 1991. As Corrected May 5, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Frank W. Meekins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered a judgment of conviction after a jury trial for the offenses of murder, rape, and aggravated kidnapping. Defendant claimed he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, that he was denied due process, that the prosecutor misrepresented the evidence and its burden of proof, and that his sentence exceeded the statutory guidelines.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his convictions for murder, rape, and aggravated kidnapping. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court as modified. The court held that the trial court did not err when it determined that the mental incapacities of a state witness could be given due weight by the jury hearing her testimony. The court ruled that defendant had no right to participate in a preliminary examination of the witness in an effort to discredit her competency. The court held that the prosecutor's comments were not improper, that the testimony of various family members of the victim was simply incidental to the admission of proper evidence and not presented in a manner calculated to mislead the jury, and that defendant was not denied effective representation of counsel. The court found that defendant failed to establish a prima facie case of discrimination in support of his Batson challenge, and that defendant was properly sentenced under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, § 122-1 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that defendant's sentence be reduced to the statutory maximum for the offense of aggravated kidnapping. In all other respects, the court affirmed the order of the trial court that entered judgments of conviction for murder, rape, and aggravated kidnapping.

Dobrydnia v. Indiana Group, Inc.


No. 3-90-0445


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


209 Ill. App. 3d 1038; 568 N.E.2d 1002; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 384; 154 Ill. Dec. 781



March 12, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication April 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. Louis J. Perona, Judge, presiding. No. 89-L-310



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the husband employee and his wife, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which granted defendant insurance company's motion to dismiss the wife's loss of consortium claim because her recovery was barred by § 5 of the Workers' Compensation Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.5(a)(1989). The wife asserted the act did not bar her claim.


OVERVIEW: The husband was injured while employed at an elementary school and brought an action to recover damages based on the alleged negligence of the insurance company to adequately inspect a boiler, its appurtenances, and accompanying equipment. The insurance company was the insurer for the school district. The wife filed an action for loss of consortium. The trial court granted the insurance company's motion to dismiss the wife's claim and the wife appealed. The court affirmed and held that § 5(a) barred the wife's cause of action for loss of consortium because the language of the statute clearly barred her claim. The court stated that while the wife's loss of consortium claim may have been an independent claim for damages, it arose out of the husband employee's injury. The court disagreed with the wife that she was not a person "wholly or partially dependent" upon her husband, as appeared in the language of the statute, and found that a spouse, whether or not dependent, received benefits directly or indirectly under the act. Finally, the court stated that § 5(a), as previously construed by an Illinois court, prohibited recovery for loss of consortium claims against an employer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the insurance company and against the wife for her loss of consortium claim.

 

1125 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


McKeown v. Homoya


No. 5-90-0347


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


209 Ill. App. 3d 959; 568 N.E.2d 528; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 378; 154 Ill. Dec. 528



March 11, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County; the Hon. C. David Nelson, Judge, presiding. No. 89-L-14



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor filed an action in the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois) against defendant bar owner after her father became intoxicated at the bar owner's establishment and was killed in an automobile accident. The trial court dismissed the complaint, holding that Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 43, par. 135 (the Dramshop Act) did not provide a common law action of negligence for loss of support. The minor appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contended on appeal that the Dramshop Act unconstitutionally denied her an available remedy by excluding any relief for loss of support and that a common law cause of action should have been recognized under the circumstances of a tavern selling large quantities of alcohol to an intoxicated individual after requesting him to leave the premises because of his intoxication. The court held that the Dramshop Act provided the exclusive remedy in Illinois against tavern owners and operators for injuries caused by an intoxicated person or in consequence of intoxication, there being no common law liability for the negligent sale or supply of liquor in the state and that any extension of liability for the sale or supply of liquor beyond the historical limits of the Dramshop Act was a function of the legislature, not of the courts. The court further held that there was no common law cause of action based upon the willful and wanton misconduct by a tavern owner in connection with the sale or supply of alcohol, no matter how egregious the underlying facts of the cause of action were.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the minor's complaint for failure to state a cause of action for which relief could be granted.

Boonstra v. Chicago


No. 1-89-2759


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


214 Ill. App. 3d 379; 574 N.E.2d 689; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 295; 158 Ill. Dec. 576



March 6, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 12, 1991. Released for Publication July 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Frank M. Siracusa, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate administrator challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellee city's motion to dismiss in the administrator's action to recover estate property allegedly taken unconstitutionally by the city. Decedent's taxicab operator's license, formerly assignable, was taken by the city after decedent's death upon the passing of a city ordinance making all operators' licenses non-assignable.


OVERVIEW: Decedent when alive had a taxicab operator's license at a time the city's ordinances made such licenses assignable and even devisable for only a minor fee; the licenses themselves had a market value up to $ 27,000. An ordinance was passed making the licenses nonassignable, and two days after decedent's passing; city representative took his license. Six years later, after several unfavorable federal court rulings, an amended ordinance made the licenses assignable once more. But when appellant estate administrator sought to recover the license, the trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss on the grounds that the license was not "property," and even it was, the city had the power to amend the nature of that property right. On review, the court held that even though the property right was created by legislative action, once created it could not be taken away without due process and just compensation even by statutory amendment. Undoubtedly, the license was constitutionally protected property; it could be owned, marketed, and transferred. The administrator had stated a viable cause of action. The statute of limitations defense, not argued until the appeal, was deemed waived.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that granted the city's motion to dismiss because the estate administrator had stated a viable cause of action because decedent's taxicab operator's license was constitutionally protected property that could not be taken by the city without due process and just compensation. The statute of limitations defense was deemed waived and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

American Nat'l Bank & Trust Co. v. Anchor Organization for Health Maintenance


No. 1-90-0780


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


210 Ill. App. 3d 418; 569 N.E.2d 128; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 282; 155 Ill. Dec. 128



March 1, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Odas Nicholson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, guardian and parents, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant health organization's motion to dismiss plaintiffs' medical malpractice action pursuant to § 26 of the Voluntary Health Services Plans Act (VHSPA), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 32, para. 620 (1987).


OVERVIEW: The guardian represented a minor that suffered a brain injury when defendant doctor used forceps during the minor's birth. The trial court granted the health organization's motion to dismiss, finding that it was immune pursuant to § 26 of the VHSPA. The appellate court reversed. The court found that the 1988 amendment to § 26, eliminating the health organization's statutory immunity, was not applicable because it applied prospectively and the cause of action accrued prior to the amendment. The court held that the legislature had a rational basis for immunizing voluntary health services plans like the health organization under § 26. However, the health organization was acting in a dual capacity as a health maintenance organization (HMO) and a voluntary health services plan when the minor was injured. The court concluded that it would be unconstitutional to apply § 26 of the VHSPA to the health organization because it was acting also as an HMO, and it was not eligible to take advantage of the immunity that its charter with the VHSPA allowed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the health organization from the cause of action and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

1129 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tripp


No. 5-90-0175


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


208 Ill. App. 3d 1006; 567 N.E.2d 769; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 267; 153 Ill. Dec. 811



February 26, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County; the Hon. Loren P. Lewis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction and sentence by the Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois) for armed violence predicated on theft of a motor vehicle and theft of a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: On defendant's motion to dismiss, the trial court initially dismissed the charges of armed violence predicated on theft of a motor vehicle and theft of a motor vehicle. The trial court reasoned that § 4-103(a)(1) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103(a)(1) (1987), was unconstitutional. The supreme court vacated the trial court's judgment on the grounds that the statute was constitutional. On remand, defendant claimed that her conviction under the statute violated the Double Jeopardy Clause. The court affirmed the convictions because there was no violation of double jeopardy. The court reasoned that the trial court's initial dismissal of the charge was not a decision based on the merits but was instead a dismissal unrelated to guilt or innocence. Therefore, defendant was neither convicted nor acquitted and double jeopardy did not bar the prosecution. Also, the convictions did not violate double jeopardy because the judgment on the charge of armed violence was proper based upon defendant's conviction for theft of a motor vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for armed violence predicated on theft of a motor vehicle and theft of a motor vehicle.

Gilmore v. County of Du Page


No. 2-90-0589


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


209 Ill. App. 3d 66; 567 N.E.2d 1111; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 253; 153 Ill. Dec. 884



February 22, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication March 25, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John W. Darrah, Judge, presiding. No. 89-MR-0019



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which affirmed a determination by defendant county's zoning board that the use of part of the property owners' home as a dentist's office violated a zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The property owners purchased a home and converted a part of it that had been used as a chiropractor's office into a dentist's office. The county's zoning board concluded that the use of the property for a dental office constituted an illegal change of use under Du Page County, Ill., Zoning Ordinance § 37-5.2-8(c). The trial court affirmed the board's determination. The issue on appeal was whether the board erred in holding that the conversion from a chiropractor's office to a dentist's office was a prohibited change from one nonconforming use to another and not the continuation of a lawful prior nonconforming use. The court affirmed the judgment against the property owners. The court concluded that the board's strict construction of the zoning ordinance to require identity of use rather than similarity was not clearly erroneous, arbitrary, or unreasonable. The court also concluded that the zoning ordinance was not unconstitutional as applied to the property in question because the restriction on changes from one nonconforming use to another was rationally related to bringing the neighborhood into conformity with a valid exercise of the county's zoning power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the property owners that affirmed the determination by the county's zoning board that the use of part of their home as a dentist's office violated a zoning ordinance.

Garland v. Kauten


No. 4-90-0433


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


209 Ill. App. 3d 30; 567 N.E.2d 707; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 240; 153 Ill. Dec. 749



February 21, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 21, 1991. As Corrected March 15, 1991. Petition for leave to Appeal Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Richard J. Cadagin, Judge, presiding. No. 89L133



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted the motions of defendant health professionals to dismiss that were filed pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1989) and denied the patient's motion to vacate and reconsider in the patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: After the patient brought a medical malpractice action against the health professionals, the health professionals filed a motion to dismiss. The trial court dismissed the patient's action with prejudice and denied the patient's motion to vacate and reconsider. On appeal, the patient contended that Ill. Rev. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court dismissal of the patient's medical malpractice action that was brought against the health professionals.

People v. Krueger


No. 2-89-1207


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


208 Ill. App. 3d 897; 567 N.E.2d 717; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 242; 153 Ill. Dec. 759



February 21, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication March 19, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 19, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Peter J. Dockery, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County, Illinois, which denied his petition for recission of the summary suspension of his driver's license, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2-118.1, based on his arrest for driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's parents went away for vacation and asked their neighbor to watch the house, but asked nothing else of her. Hearing knocking on a window, the neighbor investigated and found police officers, who told her that defendant had been in a car accident and that they needed to talk to him. The officers eventually convinced the neighbor to let them into the house. defendant cooperated, but failed field sobriety tests. An hour and 35 minutes, defendant failed a breath test. The trial court denied defendant's petition for recission the summary suspension of his driver's license, but the court reversed and remanded. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2-118.1 (1989) required a valid arrest in order to suspend a driver's license. The court found that this construction was preferable to abuses contemplated by driver's licenses being suspended under invalid arrests or unconstitutional police activity. The court held that the exclusionary rule could be applied to this civil proceeding. The court found that the state did not meet its heavy burden of proving exigent circumstances to justify the "emergency exception" to the warrantless arrest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the denial of defendant's petition for recission of the summary suspension of his driver's license after police arrested him in his home without a warrant and without exigent circumstances to justify their presence.

Chicago v. Department of Revenue


No. 1-89-3060


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


210 Ill. App. 3d 273; 569 N.E.2d 65; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 223; 155 Ill. Dec. 65



February 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Mary M. Conrad, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed a portion of the ruling of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the denial by defendant, the Department of Revenue, of real estate tax exemption claimed for four contiguous parcels of land. The Department appealed that portion of the circuit court's ruling that overruled its decision that two buildings located on the land were likewise not entitled to tax exemption.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the acquisition of all of a sublessor's rights, title, and interest in two buildings, which were used solely for municipal purposes, the city became sublessee of the land owned by the lessor and responsible for property taxes. The city sought to have the land and the buildings exempted from property taxes, asserting that the property was owned by a unit of local government and was entitled to exemption under § 19.6 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 500, 500.6 (1987) because it produced no income. However, the Department argued that, despite municipality ownership of the buildings, the land and the buildings could not be severed for tax status purposes. In affirming the judgment, the court found that any ruling that exempted the city leased land from taxation violated Ill. Const. art. IX, § 6, which expressly limited the legislature's powers of tax exemption to city owned. Thus, city leased property could not be exempt from taxation. However, because the city did own the buildings and because the severance of property interests for exemption purposes was allowed, the circuit court properly accorded the buildings tax-exempt status.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Illinois Power Co. v. Illinois Commerce Comm'n


Nos. 3-89-0282, 3-89-0297, 3-89-0318 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


208 Ill. App. 3d 779; 566 N.E.2d 1372; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 191; 153 Ill. Dec. 266



February 8, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication March 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for review of order of Illinois Commerce Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a company, Illinois Attorney General, an agency, and a board, sought review of an order by appellee Illinois Commerce Commission (commission), which determined that only 27.2 percent of the nuclear power electrical generation station was used and useful and that the deferred assets account balance was to be reduced by $ 101,644,000.


OVERVIEW: The company and the attorney general challenged the commission's determination that only 27.2 percent of the station was used and useful for purposes of inclusion in the company's rate base. The company contended that the commission's decision to reduce, for ratemaking purposes, the deferred assets account balance was wrong as a matter of law. After review of cases and commission decisions, and the provision in the last paragraph of § 9 -- 215 of the amended Public Utilities Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 9 -- 215 (1989), the court held that the commission erred in using the needed and economic benefits tests to determine whether and what portion of the station was used and useful for purposes of inclusion in the company's rate base. The court reversed the commission's decision on the used and useful issue because the determination was to be based on established pre-1986 standards. The court reversed the commission's determination that the deferred assets account balance must have been reduced because the court found that the commission misapplied the Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 92. In all other respects, the court affirmed the commission's order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the portion of the order for further proceedings on the issue of whether and/or what portion of the station was used and useful. In addition, the court reversed the commission's decision to reduce, for ratemaking purposes, the deferred assets account balance by $ 101,644,000. In all other respects, the court affirmed the commission's order.

In re Marriage of Vest


No. 5-89-0467


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


208 Ill. App. 3d 325; 567 N.E.2d 47; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 217; 153 Ill. Dec. 332



February 8, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Jan Fiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent husband appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which allowed petitioner wife's petition for disposition of property seeking a portion of the husband's military pension pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 510.1 (1987), awarded the wife one-half of the husband's pension and $ 1,000 toward her attorney fees, and granted the wife's motion for attorney fees on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The wife filed a petition for disposition of property, seeking a portion of the husband's military pension. The trial court allowed the petition pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 510.1 (1987), and awarded the wife one-half of the husband's pension and $ 1,000 toward her attorney fees. After the husband filed notice of appeal, the trial court granted the wife's motion for attorney fees on appeal. The husband appealed, contending that the trial court erred in finding that he had failed to prove the affirmative defense set forth in Ill. Rev. Although no division of the husband's military retirement pension was made in a settlement agreement or judgment of dissolution, the original disposition of military retirement benefits was part of a carefully derived plan that was fair to both parties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's allowance of the wife's petition for disposition of property and affirmed the trial court's awards of attorney fees to the wife in the wife's action for disposition of property.
