People v. Steffens


No. 4-90-0291


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


208 Ill. App. 3d 252; 566 N.E.2d 985; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 157; 153 Ill. Dec. 135



February 7, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication March 11, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. Luther H. Dearborn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of possession of a rosette rivet which had not yet been attached to, or which had been removed from, its original vehicle, in violation of § 4 -- 103(a)(5) of the Illinois Vehicle Code (code section), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4 -- 103(a)(5) (1989), and imposed sentence of two years' conditional discharge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offered rose-headed rivets for sale at a vendor booth in an auto show. He sold rivets to a state police officer at the show. The court held that: (1) the code section was not void for vagueness because a "rosette rivet," as used in the section, was the rose-headed rivet used to fasten manufacturer identification plates to motor vehicles; (2) there was no violation of either the due process or proportionate penalty clauses of the state constitution in the penalty provision of the code section that prohibited possession of the rosette rivet by unauthorized persons; (3) the code section did not violate the equal protection clause of the state constitution because the classification of the code as to the possession of rivets was relevant to a valid state purpose that sought the curtailment of theft and resale; and (4) a proper foundation was laid for the officer as an expert witness who had been employed by the state police for over 20 years, had received special training and refresher courses, was taken to a vehicle manufacturing plant, and had seen over 10,000 rivets.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

People v. Stefan


No. 2-89-0789


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


208 Ill. App. 3d 205; 567 N.E.2d 18; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 143; 153 Ill. Dec. 303



February 5, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication March 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Richard A. Lucas, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss the counts of his indictment, which charged defendant with criminal and reckless disposal of hazardous waste.


OVERVIEW: The indictment stemmed from charges that defendant discharged toxic waste into a public sewer system. A prior indictment based upon the same incidents was nolprossed. Defendant contended that the counts were barred by prior prosecutions based on double jeopardy because the elements of the offenses were identical. The court held that the original offense, violation of Addison Village, Ill. Code § 23.13, and the offenses charged in the case at bar, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, paras. 1044(c)(1), (e)(1), were sufficiently different to make them separate offenses. Ch. 111 1/2, paras. 1044(c)(1), (e)(1) required proof of a knowing disposal and delivery of hazardous waste, whereas the village ordinance required no such proof as to mental state and was an absolute liability offense. Also, the village's ordinance was regulatory, not penal and the ordinance required proof of a fact that the statute did not. Therefore, under the Jackson test, the court found that the pertinent ordinance and statute dealt with separate offenses and defendant's prosecution was not barred by the prohibition against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss two counts of the indictment.

January 30, 1991, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant businesses sought a declaration that South Holland, Ill., Code art. I, ch. 9, §§ 9-3(a) to (e) was arbitrary, capricious and unreasonable. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found in favor of appellees, the village and some of its officials. The trial court also granted the village judgments on the pleadings in its quasi-criminal complaints against the businesses for violating the Sunday blue laws. The businesses appealed.


OVERVIEW: The consolidated appeals were in regard to the village's enforcement of an ordinance that prohibited certain business activities on Sundays. The businesses argued that the ordinance was arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable, that the language of the ordinance was vague, that it was an unauthorized use of police power because it barred some commercial activities that did not necessarily disturb Sunday worship. The village argued that the exemptions to the ordinance were reasonable and that it was reasonable to distinguish among manufacturing, retail, and construction businesses. The court found 1) that the ordinance was not vague as to whether the rental of videocassettes and the sale of truck washes were permitted on Sundays, as it was clear that those activities were prohibited; 2) that the ordinance was not an unauthorized delegation of legislative authority to the executive branch; 3) that the ordinance had a rational relationship to the objective of promoting peace and quiet and that the businesses did not demonstrated an equal protection violation; and 4) that the ordinance did not have an irrational number of exemptions and was a reasonable exercise of police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment with the exception of the order granting the village's motion for judgment on the pleadings in regard to some of the quasi criminal complaints.

People v. Rogers


No. 3-89-0716


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


208 Ill. App. 3d 808; 566 N.E.2d 782; 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 37; 152 Ill. Dec. 905



January 10, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication March 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. John A. Gorman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to armed violence under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A -- 2 (1989) and was sentenced to an eight-year term of imprisonment. No direct appeal was taken from the guilty plea or sentence, but defendant filed a post-conviction petition, claiming that the conviction was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois) dismissed the petition as frivolous, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with criminal damage to property under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 21 -- 1 and armed violence based upon criminal damage to property, after he fired six shots into a hotel room door. Defendant pled guilty to armed violence, and the State dropped the charge of criminal damage to property. Defendant claimed that his conviction was void because the offense of armed violence could not be predicated constitutionally on the offense of criminal damage to property. In affirming the judgment that dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, the court rejected defendant's argument and ruled that: (1) the crime of criminal damage to property had already been found to be a proper predicate felony for an armed violence conviction and cases from the Illinois Supreme Court that indicated otherwise were distinguishable and inapplicable because defendant's conduct was premeditated and voluntary and the deterrent purpose of the armed violence statute was served; (2) the legislature was not precluded from punishing more severely someone who damaged property while carrying a dangerous weapon, and the statutory scheme producing that result was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

In re Estate of Brown


No. 4-89-0393


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


207 Ill. App. 3d 139; 565 N.E.2d 312; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1960; 152 Ill. Dec. 70



December 31, 1990, Filed

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Warren A. Sappington, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which found for petitioners, maternal grandfather and his wife (grandparents). The mother argued that the guardianship provision in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 11-7 (1987) was unconstitutional, that the grandparents lacked standing, and that the appointment of the grandparents as co-guardians of her minor child was against the weight of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: The mother entered a rehabilitation program for substance abuse following the birth of her minor child. She arranged for the grandparents to assume care, control, and custody of the child. The mother moved in with the grandparents on her release, but left without notice, establishing contact sporadically. The grandparents filed a petition for guardianship over the minor child. The circuit court awarded custody to the grandparents and visitation rights to the mother. On the mother's motion for reconsideration, the circuit court appointed the grandparents as co-guardians. The mother appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that the mother's equal protection challenge under § 11-7 was not persuasive. Section 11-7 embodied the superior rights doctrine. The child was removed from the mother on a showing that she was not fit. The mother was accorded a full evidentiary hearing. The argument that the grandparents lacked standing was waived, but the court found that standing existed because the grandparents had standing to commence the guardianship action. The guardianship appointment was not against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court awarding co-guardianship of the mother's minor child to the grandparents.

People v. Fudge


No. 1-88-0807


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


208 Ill. App. 3d 611; 567 N.E.2d 535; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1981; 153 Ill. Dec. 577



December 31, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Fred G. Suria, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) following a bench trial after which he was found guilty of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and sentenced to serve five years' imprisonment. On appeal, defendant argued that his conviction had to be vacated because the possession of stolen motor vehicle statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103(a)(1), violated due process and the guarantee of proportionate penalties.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal that the possession of a stolen motor vehicle statute was unconstitutional because it did not use a reasonable method to further or protect the state interest for which it was enacted. Defendant further contended that the offense was a lesser-included offense of theft, and, therefore, imposition of a greater penalty violated the Illinois Constitutional requirement of proportionate penalties. The court disagreed. The court noted that the Illinois Supreme Court had held that the statute did not violate the due process and proportionate penalty clauses of the Illinois Constitution and that the statute applied to all persons, including organized motor vehicle thieves. The court noted that the Illinois Supreme Court had concluded that all persons who possessed a stolen motor vehicle, including organized motor vehicle thieves, were punishable under the statute and that the steady increase in the penalty provision for possession of a stolen motor vehicle was indicative of the legislature's intent to make possession of a stolen motor vehicle a separate, more serious offense than theft, rather than a lesser included offense of theft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

People v. Weber


No. 1-90-1113


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


208 Ill. App. 3d 509; 567 N.E.2d 413; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1953; 153 Ill. Dec. 455



December 28, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Lester D. McCurrie, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of child pornography under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20.1(a)(2) (1985), and sentenced defendant to 13 months' conditional discharge after a police raid at defendant's home uncovered a book with pornographic pictures of minors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for child pornography under the amended child pornography statute which made it illegal to merely possess child pornography, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20.1(a)(2) (1985), where under the former statute possession had to be with intent to disseminate the child pornography. Defendant appealed his conviction arguing that there was insufficient evidence to prove that he possessed a book containing child pornography with the intent to disseminate it, and that as he was indicted under the amended child pornography statute providing it was illegal to possess child pornography, application of the amended statute was a violation of ex post facto law. Despite defendant's argument that application of the amended statute constituted an ex post fact violation, the court affirmed defendant's conviction because although defendant's possession of the child pornography occurred before the amendment to the statute, defendant violated the statute by his continued possession of the book. The court found that defendant's conviction was not an unconstitutional ex post facto violation, and that defendant could not claim ignorance of the amended law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions under the amended statute prohibiting possession of child pornography.

People v. McCleary


No. 1-88-0203


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


208 Ill. App. 3d 466; 567 N.E.2d 434; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1974; 153 Ill. Dec. 476



December 28, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Kenneth Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty but mentally ill (GBMI) of murdering two people. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to mandatory life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court addressed numerous contentions raised on appeal by defendant. The court agreed with defendant's primary contention that the trial court improperly instructed the jury regarding the burden of proof for a finding of GBMI. Accordingly, the court reversed defendant's conviction, and remanded the matter for a new trial. The court reasoned that the trial court mistakenly instructed the jury that the preponderance of the evidence standard, rather than the reasonable doubt standard, applied in determining defendant's sanity. The court noted that the GBMI verdict required the state to prove three elements beyond a reasonable doubt: that defendant committed the act, that defendant was not insane, and that defendant was mentally ill. The state conceded that the instruction given by the trial court misstated the burden of proof, but argued that the error was harmless because defendant would have been found GBMI even with the proper instruction. The court held that the error was not harmless because the altered GBMI instruction might have affected the outcome of the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's two murder convictions and remanded the matter for a new trial.

North Park Public Water Dist. v. Machesney Park


No. 2-90-0485


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


216 Ill. App. 3d 936; 576 N.E.2d 849; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1883; 159 Ill. Dec. 926



December 18, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication September 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 89-Mr-0095; Hon. Alford R. Penniman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant local water district challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which granted appellee city a summary judgment in the district's action for declaratory judgment and damages. The trial court held that the city's mandate that the district move its water lines at its own cost was not an illegal taking of its easement under the Water District Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 188 et seq. (1989).


OVERVIEW: When the city began road improvements it became necessary for the local water district to move its water mains. When the city refused to reimburse the district for its expenses, the district argued that the easement for the pipes granted under § 9 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 196 (1989), was a protected property right and that the city's failure to pay was an illegal taking of that property without compensation. The trial court did not agree and granted the city a summary judgment. On review the court held that any franchise rights granted to the district by the city or by the city as an agent of the state were given subject to the inherent police powers of the state as the sovereign. It held that a city could not lawfully grant any rights or privileges which were inconsistent with the public necessities or surrender its rights to control the public streets. Because the utility's rights under the franchise ordinance were taken subject to the city's police power, the city's subsequent exercise of that power in improving the roads did not constitute an unconstitutional taking of the district's property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the city in the water district's action for declaratory judgment and damages under the Water District Act.

 

1147 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


American Nat'l Bank & Trust Co. v. Chicago


Nos. 1-88-3369, 1-89-0002 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


209 Ill. App. 3d 96; 568 N.E.2d 25; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1884; 154 Ill. Dec. 25



December 18, 1990  
December 18, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. David J. Shields, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff building owner appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed some of the building owner's claims and entered a judgment in favor of defendant city on the building owner's other claims. The building owner claimed that the city violated his due process rights by amending the zoning ordinance to allow intervenor neighbor to build a new building.


OVERVIEW: A building owner's building was adjacent to the proposed building site of a neighbor, and the neighbor's new building would block the building owner's view of the city and damage its heating and cooling system. The city approved an amendment to the zoning ordinance to allow the new building. The court found that (1) the plan commission complied with the guidelines despite the fact that its report did not discuss or refer to the guidelines and despite the fact that the planning commissioner drafted the report before the hearing, (2) the city substantially complied with the required procedures where the building owner's objections were heard at the hearing, (3) the building owner received adequate notice of the hearing and had ample opportunity to object, (4) the trial court did not err in refusing to allow depositions of the commissioners, (5) the rezoning amendment was not arbitrary and capricious where the new building would provide a substantial benefit, (6) the trial court did not err in excluding experimental evidence where the expert described the potential odor, and (7) there was no legal right to the free flow of light and air from adjoining land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the building owner's claims.

 

1148 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dean


No. 1-89-0882


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


207 Ill. App. 3d 640; 566 N.E.2d 340; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1879; 152 Ill. Dec. 653



December 14, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John W. Crilly, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgement Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of unlawful use of weapons and sentenced him to one year's probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of use of weapons and sentenced to one year of probation. On appeal, defendant contended that he was denied equal protection of laws under the weapons statute an that the state failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the trier of fact was not required to accept defendant's exculpatory testimony but had to consider the evidence as a whole, weighing all the circumstances of the incident in assessing the possibility of the accused's version of events. In this case, defendant was unable to persuade the court that the circuit court erred in its assessment of the evidence. Therefore, the court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which convicted defendant of unlawful use of weapons and sentenced him to a year of probation.

 

1149 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Greeson v. Mackinaw Township


No. 3-90-0248


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


207 Ill. App. 3d 193; 565 N.E.2d 695; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1873; 152 Ill. Dec. 162



December 13, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication January 30, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; No. 88L185; the Hon. Bruce W. Black and the Hon. John A. Gorman, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver appealed the decision of the Circuit Court, Tazewell County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to defendant township and dismissed the complaint against defendants, township highway commissioner, county, and county superintendent of highways, based on the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, in plaintiff's action for damages resulting from an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: The driver was injured when her car overturned on an S curve on a road owned by the township and located in the county. The driver filed a complaint and alleged that defendants knew or should have known of the unreasonably dangerous condition of the road and that they negligently and carelessly failed to warn the motorists of the condition. The trial court granted summary judgment for the township and dismissed the complaint against the remaining defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed the summary judgment and dismissal of the complaint. The court held that the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 2-201 (1987), which provided immunity to a public employee for acts or omissions within the exercise of his discretion, protected the township highway commissioner and the county superintendent of highways from liability to the driver because the placement of the warning sign before the curve was an exercise of their discretion. Because the individual employees were not liable, the court held that the township and the county could not be held liable under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 2-109 (1987).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for the township and the dismissal of the complaint as to the township highway commissioner, the county, and the county superintendent of highways.

 

1150 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tolliver


No. 5-88-0585


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


205 Ill. App. 3d 711; 563 N.E.2d 1242; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1854; 151 Ill. Dec. 136



December 6, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County; the Hon. Dennis M. Huber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a conviction and sentence entered in the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Illinois). He had been convicted of possession of a car title without a complete assignment, in violation of § 4-104(b)(1), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 4-104(b) (1987), which was a Class 4 felony. His pretrial motion to dismiss on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold a used car to another man. The title did not have his name on it, and he refused to put his name on it or refund the buyer's money. Defendant was charged with violating § 4-104(b). The face of the title did not define or explain a complete assignment, and it did not include any warning that the failure to assign the title to a specific person was a violation of the law. The trial judge noted that while it was not clear on the face of the title what a person's obligation was, there was no valid reason for not completing it. On appeal, defendant challenged the statute's constitutionality, asserting first that the offense of violating § 4-104(b) was punished more harshly than other similar or related offenses requiring a greater degree of culpability. The court rejected the argument that the sentencing scheme violated the state constitution's proportional penalties clause. Defendant also argued that the statute was overly broad. The court agreed that, because the statute required no criminal intent, it punished innocent conduct. The breadth of the statute was far greater than needed to achieve the underlying purpose of the statute, to prevent auto theft.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

1151 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jerome


No. 2-89-0002


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


206 Ill. App. 3d 428; 564 N.E.2d 221; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1839; 151 Ill. Dec. 244



December 6, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication January 7, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John E. Sype, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his first-degree murder conviction under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1(a) and his sentence for 22 years' imprisonment by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois). Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on self-defense and second-degree murder and also alleged that the second-degree murder statute in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--2(a) (1987) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was an unregistered guest at a hotel where the victim worked as a clerk, was being led out of the hotel when he admitted to stabbing the victim in the back. The victim died as a result of the stabbing, but identified defendant as the perpetrator before he died. Defendant alleged that the victim was shoving him down the stairs and also had told other persons that he was a homosexual. The trial court refused to give to the jury defendant's jury instructions for self-defense and second-degree murder. The court affirmed defendant's sentence and conviction for first-degree murder. The court held that the proposed jury instructions were not appropriate because defendant presented very little evidence that the victim threatened him with unlawful force and because defendant did not allege that he believed he was in imminent danger of death or great bodily harm sufficient to justify his use of a knife on the victim. The court also held that the second-degree murder statute in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--2(a) did not violate a defendant's constitutional rights because requiring a defendant to prove a mitigating factor did not violate a defendant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for first-degree murder and his sentence for 22 years' imprisonment.

Worth v. Hahn


No. 1-88-3025


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


206 Ill. App. 3d 987; 565 N.E.2d 166; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1819; 151 Ill. Dec. 895



December 5, 1990  
December 5, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Cyril J. Watson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting plaintiff village's motion for judgment on the pleadings in the village's action against the property for violation of a zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The village cited the property owner for constructing a garage on his property in violation of the village's zoning ordinance. The property owner filed a motion to dismiss the complaint and requested a variance from the zoning requirements, and the trial court directed the village to conduct a hearing on the property owner's request. Thereafter, an amended complaint was filed, and after defendant filed an answer and a counterclaim, the village responded and filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings and a motion to dismiss the countercomplaint. The court entered judgment on the pleadings in favor of the village on two counts of its complaint and dismissed the countercomplaint. The property owner filed a motion for reconsideration, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that village was entitled to judgment on the pleadings because the property owner admitted that the size of his garage exceeded the requirements in the ordinance. The court held that the other issues raised on appeal were waived because the record on appeal did not demonstrate the errors of which the property owner complained, and the errors were not included in his prayer for relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting judgment on the pleadings in favor of the village in its action filed against the property owner for violating a zoning ordinance.

Sarka v. Rush Presbyterian-St. Luke's Medical Center


Nos. 1-89-2145, 1-89-2173 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


207 Ill. App. 3d 587; 566 N.E.2d 301; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1793; 152 Ill. Dec. 614



November 30, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne and the Hon. Charles J. Durham, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor, by his mother, challenged the orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which compelled the minor, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 215, to submit to a CT scan under sedation by chloral hydrate and held the minor's mother and attorneys in contempt for their refusal to comply with the order. 87 Ill. 2d R. 215. The trial court held that defendant hospital demonstrated the safety of chloral hydrate.


OVERVIEW: In a medical malpractice action, the minor, by his mother, claimed that his severe and permanent brain damage was caused by injuries sustained during his birth at defendant hospital. The hospital requested a Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 215 examination by CT scan while the minor was sedated to determine if the minor suffered from congenital schizencephaly. The trial court ordered the examination and held the minor's mother and attorneys in contempt for the minor's failure to submit to the CT scan. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The successor trial judge did not abuse his discretion in ordering the minor to submit to a CT scan under sedation because chloral hydrate was routinely and safely used, the risks of life-threatening complications were negligible, and the minor presented no evidence of harm that would result from the CT scan. The court required, however, that the order specify the dosage of chloral hydrate to be administered, the names of the physicians who would perform the CT scan, and the precautions to be taken in the event of an emergency. The court rejected the constitutional issues raised in the amici curiae brief as meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court vacated the contempt order and the fines.

 

1154 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ahmad


No. 1-88-0941


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


206 Ill. App. 3d 927; 565 N.E.2d 137; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1808; 151 Ill. Dec. 866



November 30, 1990  
November 30, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Jack G. Stein, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him, following a jury trial, of murder and sentencing him to a term of 26 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the murder of the victim and, at a subsequent reinstatement hearing, was found fit for trial and was tried before a jury. Following instructions to the jury on the verdicts of guilty, not guilty, not guilty by reason of insanity, and guilty but mentally ill (GBMI), the jury found defendant guilty of murder. Defendant argued that authorizing the jury to find him guilty but mentally ill introduced into the jury's fact-finding task a consideration that diverted the jury's attention from its primary task of determining his guilt or innocence. The court held that defendant's right to due process was not denied by the submission of a GBMI instruction to the jury. Defendant next argued that the trial court erred by failing to properly instruct the jury on the statutory elements and burden of proof for the guilty but mentally ill verdict. The court found that the instruction was defective and constituted plain error because it failed to place the burden on the State to prove that defendant was not insane beyond a reasonable doubt. The court further ruled that the defect was substantial, and that it was not waived by defendant's failure to make a timely objection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment of conviction. The court remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

1155 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


In re I.D.


Nos. 4-89-0885, 4-89-0915 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


205 Ill. App. 3d 543; 563 N.E.2d 1200; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1779; 151 Ill. Dec. 94



November 29, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication January 3, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. John R. DeLaMar, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which held that they were unfit parents and terminated their parental rights to their daughter pursuant to the Adoption Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1501(D) (1989).


OVERVIEW: The parents' daughter, then age two, was removed from their home after it was found that the father had sexually abused two older girls and that the mother, who had serious mental limitations, was unable to respond to the situation. The trial court also found that the child's environment had caused serious delays in her development. Almost two years later, the trial court found that the parents were unfit as defined by the Adoption Act and terminated their parental rights. The parents appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the Adoption Act was constitutional where it was rationally related to the goal of protecting children, and not all parents with disabilities were affected, only those who could not discharge their parental responsibilities. The court concluded that one of the main reasons the child was adjudicated abused was the mother's inability to protect her or to understand how to deal appropriately with the allegations of sexual abuse. Thus, there was sufficient evidence to establish the mother's inability to discharge her parental responsibilities. The father's failure to comply with a counseling plan supported the finding that he was unfit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which found that the parents were unfit and terminated their parental rights to their daughter.

 

1156 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Rodmaker v. Johns Holding Co.


No. 4-90-0194


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


205 Ill. App. 3d 520; 563 N.E.2d 1175; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1765; 151 Ill. Dec. 69



November 26, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication January 3, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 9, 1991. Second Correction March 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Warren A. Sappington, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant credit bureaus appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) that certified plaintiff employee as a class representative in her lawsuit challenging the credit bureaus' notice procedures for the garnishment of wages.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed suit against the credit bureaus claiming that the wage garnishment notices they served did not comply with the Illinois Wage Assignment Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 39.2b (1987). The employee sought certification as a class action lawsuit. The trial court certified the class, and the credit bureaus appealed. The court reversed and remanded. Under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-801, a class action could be maintained only if there were questions of fact or law common to the class, which predominated over any questions affecting only individual members. Here, those affected by violations of the Act were entitled to recover not only a statutory penalty but also compensatory damages. The compensatory damages issue could only be determined on an individual basis as to each person injured by a violation of the Act. Though the existence of an individual question did not necessarily defeat a class action, where that individual question was more time consuming and more difficult to prove, as was the case with compensatory damages, than the common question which was readily proved, maintenance of the suit as a class action was not permissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment certifying the employee's representation of the class challenging the credit bureau's wage garnishment notices was reversed and remanded.

People v. Champaign News-Gazette (In re A Minor)


Nos. 4-90-0167, 4-90-0168 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


205 Ill. App. 3d 480; 563 N.E.2d 1069; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1733; 150 Ill. Dec. 942



November 15, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication January 3, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 9, 1991. Second Correction January 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ford County; the Hon. William M. Roberts, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper in an interlocutory appeal challenged a ruling from the Circuit Court of Ford County (Illinois), which excluded the newspaper from juvenile proceedings involving two minors.


OVERVIEW: One of the newspaper's reporters was in court on the day scheduled for the adjudicatory hearing of two minors who were the victims of parental physical and sexual abuse. The trial judge ordered the reporter from the courtroom when the reporter identified himself and denied the reporter an immediate hearing on the exclusion order. Following a hearing on the newspaper's motion for reconsideration that enjoined the newspaper from disclosing the minors' identities, the newspaper appealed. The court determined that the newspaper could not be restrained from publishing information that it obtained through common reportorial techniques, but the trial court could exclude the newspaper from the proceedings even without the parties' request for exclusion, holding that the court as parens patriae had a duty to protect a minor when danger of harm was perceived. The state's interest in protecting the minors was compelling, and the trial court properly exercised its discretion under the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 801-5(6) (1989). The press did not have an absolute right of access to juvenile proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's injunction against the newspaper as to disclosure of the minor's identities, but concluded that the newspaper could not be restrained from publishing information gleaned through common reportorial techniques.

People v. Wehrwein


No. 1-87-2602


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


209 Ill. App. 3d 71; 568 N.E.2d 1; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1696; 154 Ill. Dec. 1



November 5, 1990  
November 5, 1990, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James M. Schreier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of possessing a certificate of title without complete assignment, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, par. 4 -- 104(a)(2) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to being convicted for possessing a certificate of title without complete assignment, defendant argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. However, in affirming the conviction, the court concluded that the statute was sufficiently definite to survive a vagueness challenge, because it provided a person of ordinary intelligence with notice of what conduct is prohibited. The court also held that the statute sufficiently restricted an officer's ability to arrest individuals under the statute and thus did not encourage arbitrary enforcement. Reviewing the record, the court then held that the evidence supported the trier of fact's conclusion that defendant had the requisite intent to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possessing a certificate of title without complete assignment.

Old Ben Coal Co. v. Department of Mines & Minerals


No. 5-89-0353


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


204 Ill. App. 3d 1062; 562 N.E.2d 1202; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1683; 150 Ill. Dec. 399; 112 Oil & Gas Rep. 400



November 1, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County; the Hon. Loren P. Lewis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois) affirmed a decision that was made by defendant Illinois Department of Mines and Minerals (IDMM), which required plaintiff coal mining company to repair or restore structures damaged by subsidence. The coal mining company appealed the affirmance of the decision.


OVERVIEW: The coal mining company contended that the IDMM had no authority under the Illinois Surface Coal Mining Land Conservation and Reclamation Act (Illinois Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 96 1/2, par. 7901.01 et seq. (1981) to require the repair or restoration of structures damaged by subsidence because the Illinois Act authorized only those standards which complied with the Federal Surface Mining Control and Reclamation Act of 1977 (Federal Act), 30 U.S.C.S. § 1201 et seq., and there were no promulgated Federal Act standards. In affirming the judgment, the court held that the coal mining company was required, through the Illinois Act, to repair and restore structures damaged by subsidence. The court found that because 30 C.F.R. § 817.121(c)(2) deferred to state law on the subject, the IDMM had authority under § 1.02(b), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 96 1/2, par. 7901.02(b) (1989), of the Illinois Act to promulgate regulations requiring the same. Because § 817.121(c)(2) recognized that state law may require repair or restoration of structures damaged by subsidence, the IDMM requirements promulgated under the Illinois Act were in compliance with the Federal Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court, which upheld the conditions contained in four permanent coal mining reclamation program permits issued by the IDMM, and which required the coal mining company to repair or restore structures damaged by subsidence, was affirmed.

Billman v. Crown-Trygg Corp.


No. 1-88-2215


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


205 Ill. App. 3d 916; 563 N.E.2d 903; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1670; 150 Ill. Dec. 776



October 29, 1990  
October 29, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 10, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Willard J. Lassers, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed two counts of their complaint against defendant construction companies for negligence in the reconstruction and modification of the intersection of two roads.


OVERVIEW: The individuals filed a complaint against the construction companies for injuries suffered in a traffic accident at an intersection that the construction companies had reconstructed and modified. The trial court granted the construction companies' motion to dismiss two counts of the first amended complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court rejected the individuals' argument that the work completed by the construction companies was merely a replacement and not an improvement to real property. The court held that the work performed by the construction companies constituted an improvement to real property under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-214(b) (1987), and therefore the individuals' claim was barred by the statute of repose for such claims. The court determined that real property was not limited to buildings. The court found the individuals' claim that the statute was unconstitutional to be unpersuasive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that dismissed two counts from the individuals' complaint against the construction companies.

 

1161 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schmitt


No. 4-89-0264


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


204 Ill. App. 3d 820; 562 N.E.2d 377; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1644; 149 Ill. Dec. 913



October 25, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication November 27, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 27, 1990. As Corrected January 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County; the Hon. Robert L. Welch, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14 (1987), and criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-3 (1987). At trial, the child victim testified via closed circuit television, as permitted by § 106A-3 of the Ill. Code of Crim. P., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 106A-3 (1987).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of sexual assault. The victim, his nine-year-old son, testified via closed circuit television. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of the procedure. The court affirmed, but remanded to correct the sentencing order. The court concluded that defendant's rights to confrontation and due process were not violated. The prosecutor, defense counsel, defendant, judge, the child, and the child's mother were in the judge's chambers during the child's testimony, which was broadcast into the courtroom for the jury. Defendant was not screened from the child's sight. The court found defendant was given full opportunity to probe and expose infirmities in the child's testimony, and the jury had adequate opportunity to assess the child's demeanor while he testified. The court also held the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding the procedure was in the child's best interest. The state's cross-examination of defendant was not so inflammatory as to threaten deterioration of the judicial process. The cause was remanded to clarify the record to reflect a verdict of guilty to one count of aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sexual assault conviction as modified, and remanded the cause for correction of the sentencing order.

People v. Matthews


No. 1-86-2816


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


205 Ill. App. 3d 371; 562 N.E.2d 1113; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1623; 150 Ill. Dec. 310



October 19, 1990  
October 19, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 10, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgement affirmed and mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting appellant of murder, armed violence, and theft, and assessing punishment of natural life in a penitentiary and four five-year sentences, all to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder, armed violence, and felony theft, and sentenced to concurrent life and four five-tear terms of imprisonment. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court and ordered the mittimus corrected. The court held that appellant was not subjected to an illegal arrest or compelled to make a statement involuntarily, and therefore evidence obtained as a result of his detention and statement was admissible. The court stated that there was proof that the value of items stolen were valued at more than $ 300, warranting felony theft instead of misdemeanor theft convictions. The court stated that rulings of the trial court were not violative of the federal or state constitutions. The court ruled that the imposition of the natural life sentence without consideration of factors in mitigation was not in violation of federal constitutional guarantees; the court also rejected appellant's contention that he was improperly sentenced under a mandatory life statute. The court further held, however, that two counts of murder merged into other murder counts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and ordered the mittimus corrected. The convictions for murder, felony theft, and armed violence were valid as admitted evidence was not illegally obtained, items stolen were valued in excess of $ 300, and the trial rulings and the sentences were not violative of the sate and federal constitutional guarantees.

 

1163 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Bryant v. Sherman


No. 4-90-0419


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


204 Ill. App. 3d 583; 561 N.E.2d 1320; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1583; 149 Ill. Dec. 624



October 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 26, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Richard J. Cadagin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted the request of appellees, sand pit owners and sand hauler, for a preliminary injunction barring the enforcement of an ordinance enacted by the village that placed a weight limit on the one road within the village limits that appellees used in their business.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance restricting the weight of trucks also had a provision for issuance of a permit to trucks over the weight limit upon payment of a fee. On appeal, the village argued that appellees had an adequate remedy in that they could continue to operate during pendency of their challenge of the ordinance by obtaining a permit. The court found that the cost of the permit would make the sand hauling business uneconomical, thereby causing appellees irreparable harm. The court found that this evidence supported the trial court's determination that obtaining a permit did not constitute an adequate legal remedy. The court rejected the village's argument that appellees had not proved they would prevail on the merits, stating that the movant had only to raise a fair question about the existence of his rights. The court found that appellees had met this burden by showing that the municipality had no power to impose a tax or license fee and that the permit fee could not be sustained because it was not related to enforcement of the ordinance but was meant to compensate the municipality for paving the road more frequently than would otherwise be required if it were not used by heavy trucks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the preliminary injunction barring the village's enforcement of an ordinance that restricted the weight of trucks that could use a certain road except upon payment of a permit fee. The court found that obtaining a permit pursuant to the ordinance did not constitute an adequate legal remedy and that appellees had raised a fair question as to the validity of the ordinance.

 

1164 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Urioste


No. 5-88-0591


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


203 Ill. App. 3d 1062; 561 N.E.2d 471; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1596; 149 Ill. Dec. 193



October 11, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. Charles Chapman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which found him guilty but mentally ill of murder, home invasion, armed violence, and attempted aggravated criminal sexual assault, and sentenced him to concurrent terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty but mentally ill of murder, home invasion, armed violence, and attempted aggravated criminal sexual assault, and was sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment. Defendant appealed, contending that the evidence presented at trial was not sufficient to prove his guilt of the offenses beyond a reasonable doubt. The court affirmed, concluding that there was ample evidence to support the verdict. A witness' identification of defendant as her daughter's assailant was corroborated by other witness testimony, physical evidence, and by defendant's statements. Given the variety and strength of the evidence against defendant, the court could not say that the trial court's determination of guilt was in error. Because defendant was not within the class of persons identified as falling into the gap between "preponderance" and "beyond a reasonable doubt," the statutory scheme had been applied constitutionally to him. The court determined that the evidence was sufficient to conclude that defendant did knowingly and intelligently waive his Miranda rights. Thus, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress his statements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which found defendant guilty but mentally ill of murder, home invasion, armed violence, and attempted aggravated criminal sexual assault, and sentenced him to concurrent terms of imprisonment.

 

1165 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


National Pride of Chicago, Inc. v. Chicago


No. 1-88-3133


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


206 Ill. App. 3d 1090; 562 N.E.2d 563; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1563; 150 Ill. Dec. 33



October 5, 1990  
October 5, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 19, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner of a self-service car wash (owner), appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County(Illinois), which dismissed the owner's suit for declaratory relief and injunction against defendant city to preclude application of the Chicago Transaction Tax Ordinance (ordinance) to the owner's business.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a revenue ruling, the city attempted to collect the transaction tax (tax) against operators of self-service car washes, but not against operators of tunnel or automatic car washes. The owner asserted that this was a violation of the state and federal constitutions. The circuit court granted summary judgment to the city. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the customer's use of the owner's equipment at the owner's facility did not constitute a "lease" of personal property subject to the tax, thus the ruling was an illegal expansion of the terms of the ordinance. The court found that the ruling made an artificial distinction between the owner and competitors based solely on the customer's hands-on participation in the owner's wash process. The court held that this distinction was arbitrary and based on no real or substantial difference, thus it violated the intent of the ordinance and the uniformity requirements of Ill. Const. 1970, art. IX, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court judgment, which dismissed the owner's suit for declaratory and injunctive relief against the city to preclude application of the ordinance to the owner's business.

 

1166 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Priola


No. 2-88-1014


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


203 Ill. App. 3d 401; 561 N.E.2d 82; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1539; 148 Ill. Dec. 776



October 2, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication November 15, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Robert D. McLaren, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; modified in part; and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual abuse, sentenced him to a three-year term of imprisonment, ordered him to reimburse the county for legal services that were provided by the public defender, and ordered that his conviction be reported to the secretary of state so that his driver's license would be revoked.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16 (1987). The trial court sentenced him to a three-year term of imprisonment, ordered him to reimburse the county for legal services provided, and ordered that his conviction be reported so that his driver's license would be revoked. The court affirmed the conviction, modified the amount to be paid as reimbursement to the county, and reversed the order that the conviction be reported. The jury could have found defendant guilty of the charge, even if there was no evidence that defendant touched the minor victim in the vaginal area, of which there was, in fact, evidence. The minor victim's testimony as to that charge was consistent, and, even though her testimony on a related charge was inconsistent, such testimony did not ruin her credibility, which was an issue for the jury's determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual abuse, but it modified the amount that defendant was ordered to pay to reimburse the county for legal services provided by the public defender. The court reversed the order that directed that the conviction be reported in order that defendant's driver's license would be revoked.

Safanda v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


Nos. 2-89-1256, 2-90-0200 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


203 Ill. App. 3d 687; 561 N.E.2d 412; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1538; 149 Ill. Dec. 134



October 2, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication November 5, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Michael J. Colwell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) that dismissed two counts of her complaint in administrative review and dismissed certain parties as defendants. The landowner filed suit against defendant zoning board of appeals of the City of Geneva (board) and others after her application for a rear-yard variance to enable her to build a single-family residence on her property was denied.


OVERVIEW: The landowner contended that: (1) count VI alleging that the board's meeting was held in violation of the Open Meetings Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, para. 41 et seq. (1989), should not have been dismissed as untimely filed; (2) the court erred in dismissing the city as a defendant; (3) the individual board members were proper parties to the suit and should not have been dismissed; and (4) the court erred in dismissing counts IV, V, and VI. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings. In so ruling, the court concluded that count VI was timely filed, and remanded with instructions to reinstate that count. The court affirmed the dismissal of the city and individual board members because the board, not the city, was responsible for the application of the zoning code and the city made no administrative decision to be reviewed; and the landowner provided no cognizable argument why the dismissal of the members was error. The court also found error in the dismissal of count IV because it sufficiently alleged a due process violation, and in count V that sought reversal of the board's decision and a variance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the individual board members under count III and affirmed the dismissal of the city as a party to the suit. The court reversed the circuit court's dismissal of counts IV, V, and VI, and remanded the cause to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Kus v. Sherman Hosp.


No. 2-89-1309


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


204 Ill. App. 3d 66; 561 N.E.2d 381; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1508; 149 Ill. Dec. 103



September 28, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 9, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. James F. Quetsch, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which dismissed with prejudice his negligence complaint against defendant hospital.


OVERVIEW: One of the hospital's doctors implanted an intraocular lens into the patient's left eye. This was done after the Federal Drug Administration had withdrawn its approval of the lens and the hospital was so informed. The patient subsequently lost vision in his left eye and incurred damages. The trial court granted the hospital's motion to dismiss the patient's complaint because the patient did not comply with § 6 -- 622 of the Code of Civil Procedure, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1989) in that the complaint lacked the necessary affidavit attesting to the soundness of the complaint. The patient argued that his complaint did not fall within the statute's purview because it sounded in administrative hospital negligence, not in healing art malpractice. The court held that the hospital's alleged negligence was based on conduct that was not measured by common knowledge but required medical knowledge. As such, the patient was required to comply with the statute. However, because the patient believed that the statute did not apply, the trial court abused its discretion in dismissing the complaint with prejudice and the court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the patient's negligence complaint.

People v. Navarro


No. 1-88-1803


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


204 Ill. App. 3d 1097; 562 N.E.2d 987; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1517; 150 Ill. Dec. 184



September 28, 1990  
September 28, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 19, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas P. Durkin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for delivery of more than 30 grams of a controlled substance in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 =, para. 1401(a)(2) (1983). Defendant contended that his Fifth Amendment rights against double jeopardy were violated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of delivery of more than 30 grams of a controlled substance. Defendant was indicted and initially tried in a bench trial with two co-defendants. Defendant was found guilty and retained a new attorney, who filed a motion for new trial alleging ineffectiveness of counsel, which was granted. The State conceded that defendant was entitled to a new trial based on the jury statute being declared unconstitutional. Prior to the retrial, defendant attempted to waive a jury, but the State invoked its right to a jury under a statute later found to be unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that because defendant was given a new trial due to the ineffective assistance of his initial counsel and not due to lack of evidence or an adjudication that defendant was not guilty, double jeopardy did not prohibit a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the circuit court.

People v. Letsos


No. 2-89-0709


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


203 Ill. App. 3d 443; 561 N.E.2d 371; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1522; 149 Ill. Dec. 93



September 28, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John J. Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of violating § 44(j)(1)(A) of the Illinois Environmental Protection Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1044(j)(1)(A) (1989), based on allegations that defendant discharged a contaminant into the waters of the state without a permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to two years' probation, 200 hours of community service and a $ 7,500 fine for violating § 44(j)(1)(A) of the Illinois Environmental Protection Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1044(j)(1)(A) (1989), by pumping gasoline from an underground storage tank into the town sewer. Defendant appealed, arguing that subsection 44(j)(1)(A) was unconstitutional in that it was vague, ambiguous, and subject to arbitrary enforcement and that the state failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt because the state failed to prove that defendant knew he was pumping gasoline. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that § 44(j)(1)(A) was not unconstitutionally vague when it was read together with the appropriate sections of the Federal Pollution Control Act. The court found that the relevant statutory provisions considered as a unit were sufficiently clear and precise in defining the offense under § 44(j)(1)(A). The court found that the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant knowingly violated subsection 12(f) of the Act, because at some time during the pumping process, defendant had knowledge that he was pumping gasoline.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for discharging a contaminant into the waters of the state without a permit.

People v. Deveaux

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of possession with intent to deliver more than 30 grams of a controlled substance in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(a)(2) (1985), and possession with intent to deliver more than 500 grams of cannabis in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 705(e) (1985).


OVERVIEW: The police obtained a warrant to search an apartment based on an informant's tip that defendant gave him a substance that defendant knew to be cocaine. People v. House


No. 4-90-0075


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


202 Ill. App. 3d 893; 560 N.E.2d 1224; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1485; 148 Ill. Dec. 627



September 27, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication October 29, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 29, 1990. Rehearing Denied October 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court County of Adams; No. 86CF149; Honorable Dennis K. Cashman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial by the Circuit Court County of Adams (Illinois) of his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arraigned after beating a woman in a car and firing shots. Defendant initially lied about his identity. The trial court advised defendant of the charges and admonished him that a trial would occur in his absence if he failed to appear. Defendant failed to appear, and a trial in absentia was conducted. Defendant was convicted of perjury, unlawful use of firearms by a felon, and aggravated assault. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed and held that no error occurred in trying defendant in absentia. The court reasoned that certified mail notice was not necessary because defendant was personally present when the trial court set his trial date, was admonished that the trial would occur in his absence if he failed to appear, and no new trial date was ever set. The court found that defendant was not surprised by the technical amendment made to the information. The court found that joinder of the offenses was not erroneous where defendant opposed severance at trial. The court found that consecutive sentences were appropriate where the perjury had a separate motivation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

People v. Buckner


No. 4-89-0570


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


203 Ill. App. 3d 525; 561 N.E.2d 335; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1463; 149 Ill. Dec. 57



September 25, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication November 2, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 26, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. John K. Greanias, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois). A jury convicted defendant of first-degree murder, armed violence, and burglary, and the circuit court sentenced him to 40 years on the first-degree murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: The first issue defendant raised on appeal was whether the requirement under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9 -- 2 (1987) that defendant show, by a preponderance of the evidence, that he acted under sudden and intense passion to be convicted of second-degree rather than first-degree murder violated the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution.The court concluded that the statute was constitutional because it did not require defendant to prove any elements of first-degree murder. Defendant contended that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he committed burglary by entering his wife's car with intent to commit a theft therein because the evidence showed he had driven his wife's car on prior occasions with her permission. Although the car was marital property, the court concluded that defendant was properly convicted of burglary. Defendant also argued that the 40-year sentence was excessive because the circuit court failed to consider his potential for rehabilitation, his age, and work record. The court found that the circuit court did not abuse its discretion when it sentenced defendant to 40 years' imprisonment for first-degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentence.

People v. Ferguson


No. 1-89-0809


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


204 Ill. App. 3d 146; 561 N.E.2d 1118; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1452; 149 Ill. Dec. 422



September 21, 1990, Decided  
September 21, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 22, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Jack Stein, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, following a bench trial, convicted him of possession of a stolen motor vehicle in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4 -- 103(a)(1) (1987) and sentenced him to three years in the Illinois Department of Corrections. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence and the constitutionality of the inference of guilt contained in para. 4 --103.


OVERVIEW: Officers pulled over a car after it nearly struck a pedestrian. They noticed that the steering column had been "peeled," ran a computer check of the car, and learned that it had been reported as stolen. Defendant told the officers that he did not know to whom the car belonged. Defendant was charged with possession of a stolen motor vehicle. At trial he testified that a man at a local beach had lent him the car to get beer and that he did not know the car was stolen or that the steering column had been damaged. The trial court convicted him of violating para. 4-103(a)(1). On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction because, under the statute, an inference of defendant's knowledge that the vehicle had been stolen could be drawn from the fact of his exclusive possession of the car. The court upheld the legality of the statutory inference because it was not irrefutable and could be rebutted by defendant's explanation. The court found that defendant's explanation that he had obtained a car from a man he had never seen before, and that he did not see that the steering column was "peeled," strained belief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding defendant guilty of possession of a stolen motor vehicle.

People v. Hood

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division

September 19, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gerald T. Roher, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found her guilty but mentally ill (GBMI) of murder and sentenced her to 30 years' imprisonment in connection with the death of her daughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took a cord from her bathrobe and tied it around her two year old daughter's neck strangling her. Thereafter, defendant submerged her daughter under water in the bathtub fully clothed for a few minutes. She then removed her daughter from the bathtub, dried her and dressed her, and then placed her in bed. Defendant called her husband at work and told him to come home. She made a statement to the police admitting she killed her daughter and describing the incident. Defendant was charged with murder. The defense theory at trial was that defendant was insane at the time of the offense. Defendant was found GBMI and sentenced to 30 years' imprisonment. She sought review contending that the GBMI statute was unconstitutionally vague and unconstitutional because it did not bear a rational relationship to the public interest it was intended to serve. The court affirmed defendant's conviction finding that defendant lacked standing to challenge the GBMI statute's constitutional validity because she did not suffer a direct injury as a result of the statute's enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.
