People v. Henry


No. 1-86-2861


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


203 Ill. App. 3d 278; 560 N.E.2d 1205; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1428; 148 Ill. Dec. 608



September 19, 1990  
September 19, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Philip J. Carey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; sentence vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for theft of a motor vehicle and possession of a stolen motor vehicle, denied defendant's request for a substance abuse evaluation, and sentenced defendant to a term of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted defendant for theft of a motor vehicle and possession of a stolen motor vehicle and was sentenced to a term of imprisonment. Defendant's conviction had previously been reversed by the court. Subsequently the court's reversal was reversed by the state supreme court and remanded to court. On remand, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that the trial court's finding that under the totality of circumstances defendant had intended to permanently deprive the automobile's owner of possession of the automobile was supported by the evidence. However, the court vacated defendant's sentence of imprisonment and remanded for a new sentencing hearing. The court held that the trial court had no discretion to grant a substance abuse evaluation under the Alcoholism and Substance Abuse Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, par. 6302 (1985) et seq., and that the trial court improperly ignored defendant's statements that he was a drug addict. The court concluded that the trial court had sufficient reason to believe that defendant was an addict and was thus required to order an evaluation of defendant under the act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for theft of a motor vehicle and possession of a stolen motor vehicle, but vacated defendant's sentence of imprisonment and remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

 

1177 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Gotsch v. Burbank


Nos. 1-90-0340, 1-90-0341 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


203 Ill. App. 3d 271; 560 N.E.2d 1183; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1417; 148 Ill. Dec. 586



September 18, 1990  
September 18, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Kenneth Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, tavern and amusement company owners (owners), appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the relief sought by the owners in their action against defendant city for declaratory and injunctive relief from the enforcement of an ordinance which prohibited devices capable of awarding prizes or money from being located on the premises of licensed liquor establishments.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance which prohibited devices capable of awarding prizes or money from being located on the premises of licensed liquor establishments. The city's liquor control officer issued letters to all holders of liquor licenses in the city informing them of the ordinance and that the use of poker machines, card machines, or any game or similar machine or device was to be abated immediately. The owners filed an action against the city for declaratory and injunctive relief from the enforcement of an ordinance. The trial court denied any relief to the owners. The owners appealed, contending that their electronic video poker machines were not within the class of machines covered by the ordinance. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the trial court's finding was against the manifest weight of the evidence and that the owners' machines fell outside the class of machines prohibited by the city's ordinance. The parties stipulated that the ordinance was intended to prevent gambling. No evidence was offered to sustain the proposition that the ordinance was intended to create a prohibition on all poker and card machines incapable of awarding prizes or money.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, which denied the owners relief in their action against the city for declarative and injunctive relief against the enforcement of an ordinance which prohibited devices capable of awarding prizes or money from location at establishments with liquor licenses.

People v. Lowe


No. 4-89-0970


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


202 Ill. App. 3d 648; 560 N.E.2d 438; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1391; 148 Ill. Dec. 136



September 13, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 23, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court County of Brown; No. 89CF3; Honorable Robert W. Cook, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court, County of Brown (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated battery "on or about a public way," Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4(b)(8) (1987). He argued that the statute was unconstitutional for overbreadth and vagueness. Plaintiff, the People of the State of Illinois, contended that the phrase "on or about a public way" was consistent with its legislative intent.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court noted that the constitutionality of the Illinois aggravated battery statute had been upheld under both due process and equal protection challenges. A statute only need be sufficiently certain to give fair notice to a person of ordinary intelligence that his contemplated conduct was forbidden by law. The court held that the legislature wanted the courts to have broad discretion to determine whether a person committed a battery "on or about a public way," and chose flexible terms in order to insure the broad protection of the public health and safety. The court determined that the definition given by the circuit court of "about," as the immediate neighborhood of or near, was a permissible definition. The court found that defendant's contention that the more appropriate definition would have been "immediately adjacent to the public way; so close to the public way as to interfere with the public's travel" was without merit. To limit the meaning to the definition offered by defendant would be in direct conflict with the legislature's intent. The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision and conviction of the circuit court. The court rejected the constitutional challenges to the statute and found sufficient evidence for a jury to conclude that a battery occurred "on or about a public way."

 

1179 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


No. 1-88-1128


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


203 Ill. App. 3d 22; 560 N.E.2d 1028; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1367; 148 Ill. Dec. 431



September 7, 1990  
September 7, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Philip J. Carey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of the possession of a stolen motor vehicle. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the motor vehicle statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4--103 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion for a new trial, and the circuit court vacated a theft conviction. The appellate court affirmed the stolen possession conviction. The court first rejected the state's argument that defendant waived the constitutionality issue by not raising it in the circuit court. Defendant raised the issue in his new trial motion, and regardless, recent law held that the constitutionality of a statute could have been challenged for the first time on appeal. However, all of defendant's constitutional arguments had previously been heard by the courts and rejected. The statute did not violate due process, and it did not create a disproportionate penalty given the legislature's concern that vehicle theft was a greater crime than ordinary theft. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it allegedly had contradictory mental states required scienter and constructive knowledge. The statute only created an evidentiary presumption, not a mental state of constructive knowledge.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for the possession of a stolen motor vehicle was affirmed on appeal.

People v. Smith


No. 4-89-0898


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


202 Ill. App. 3d 606; 560 N.E.2d 399; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1357; 148 Ill. Dec. 97



September 6, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court County of Champaign No. 88CF698; Honorable Harold L. Jensen, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the revocation of his probation by the Circuit Court County of Champaign (Illinois). Defendant contended that the trial court could not resentence him in his absence and that the petition to revoke his probation was fatally defective.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's arraignment on charges of aggravated battery and a misdemeanor offense, the trial court advised him that if he failed to appear in court for any hearing in the matter he waived his right to confront witnesses and the court could proceed in his absence. An indictment was later issued and at a preliminary hearing the trial court again advised defendant that his failure to appear in any hearing constituted a waiver of his right to confront witnesses and that his trial would proceed in his absence. Defendant pled guilty to aggravated battery and was sentenced to probation. The State filed a petition to revoke defendant's probation, defendant stipulated to the violation of probation, and a resentencing hearing was held on the violation. Prior to the hearing defendant was in the courtroom but left and did not return. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that it was not reversible error for the trial court to resentence defendant in his absence because the trial court twice advised defendant that his trial would proceed in his absence if he failed to appear at any hearing in the matter and the sentencing hearing was part of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

 

1181 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Seaman


No. 5-88-0357


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


203 Ill. App. 3d 871; 561 N.E.2d 188; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1326; 148 Ill. Dec. 882



August 30, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Lloyd A. Karmeier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), in which he was found guilty but mentally ill on each count of attempted murder and armed violence for an attack upon his wife. He was sentenced for nine years concurrently. He was first declared unfit to stand trial. After a second examination, he was declared fit. He appealed his convictions on various grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the constitutionality, as applied to him, of the Illinois law of insanity and mental illness. He contended that § 6 -- 2 of the Criminal Code of 1961, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 6 -- 2 (1987), and § 115 -- 4(j) of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115 -- 4(j) (1987), violated his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection. On appeal, the court found that those sections did not threaten a constitutional right and limited its inquiry to whether the "guilty but mentally ill" (GBMI) classification had a rational basis. The court could not discern the impermissible classification involved and found no equal protection violation. The court also held that because no fundamental constitutional right was threatened, its review for substantive due process purposes involved only the reasonableness of the law. The court found the GBMI statute was rationally designed to accomplish the legislative goal of reducing the number of persons erroneously found not guilty by reason of insanity and to characterize such defendants as in need of treatment. The court affirmed judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which did not err when: it found no violation of defendant's right to a speedy trial; it admitted the state's expert's testimony on sanity; it found that defendant was mentally ill beyond a reasonable doubt; it found the legal provisions on insanity, mental illness, and "guilty but mentally ill" verdict constitutional; and it removed two prospective jurors for cause.

People v. Flanagan


No. 4-88-0485


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


201 Ill. App. 3d 1071; 559 N.E.2d 1105; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1307; 147 Ill. Dec. 765



August 30, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 2, 1990. As Corrected October 23, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Menard County; the Hon. Carson K. Klitz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction of the felony offense of aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 --14(b)(1) (1987), from the Circuit Court of Menard County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant initially contended that he was denied due process by the state's failure to institute formal probation revocation proceedings in an underlying misdemeanor action for which he had been charged, and for which, after entering a negotiated agreement, he was serving probation. The trial court found that the misdemeanor charge and the probation sentence imposed were separate and distinct from the felony charges the state elected to file. On appeal, the court held that the state's charging action, viewed in its entirety, complied with due process. Following verification of the negative probation reports, the state was free to file either a revocation of probation petition or the remaining felony charges for different offenses against defendant under the plea agreement. Defendant contended that the misdemeanor action barred the felony action under the doctrine of double jeopardy. The court disagreed. The statutory elements of the charged offenses were distinct. Each offense required proof of a fact which the other did not, they did not constitute the same offense. The court also did not find the alleged prosecutorial vindictiveness, or a wrongful substitution of the trial judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

People v. Bryant


No. 1-87-1822


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


202 Ill. App. 3d 290; 559 N.E.2d 930; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1214; 147 Ill. Dec. 590



August 16, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Themis Karnezis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), where he was found guilty by a jury on charges of murder, attempted murder, armed robbery, home invasion, and residential burglary. Defendant alleged error in the circuit court's admission of certain evidence, the rejection of certain jury requests, and the use of the wrong standard to evaluate defendant's objections to the state's peremptory challenges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on charges of armed robbery and aggravated battery, and was appointed counsel on those charges. While in custody, he was interviewed about the instant crimes, and after being advised twice of his Miranda rights, he gave a statement to police detailing his involvement in them. Defendant later filed a motion to suppress his statement, which was denied, and defendant was convicted on the instant charges. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed his convictions, holding that because defendant did not request that his previously appointed counsel be present while he was being interrogated about the instant crimes and the record did not indicate that defendant was pressured into confessing to his involvement in them, defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived his Fifth Amendment rights and thus admission of the statement was proper. The court found that the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of an unrelated warrant because it was necessary to establish the steps leading up to defendant's confession in the instant crimes and that defendant failed to preserve error and/or sustain his burden of proof on his remaining claims on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, attempted murder, armed robbery, home invasion, and residential burglary.

 

1184 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Richmond


No. 4-89-0323


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


201 Ill. App. 3d 130; 559 N.E.2d 302; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1228; 147 Ill. Dec. 302



August 16, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; No. 88CF685; the Hon. Jerry L. Patton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court, Macon County (Illinois), which convicted him of first-degree murder. Defendant alleged error in the introduction of testimony that he requested an attorney immediately upon learning of the victim's death, in the introduction of evidence of other crimes, and in the trial court's refusal to permit an offer of proof related to the testimony of a prosecution witness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1987). On appeal, defendant objected to the admission of testimony that defendant requested an attorney immediately upon learning of the victim's death. The court found that defendant did not object at trial, nor did he object in his post-trial motion. Defendant thus waived the alleged error. The court found that the plain error exception to the waiver rule did not apply because the evidence was not closely balanced, and defendant's substantial rights were not affected. Defendant also objected to the introduction of testimony as to other crimes that he committed. The court found that such evidence was inadmissible to show defendant's propensity for committing crimes but admissible for the purpose of showing motive and modus operandi, as well as to demonstrate defendant's dislike of the victim. Defendant also objected to the trial court's refusal to permit an offer of proof related to the testimony of a prosecution witness. The court found that an offer of proof regarding the witness' testimony in prior unrelated cases was too remote to impeach her testimony in defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1185 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Burton


No. 4-89-0794


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


201 Ill. App. 3d 116; 558 N.E.2d 1369; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1217; 146 Ill. Dec. 1035



August 16, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 12, 1990. Second Correction September 20, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of De Witt County; No. 89CF1; the Hon. Stephen H. Peters, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court of De Witt County (Illinois), which convicted him of three counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and sentenced defendant to concurrent terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: An indictment was returned charging defendant with various counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault against children. Defendant was convicted of three counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse. The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent terms of imprisonment. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant was not entitled to have the jury instructed as to the necessity of the state proving beyond a reasonable doubt the existence of each of the mental states implied by § 4-3(a) of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 4-3(a) (1987). By the terms of § 4-3(a), the state was required to prove a mental state for each of the elements of the offense of aggravated criminal sexual assault even though no such mental states were expressly set forth in the statutory language defining the offense. The mental state implied by § 4-3 necessarily accompanied the prohibited elements of the offense of sexual assault. The implied mental states were not specific enough to require instruction to a jury, and the circuit court did not err in giving the pattern instructions, which did not set forth those mental states.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction and sentence against defendant for aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated criminal sexual abuse.

People v. Hernandez


No. 2-88-0518


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


204 Ill. App. 3d 732; 562 N.E.2d 219; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1207; 149 Ill. Dec. 755

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. John J. Nelligan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and attempted murder and imposed an extended-term sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to murder and attempted murder and was advised that extended-term penalties would be possible if the circumstances of the offenses were found to have been accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior. The decedent was stabbed 89 times and the other victim was stabbed 7 times. His sentence for the murder was an 80-year extended-term sentence. The court affirmed the circuit court's decision and rejected defendant's contention that the probable existence of a diminished mental state was a strong mitigating factor. He argued that he may have been entitled to voluntary manslaughter instructions predicated upon the sudden, intense passion provoked in him by the sight of the woman he loved in the arms of another man. The court held that defendant's acts were not provoked by a sudden and intense passion because he had previously made remarks to his supervisor that he might kill the decedent if he found out that she was seeing someone else. The court concluded that the record showed that defendant's sentence was not affected by a victim impact statement linking the decedent's brother's suicide to the murder of the decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for murder and attempted murder.

Evanston v. Reg'l Transp. Auth.


No. 1-89-0545


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


202 Ill. App. 3d 265; 559 N.E.2d 899; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1221; 147 Ill. Dec. 559



August 15, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 29, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Roger Kiley, Jr., and the Hon. Monica Reynolds, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city objected to the plans of defendant transportation authority to build a bus garage and maintenance facility in the city and filed suit for injunctive relief in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to the authority and dismissed two counts of the authority's counterclaim. The city appealed, and the authority cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that the authority was subject to the zoning ordinance and urged that if the legislature intended to give the authority immunity from local zoning restrictions, then a specific statutory exemption had to be provided. The authority urged error in the ruling that political subdivisions had no constitutional rights. The court held that (1) the application of the city's zoning ordinance to the regional bus facility was not within the grant of home rule power; (2) the court had no jurisdiction over whether the trial court erred in permitting amendment of the second amended counterclaim because some of the counts were still pending; (3) the authority's property was public property and was not protected by the just compensation clauses of either the federal or the state constitution; (4) political subdivisions of a state had no rights under the federal or state constitution which the subdivision could invoke in opposition to its creator, the state; (5) the authority was a political subdivision of the state; and (6) the authority lacked rights to substantive due process and equal protection under either the federal or the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court found no error and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

People v. Roby


No. 5-89-0328


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


200 Ill. App. 3d 1063; 558 N.E.2d 729; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1142; 146 Ill. Dec. 766



August 1, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County; the Hon. Carl H. Becker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with aggravated battery. The Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois) dismissed the charge due to the state's failure to conduct a timely preliminary hearing. The state then filed a new charge of aggravated battery and provided a hearing that same day. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss that charge. A trial was held and defendant was convicted. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the failure to provide a timely hearing violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 7 (1970), which guaranteed an accused a prompt preliminary hearing, and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 109-3.1 (1989), which guaranteed an accused a preliminary hearing within 30 days of the date he was taken into custody. The second charge of aggravated battery was filed under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114-1(e) (1989), which defendant argued was unconstitutional to the extent that it allowed the state to file a new information charging the same offenses as an original information that was dismissed for failure to provide a prompt hearing. The court affirmed and held that § 114-1(e) was not unconstitutional. The court reasoned that the constitutional and statutory purposes of providing for a preliminary probable cause hearing were to ensure that an accused's freedom was not restricted without a prompt showing of evidence that a crime had been committed. The remedy provided for in § 114-1(e) of dismissal of the charges without prejudice succeeded in ensuring that a defendant was not unjustly detained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated battery and the order of the trial court that denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charges due to the state's failure to provide defendant a timely preliminary hearing.

Denofrio v. Kuc (In re Custody of D.A.)


No. 1-87-3827


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


201 Ill. App. 3d 810; 558 N.E.2d 1355; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1124; 146 Ill. Dec. 1021

The petition was dismissed on the ground that it was barred by the two-year limitations period set forth in § 8 of the Illinois Parentage Act of 1984 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2508(a) (1985).


OVERVIEW: The child had been in the custody of the respondent former husband of the child's deceased mother. Both the biological father and the former husband sought to establish a father-child relationship with the minor child, and also sought permanent custody. The former husband was declared the child's father. The biological father claimed to be the child's father because he lived with and had sexual intercourse with the child's mother during the time when the child was conceived. He also claimed that the child's mother told him that he was the father, he had visited the child, and contributed to the child's support. The former husband and the guardian ad litem both filed motions to dismiss the biological father's parentage petition on the ground that the two-year statute of limitations of the Act barred his claim. The court found that the parentage petition was filed about five years after the child's birth, about 22 months after the Act was passed and over 12 months after it was effective. The court held that the delay of one year and 10 days to file a paternity action was not reasonable under the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, which dismissed the biological father's petition to establish paternity rights.

 

1192 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bloyer


No. 2-89-0219


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


200 Ill. App. 3d 872; 558 N.E.2d 1056; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1128; 146 Ill. Dec. 857



July 31, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication September 6, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 6, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County; the Hon. Lawrence A. Smith, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of armed violence predicated on the underlying offense of unlawful restraint. Defendant contended that the conviction based on unlawful restraint with a category I weapon violated the guarantee of proportional sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant used a knife to force the victim into his vehicle to force her to have sex, but she escaped. The state supreme court had ruled that a conviction of armed violence based on unlawful restraint with the use of a category I weapon was disproportional because more serious offenses were punished less severely. The appellate court affirmed on the basis that it did not have to review new case law at all. The legislature cured the defect by adding the offense of aggravated unlawful restraint, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10--3.1 (1987). With the new crime, there was a proportional structure between the different categories of unlawful restraint and kidnapping. With the new law, unlawful restraint could have risen to the level of aggravated unlawful restraint, a Class 3 felony. Simple kidnapping could have risen to the level of aggravated kidnapping, a Class 1 felony. Accordingly, at whatever level, unlawful restraint was punished as a less serious offense than kidnapping. In conclusion, there was no constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Niles v. Chicago


No. 1-87-1749


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


201 Ill. App. 3d 651; 558 N.E.2d 1324; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1110; 146 Ill. Dec. 990



July 26, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff suburban municipalities filed an action against defendant city challenging the water rates charged by the city as being excessive and unreasonable and seeking injunctive relief. They also sought a refund of costs attributable to sewer services. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment denying the suburban municipalities the relief requested, and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: The suburban municipalities received their water supply from the city, and they claimed that the water rates charged by the city were excessive because they were not reasonably related to the cost of service. The court held that the suburban municipalities were entitled to a refund of costs attributable to sewer services but ruled that the water rates charged by the city were otherwise reasonable. In so holding, the court ruled that (1) the rates established by the city were legislative acts and were therefore entitled to a presumption of validity; (2) the method selected by the city for calculating the water rate was rationally related to a legitimate legislative purpose; (3) the suburban municipalities failed to carry their burden of proving that the rates were excessive and unreasonable; and (4) charging the suburban municipalities for costs attributable to the provision of sewer service was unreasonable because the suburban municipalities received no sewer service from the city.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the portion of the judgment which denied the suburban municipalities relief as to the issue of sewer costs and remanded the case for further proceedings on that issue, but otherwise affirmed the order of the lower court.

Coronet Ins. Co. v. Washburn


No. 1-89-0981


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


201 Ill. App. 3d 633; 558 N.E.2d 1307; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1078; 146 Ill. Dec. 973



July 24, 1990, nunc pro tunc June 5, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert L. Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state director of insurance appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion to dismiss plaintiff insurance company's action and denied his motion to dissolve a temporary restraining order, and which permanently enjoined him from enforcing Department of Insurance Rule 919.60(d) that prohibited insurance companies from requiring insureds to take polygraph tests.


OVERVIEW: The insurance company insisted that it was necessary to request insureds to take a polygraph test to detect whether they were attempting to defraud the company. The state director of insurance had promulgated an amendment to the insurance regulations to prohibit insurers from requesting or requiring the polygraph tests. The company filed an action for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, alleging that the director's amendment violated the Illinois Administrative Procedures Act (IAPA), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 1002 et seq. (1987). The trial court permanently enjoined the director from enforcing the amendment and denied his motion to dismiss and dissolve a temporary restraining order. The court reversed, finding that the director did not exceed his authority in promulgating the amendment. The court found that the proposed regulation did not unduly restrict the company's ability to conduct a claims investigation and that it was within the scope of the enabling statute, the Insurance Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, paras. 766.5, 766.6 (1987). The court found that the regulation was not unconstitutionally vague and the director did not violate the IAPA.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that enjoined the state insurance director from enforcing an amendment to the insurance regulations, which prevented the insurance company from requiring its insureds to take polygraph tests.

 

1195 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Barth v. Massa


No. 5-88-0185


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


201 Ill. App. 3d 19; 558 N.E.2d 528; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1063; 146 Ill. Dec. 565



July 17, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Stephen M. Kernan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor shot appellee officer. The officer filed an action for damages based on negligence and willful and wanton misconduct against the minor and on negligent entrustment and negligent parental supervision against appellant parents. The Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) issued the officer a directed verdict against the minor and a general verdict against the minor and parents. The minor and parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: A minor confessed to shooting an officer with a pistol during the minor's commission of a burglary. The officer filed an action for negligence and willful misconduct against the minor and negligent entrustment and negligent parental supervision against the parents of the minor. The circuit court entered a directed verdict against the minor and a general verdict against the parents. The minor and parents sought review. The court held that the general verdict against the parents was improper because the evidence demonstrated that they did not control the pistol, know that it existed, and have the opportunity to interfere with it. The court held that the directed verdict against the minor was proper because the evidence showed that the minor's conduct was the proximate cause of the officer's injuries, the shooting constituted willful and wanton conduct, the admission of the minor's bank statement was proper to refute his statement that he withdrew money from his bank account to pay for the pistol, and admission of hearsay testimony about a prior shooting incident was proper to show that the parents were told that the minor was involved in the prior incident.


OUTCOME: The judgment against the parents was reversed. The judgment against the minor was affirmed.

 

1196 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Biesiada


No. 3-89-0434


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


201 Ill. App. 3d 39; 558 N.E.2d 520; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1034; 146 Ill. Dec. 557



July 13, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 4, 1990. Rehearing Denied September 4, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Henry County; No. 88 CF 683; the Hon. Jeffrey W. O'Connor, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Henry County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of one count of second degree murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2(a)(1) (1987), and three counts of armed violence, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1987). The circuit court sentenced defendant to four consecutive 10-year prison terms.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was not proven guilty of armed violence beyond a reasonable doubt, that the armed violence statute was unconstitutional, and that he was subjected to double enhancement in the sentencing scheme, which resulted in consecutive terms of imprisonment. In affirming, the court held that defendant was proven guilty of armed violence beyond a reasonable doubt because he employed a dangerous weapon during the course of the underlying felony. The court also determined that the armed violence statute was not unconstitutionally applied to defendant. According to the court, the sentencing scheme that provided for a greater potential penalty for armed violence predicated upon aggravated battery than for second degree murder was not unconstitutional. Finally, the court held that the imposed sentence did not constitute double enhancement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

 

1197 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State Universities Retirement System


No. 4-89-0468


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


203 Ill. App. 3d 513; 560 N.E.2d 893; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 1018; 148 Ill. Dec. 296



July 12, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication October 31, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 27, 1990. Rehearing Denied October 31, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Jeffrey B. Ford, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State Universities Retirement System (SURS) appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which held that it was liable for attorney fees with respect to a recoupment of disability benefits. Plaintiff attorney who requested payment of the fees cross-appealed the portion of the order holding that his only recourse for obtaining payment of the fees was an action in the Court of Claims.


OVERVIEW: The attorney filed a complaint for administrative review of a decision of the executive committee of SURS refusing to pay fees to the attorney with respect to the recoupment of disability benefits which it had obtained as a result of the attorney's efforts in securing an award of occupational disease benefits for his client. The lower court held that SURS was liable for attorney fees, but that the claim could only be pursued in the Court of Claims. On appeal, the court held that the attorney was entitled to an award of fees from the monies recouped by the SURS under the common-fund doctrine. The court held that the attorney's only recourse for obtaining payment of the fees was by means of an action in the Court of Claims. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding SURS liable for attorney fees. The court held that the attorney's only recourse for obtaining payment of the fees was by means of an action in the Court of Claims.

 

1198 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


De Silva v. Hartack


No. 1-89-1876


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


201 Ill. App. 3d 387; 559 N.E.2d 51; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 995; 147 Ill. Dec. 51



June 29, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a licensed jockey, appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of the Illinois Racing Board (IRB) upholding the jockey's suspension for violating Ill. Racing Board R. 234.


OVERVIEW: The jockey contended that Rule 234 was unconstitutionally vague or, alternatively, that his suspension was contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence. The court upheld the jockey's suspension. The court held that Rule 234 provided clear notice that the jockey's "coasting" conduct in the fifth race was prohibited. The court also determined that the IRB's suspension of the jockey was not contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

 

1199 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Drew


No. 1-86-2088


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


201 Ill. App. 3d 271; 559 N.E.2d 40; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 998; 147 Ill. Dec. 40



June 29, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Robert L. Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a stolen motor vehicle under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 4-103(b) after denying his motion to dismiss the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 4-103(b) was unconstitutional and that the cause of action should have been remanded for a Batson hearing because the state used its peremptory challenges to exclude all blacks from the jury. The court found that the statute was constitutional because it was reasonably designed to protect the public from the evils of the offense of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and its related activities. Remanding for a Batson hearing, the court held that the fact that one black person was an alternate juror did not show a lack of discrimination. The court found that because the state did not argue the untimeliness of defendant's objection to the use of peremptory challenges when defendant raised the issue at the conclusion of voir dire and in a post-trial motion, the state waived its argument regarding timeliness as it failed to raise the issue at trial.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for a Batson hearing on defendant's assertion that the state systematically discriminated against blacks in its exercise of peremptory challenges. The court directed that if defendant made a prima facie case, then the state was to have an opportunity to rebut. If the state failed to rebut, a new trial was to be ordered. If the state succeeded, defendant's conviction and sentence were to be reinstated.

 

1200 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Board of Educ., Leroy Community Unit School Dist. No. 2 v. Illinois Educational Labor Relations Bd.


No. 4-89-0588


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


199 Ill. App. 3d 347; 556 N.E.2d 857; 1990 Ill. App. LEXIS 948; 145 Ill. Dec. 239



June 28, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Released for Publication August 1, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 13, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for review of order of Illinois Educational Labor Relations Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner school district appealed the order of respondent, Illinois Educational Labor Relations Board (board), and the board cross-petitioned for enforcement of its order. The school district argued that the employee evaluation plan required by the Illinois Educational Labor Relations Act (Act) was not a mandatory subject of bargaining, that the union's charge was untimely, and that the union had waived its right to midterm bargaining.


OVERVIEW: The union represented certified personnel in the school district. The collective bargaining agreement between the union and the school district contained a provision on the school district's employee evaluation plan (plan). Although the school district solicited opinions about the plan, the school district claimed the right to unilaterally change the plan. The union filed a grievance with the board. The board ordered the school district to bargain collectively on the plan. The school district appealed, and the board sought enforcement of its order. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court denied the board's cross petition. The court held that the Act did not mandate collective bargaining on all parts of the plan. The substantive criteria in the plan were not subject to mandatory bargaining, but the mechanical aspects of the evaluation process, such as timing and remediation, were. The union's charges were timely filed. The union did not waive its right to midterm bargaining by agreeing to the collective bargaining agreement. Section 16(c) of the Act was unconstitutional because it required the court to exercise original jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: In the action brought by the school district against the board, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the order of the board, and it denied the board's cross-petition for enforcement of its order.
